Ruling on Praying Maghrib Before Reaching Muzdalifah and the Fajr Prayer
States the intra-Hanafi dispute on Maghrib prayer en route and the Fajr prayer at Muzdalifah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Maghrib prayed before Muzdalifah, identify the mufta bihi position, and explain the time and obligation of Fajr prayer and standing at Muzdalifah.

Core Idea
A Maghrib prayer before Muzdalifah is invalid and must be repeated; Fajr at Muzdalifah is offered early for an obligatory standing.

This passage from Al-Lubab addresses two key Hajj issues: the validity of Maghrib if prayed en route to Muzdalifah and the prescribed practice for Fajr on the day of Nahr. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the first point, with the relied-upon position requiring repetition. The second part establishes that the Imam leads Fajr in deep darkness (ghalas) to allow for the obligatory standing (wuquf) at Muzdalifah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed act
The act in question is praying Maghrib before reaching Muzdalifah during Hajj. The dispute concerns its validity.
2
State the majority Hanafi position
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that the prayer is invalid (la tujzi'uhu) and must be repeated before Fajr.
This is the position relied upon by later authorities like al-Mahbubi and al-Nasafi.
3
State the opposing view
Abu Yusuf considers the prayer valid (yujzi'uhu) but the pilgrim has done wrong (asa'a).
His reasoning is not given here but may relate to performing the prayer in its time.
4
Apply the tarjih
The mufta bihi is the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. The pilgrim must repeat the Maghrib if he prayed it before Muzdalifah.
5
Examine the Fajr ruling
On the day of Nahr, the Imam prays Fajr in deep darkness (ghalas) to facilitate the obligatory standing at Muzdalifah, which is wajib and its time extends until sunrise.
This part is not disputed within the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومَن صلى المغرب في الطريق لم تُجزه عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد وعليه إعادتها ما لم يطلع الفجر. هداية. قال في التصحيح: واعتمد قولهما المحبوبي، والنسفي. وقال أبو يوسف: يجزئه، وقد أساء. اهـ فإذا طلع الفجر يوم النحر: صلى الإمام بالناس الفجر بغلس؛ لأجل الوقوف، ثم وقف بمزدلفة وجوباً. ووقته من طلوع الفجر إلى طلوع الشمس، ولو لحظةً، كما مرَّ في عرفة.
And whoever prays Maghrib on the road is not acceptable according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, and he must repeat it as long as Fajr has not risen. (From Hidayah). He said in al-Tashih: al-Mahbubi and al-Nasafi relied on their statement. And Abu Yusuf said: It is acceptable for him, and he has done wrong. End. Then when Fajr rises on the day of Nahr, the Imam prays with the people Fajr in deep darkness; for the sake of standing, then he stands at Muzdalifah obligatorily. And its time is from the rising of Fajr until sunrise, even a moment, as previously mentioned in Arafah.
Source pages p. 429

Commentary
Passage type: intra-Hanafi dispute. This passage addresses the ruling for a pilgrim who prays Maghrib on the way before reaching Muzdalifah. According to Imams Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani, such a prayer is not valid (la tujzi'uhu) and must be repeated as long as Fajr has not come. This is the relied-upon position as affirmed by al-Mahbubi and al-Nasafi. Abu Yusuf, however, holds that the prayer is valid (yujzi'uhu) but the person has done wrong (asa'a) because he delayed combining. The text then states the ruling for Fajr prayer: after dawn on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah, the Imam leads the Fajr prayer in deep darkness (ghalas) and then stands in supplication at Muzdalifah, which is wajib (obligatory) according to the correct view. The time for this standing is from Fajr until sunrise, even a brief moment.

Key Terms
مزدلفة (Muzdalifah): A place between Arafah and Mina where pilgrims stay on the night of the 10th.
غلس (ghalas): Deep darkness before dawn, the preferred time for Fajr at Muzdalifah.
الوقوف (al-wuquf): The standing in supplication at Muzdalifah after Fajr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, what is the ruling if a pilgrim prays Maghrib before reaching Muzdalifah?
A) It is valid but sinful
B) It is valid and rewardable
C) It is invalid and must be repeated
D) It is invalid and no need to repeat

Key Takeaway
For Maghrib before Muzdalifah, the relied-upon Hanafi position requires repetition before Fajr; the Fajr prayer at Muzdalifah is performed early followed by an obligatory standing.

Ramy at Jamrat al-Aqaba and Day of Nahr Actions
Expands rulings with proof from hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the method and rulings for stoning Jamrat al-Aqaba and the subsequent actions on the Day of Nahr, and identify the evidence from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
The Prophet's actions set the rules: stand after jamarat with subsequent ramy, not after the last; shaving or trimming is wajib, ramy is wajib.

This lesson examines the rulings for the Day of Nahr, starting with the stoning of Jamrat al-Aqaba. The commentator expands on the method, the cutting of talbiyah, the optional sacrifice, and the obligatory shaving or trimming. A hadith from Ibn Umar provides the proof for the actions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine that ramy of Jamrat al-Aqaba is wajib (obligatory) in the Hanafi school. Recognize that it is the first action of the Day of Nahr.
The proof for wajib is the continuous practice of the Prophet; Shafi'is consider it sunnah.
2
Understand the method of ramy
Learn the specifics: seven pebbles about the size of a chickpea or date pit, thrown from the bottom of the valley (batin al-wadi) with Mecca on left and Mina on right, saying takbir with each pebble. Throwing from above is valid but inferior.
The pebbles should be small to avoid harm; larger pebbles are disliked.
3
Recognize the principle for standing after ramy
Note that standing and supplicating after ramy is sunnah for jamarat that precede another ramy. Since Jamrat al-Aqaba is the last, one does not stand. The hadith of Ibn Umar proves this.
This principle distinguishes al-Aqaba from the other two jamarat.
4
Apply the sequence of subsequent actions
After ramy, cut talbiyah with the first pebble, then sacrifice (sunnah for mufrid), then shave or trim hair (wajib). Shaving is preferred. Note that the order is wajib; shaving before ramy incurs a penalty.
A quarter of the head suffices for shaving or trimming.

At Jamrat al-Aqaba, he throws it from the bottom of the valley with seven pebbles like pebbles of khadhf. He says takbir with each pebble. And he does not stand by it. At Jamrat al-Aqaba, he throws it from the bottom of the valley, making Mecca to his left and Mina to his right, with seven pebbles like pebbles of khadhf – weigh of a fils: small pebbles; it is said: the size of a chickpea; it is said: a date pit; it is said: a fingertip. And if he throws with larger or smaller, it suffices him, except that he should not throw with large ones, for fear that he may hurt someone. And if he throws from above al-Aqaba, it suffices him, because what is around it is the place of the ritual; and the best is to be from the bottom of the valley. [Hidaya]. And if it falls on the back of a man or a camel: if it falls by itself near the jamra: it is permissible; otherwise: no. And three cubits: far; less than that: near. [Jawhara]. (He says takbir with each pebble); and if he glorifies [another dhikr], it suffices him, because dhikr is achieved; and it is from the etiquettes of throwing. [Hidaya]. * (And he does not stand by it); because there is no throwing after it. (1) i.e., if it did not fall by itself, and the man upon whom it fell took it and placed it at the target: it is not permissible. See Jawhara 1/195. And he cuts off the talbiyah with the first pebble. Then he sacrifices if he wishes. Then he shaves or cuts short, and shaving is better. And the principle: that every throwing after which there is a throwing: he stands by it and supplicates; and whatever has no throwing after it: he does not stand by it. And the basis for that is the action of the Prophet, peace be upon him. (1) * (And he cuts off the talbiyah with the first pebble if he throws before shaving; and if he shaved before throwing, he cuts off the talbiyah because it does not remain with partial release). (2) (Then he sacrifices) voluntarily (if he wishes), because he is a mufrid (performing ifrad). (Then he shaves) his entire head; and a quarter suffices; or cuts short, by taking a fingertip worth; and cutting short from a quarter also suffices. (And shaving is better) than cutting short, because shaving is more complete in removing the dirt, which is the objective. (1) This is what Bukhari narrated in his Sahih (3/175, 1582) from Ibn Umar, may Allah be pleased with them both, that he used to throw the first jamra with seven pebbles, saying takbir after each pebble, then he would go forward until he was on level ground, stand facing the qibla, stand for a long time, supplicate, and raise his hands; then he would throw the middle jamra, and supplicate; then he would throw Jamrat Dhat al-Aqaba from the bottom of the valley, and not stand by it; then he would depart, saying: 'Thus I saw the Prophet, peace be upon him, do.' (2) With the reminder that blood becomes obligatory on him if he shaved before throwing, because the order is obligatory. (3) al-tafath: dirt and dishevelment, and qada' al-tafath means its removal. al-Maghrib (tafath).
Source pages p. 432

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) on the rulings of stoning Jamrat al-Aqaba and the subsequent actions of the Day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah). The commentator, al-Maydani, explains the matn of al-Quduri. The passage begins by detailing the method of stoning: one must be in the bottom of the valley (batin al-wadi), with Mecca on the left and Mina on the right, using seven small pebbles about the size of a chickpea or date pit. It is permissible to throw larger or smaller, but large stones are disliked to avoid harm. Throwing from above the jamra is also valid, but the bottom is preferred. A hadith from Bukhari is cited as the basis: Ibn Umar reported that the Prophet performed the ramy in this manner, stood and supplicated after the first two jamarat, but did not stand after Jamrat al-Aqaba. The principle is: wherever there is a subsequent ramy, one stands and makes dua; because there is no ramy after al-Aqaba, one does not stand. The commentator then turns to the next actions: The talbiyah is cut off with the first pebble of Jamrat al-Aqaba (if the pilgrim has not yet shaved; if he shaved before ramy, the talbiyah is cut anyway because one has partially exited ihram). Then, the mufrid (one performing Hajj ifrad) may voluntarily sacrifice an animal. Finally, one must shave or trim the hair of the head; shaving all the head is best, but a quarter suffices; trimming a quarter is also sufficient. The preference for shaving is because it more completely removes the dirt and dishevelment of ihram. The commentator also notes that the order is wajib: if one shaves before stoning, a dam (penalty) becomes obligatory.

Key Terms
جمرة العقبة (Jamrat al-Aqaba): The last pillar (jamra) to be stoned on the Day of Nahr, located near Mina.
حصى الخذف (hasā al-khadhf): Pebbles the size of a chickpea or date pit, used for ramy.
التلبية (al-Talbiyah): The chant (Labbayk Allahumma labbayk) recited by a pilgrim upon entering ihram.
الحلق (al-Halq): Shaving all or a quarter of the head hair to exit ihram.
التقصير (al-Taqsir): Cutting a fingertip's length from the hair.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith cited in this passage, after stoning which jamra does the pilgrim stand and supplicate?
A) Only the first jamra
B) The first and second jamrat
C) The third jamra (Jamrat al-Aqaba)
D) None of the jamarat

Key Takeaway
The Day of Nahr actions follow a specific sequence with distinct rulings: ramy is wajib, cutting talbiyah is sunnah, sacrifice is sunnah for mufrid, and shaving/trimming is wajib; each is supported by the Prophet's practice.

Post-Stoning Rituals for the Mufrid
Describes the sequence of post-stoning rituals for a mufrid pilgrim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sequence of actions for a mufrid after stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah and explain why raml is omitted in Tawaf al-Ziyarah if sa'y was done earlier.

Core Idea
For a mufrid: talbiyah stops with the first pebble, shaving brings first tahallul, and raml only if tawaf is followed by sa'y.

This passage from al-Lubab details the precise steps a mufrid pilgrim takes after stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah on the Day of Sacrifice. It clarifies when talbiyah ends, the ruling on shaving vs trimming, and the conditions for raml in Tawaf al-Ziyarah. The author bases the sequence on the Prophet's practice and Hanafi fiqh principles.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage describes the sequence after stoning. Each action has a specific hukm: cutting talbiyah is wajib, shaving/trimming is wajib, slaughter is voluntary, Tawaf al-Ziyarah has fard and wajib parts.
The ruling for the mufrid differs from qarin and mutamatti'.
2
Locate the dalil
The author refers to the action of the Prophet (peace be upon him) as the basis. The hadith from Ibn Umar (in the footnote) shows the Prophet's practice of not standing at Jamrat al-Aqabah and the sequence of actions.
The dalil is ahad (single narration), but its meaning is clear.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
From the hadith, we derive that the talbiyah is cut at the first pebble because it is the beginning of tahallul. The Prophet's action of shaving/trimming indicates its obligation. The omission of raml in Tawaf al-Ziyarah when sa'y is done earlier is derived from the principle that raml is tied to a tawaf followed by sa'y.
The author analogizes raml to ghusl with wudu: once purification is achieved, repetition is unnecessary.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) hold that raml is performed in Tawaf al-Ziyarah regardless of previous sa'y. The Hanafi school distinguishes based on the principle that raml is sunnah only in a tawaf that is immediately followed by sa'y.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; both positions have evidence.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is that raml is omitted in Tawaf al-Ziyarah if sa'y was already performed after Tawaf al-Qudum. This is supported by the analogy and the Prophet's practice. The mufta bihi is the Hanafi view as stated in the text.
The author does not dispute this point within the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويقطع التلبية مع أول حصاة. ثم يذبح إن أحب. ثم يحلق أو يقصر، والحلق أفضل. والأصل: أن كل رمي بعده رمي: يقف عنده، ويدعو، وما ليس بعده رمي: لا يقف عنده، والأصل في ذلك فعلُ النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم.
* (ويقطع التلبية مع أول حصاة إن رمى قبل الحلق، وإن حلق قبل الرمي): قطع التلبية؛ لأنها لا تثبت مع التحلل.
(ثم يذبح) تطوعاً (إن أحب)؛ لأنه مُفرِدٌ.

وقد حلَّ له كلُّ شيءٍ إلا النساء.
ثم يأتي مكة من يومه ذلك، أو من الغد، أو من بعد الغد، فيطوف بالبيت طواف الزيارة سبعة أشواط.

(وقد حل له): أي بعد الحلق أو التقصير (كل شيء) من محظورات الإحرام إلا النساء: أي جماعهن ودواعيه.

(فإن كان سعى بين الصفا والمروة) سابقاً (عقيب طواف القدوم: لم يَرْمُل في هذا الطواف)؛ لأن الرمل في طواف بعده سعي،
And he cuts the talbiyah with the first pebble. Then he slaughters if he wishes. Then he shaves or trims, and shaving is better. The principle: every stoning after which there is another stoning: he stands at it and supplicates, and what is not followed by a stoning: he does not stand at it, and the basis for that is the action of the Prophet (peace be upon him). * (And he cuts the talbiyah with the first pebble if he throws before shaving, and if he shaves before throwing): he cuts the talbiyah; because it does not remain with partial dissolution. (Then he slaughters) voluntarily (if he wishes); because he is a mufrid. (Then he shaves) all his head, and a quarter suffices, or trims, by taking from it the length of a fingertip, and trimming from a quarter also suffices, (and shaving is better) than trimming; because shaving is more complete in removing filth, which is the goal. And everything becomes lawful for him except women. Then he comes to Mecca on that same day, or the next day, or the day after, and performs tawaf of the House, the Tawaf al-Ziyarah, seven circuits. If he had performed sa'y between Safa and Marwah immediately after the Tawaf al-Qudum: he does not do raml in this tawaf; because raml is in a tawaf after which there is sa'y, so it resembles washing with wudu. (And everything becomes lawful for him): i.e., after shaving or trimming (everything) of the prohibitions of ihram except women: i.e., intercourse and its preliminaries. (Then he comes to Mecca on that same day: i.e., the first day of sacrifice, or the next day, or the day after, and the best is the first of them, (and performs tawaf of the House, Tawaf al-Ziyarah, also called Tawaf al-Ifadah and Tawaf al-Fard, (seven circuits) obligatorily, and the obligatory part is four. (If he had performed sa'y between Safa and Marwah) previously (immediately after Tawaf al-Qudum: he does not do raml in this tawaf); because raml is in a tawaf after which there is sa'y.
Source pages p. 433

Commentary
This passage from al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Quduri presents the sequence of actions for a mufrid (one performing only Hajj, not Umrah) immediately after stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah on the Day of Sacrifice. The author begins by stating that the talbiyah is cut with the first pebble thrown, even if one shaves before throwing (in which case it is also cut because talbiyah does not remain after the first act of tahallul). Then, optionally, the pilgrim may slaughter a sacrificial animal as a voluntary act, since the mufrid is not obliged to sacrifice. Next comes shaving the entire head—or at least a quarter—or trimming, defined as cutting the length of a fingertip from the hair; again, a quarter suffices. Shaving is explicitly deemed superior to trimming because it more thoroughly removes the filth (tafath) of ihram, which is the objective. Upon shaving or trimming, all prohibitions of ihram are lifted except relations with women and their preliminaries. Then the pilgrim proceeds to Mecca for Tawaf al-Ziyarah (also called Tawaf al-Ifadah or Tawaf al-Fard), performing seven circuits, of which four are obligatory (fard) and the remaining three are wajib (obligatory but not integral). The best time is the first day of sacrifice. Finally, a condition: if the pilgrim had already performed the sa'y between Safa and Marwah immediately after Tawaf al-Qudum upon first entering Mecca, then in Tawaf al-Ziyarah he does not do raml (brisk walking with shoulder movement), because raml is prescribed only in a tawaf that is followed by sa'y; since sa'y has already been done, raml is omitted. The author analogizes this to performing ghusl (ritual bath) along with wudu—once purification is achieved, repeating it is unnecessary. The passage is a clear exposition of the Hanafi rulings for the mufrid after stoning, based on the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) as recorded in the hadith cited in the footnote.

Key Terms
مفرد (mufrid): A pilgrim performing only Hajj without combining it with Umrah in the same ihram.
التحلل (tahallul): The state of becoming free from ihram prohibitions, achieved partially by shaving/trimming and fully after Tawaf al-Ziyarah.
الرمل (raml): Brisk walking with small steps and movement of shoulders, performed in the first three circuits of tawaf when followed by sa'y.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does a mufrid cut the talbiyah?
A) When he begins shaving
B) With the first pebble thrown at Jamrat al-Aqabah
C) After completing all stoning
D) At the moment of sacrificing an animal

Key Takeaway
The mufrid's post-stoning sequence: cut talbiyah at first pebble, shave/trim (wajib), then Tawaf al-Ziyarah (fard 4 circuits), with raml omitted if sa'y was done earlier.

Rulings of Tawaf al-Ziyarah (Ifadhah)
Explains timing, raml, and obligation of Tawaf al-Ziyarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of Tawaf al-Ziyarah, identify when raml is performed, and explain the Hanafi proof from Quran and qiyas.

Core Idea
Tawaf al-Ziyarah is fard; raml depends on whether sa'i has already been performed.

This lesson examines the rulings of Tawaf al-Ziyarah (Ifadhah), the obligatory circumambulation of Hajj. The passage from al-Lubab covers timing, the number of circuits, and the crucial distinction regarding raml based on prior sa'i. By understanding the Hanafi classification of fard and wajib within the seven circuits and the role of raml, you will be able to correctly apply these rules.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its overall ruling
Tawaf al-Ziyarah is the obligatory circumambulation, a pillar (rukn) of Hajj, performed on the Day of Nahr or the following two days.
2
Understand the Hanafi breakdown of circuits
Seven circuits are performed: four are strictly fard (rukn), three are wajib. Performance of all seven is wajib.
The fard circuits are the minimum; missing one invalidates the tawaf.
3
Determine the raml ruling based on prior sa'i
If the pilgrim performed sa'i immediately after Tawaf al-Qudum, he does NOT perform raml in Tawaf al-Ziyarah. If sa'i was not done, he performs raml as sunnah and then does sa'i after the tawaf.
Raml is quick walking with short steps in the first three circuits, performed by men only.
4
Trace the proof from Quran and qiyas
The Quranic verse (Surah al-Hajj 22:29) commands circumambulation, establishing the obligation. The analogy with ghusl after wudu shows that the purpose of raml (showing strength) is already fulfilled if sa'i has been done.
The jussive 'ليطوفوا' indicates obligation in Hanafi usul.
5
Note the time frame and ruling on delay
It is makruh tahrimi to delay Tawaf al-Ziyarah beyond the three days (10th–12th Dhul Hijjah). The text begins to discuss consequences of delay, completed elsewhere.

Then he comes to Makkah on that same day, or the next day, or the day after, and performs seven circuits around the House as the Visit Tawaf. If he made the Sa'i between Safa and Marwah immediately after the Arrival Tawaf, he does not walk quickly (raml) in this tawaf, and it resembles ghusl with wudu. (And it becomes permissible for him): meaning after shaving or trimming (everything) that was prohibited during ihram except women: meaning intercourse and its preliminaries. The departure from Mina to Makkah for Tawaf al-Ifadhah: (Then he comes to Makkah on that same day): meaning the first day of Nahr, (or the next day, or the day after, and the best of them is the first). (He performs seven circuits of the Tawaf of Visit, also called Tawaf al-Ifadhah and the Obligatory Tawaf) as wajib, and the fard of them is four. (If he had made Sa'i) previously (immediately after the Arrival Tawaf: he does not walk quickly in this tawaf) because raml in a tawaf after Sa'i is not required, and no Sa'i is upon him. If he had not previously done Sa'i, he walks quickly in this tawaf, and performs Sa'i afterwards as we have mentioned, and women become permissible for him as well. (If he had not previously done Sa'i) after the Arrival Tawaf: (he walks quickly in this tawaf) as recommended, and performs Sa'i afterwards as obligatory, as we have mentioned, and women become permissible for him as well, but by the previous shaving; for it is the legal reason for permissibility, not the tawaf, except that its effect is delayed regarding women. (Hidayah). And this tawaf is the obligatory one in Hajj, and it is a pillar (rukn) of it, as it is commanded in His saying: "And let them circumambulate the Ancient House." (It is disliked) as tahrimi (to delay it beyond these days) the three days, (if he delays...)
Source pages p. 434

Commentary
This passage from al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Quduri discusses the rulings of Tawaf al-Ziyarah (also called Tawaf al-Ifadhah). The author begins by stating the timing: the pilgrim comes to Makkah on the Day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah) or the following two days. The tawaf consists of seven circuits (ashwat), of which four are fard and the remaining three are wajib; performance is wajib. The commentary then addresses the rule of raml (quick walking with short steps) in this tawaf: if the pilgrim has already performed sa'i between Safa and Marwah immediately after Tawaf al-Qudum (the arrival tawaf), then he does NOT perform raml in Tawaf al-Ziyarah. The reason given in the text is that raml in a tawaf that occurs after sa'i is not required, and this is compared to the analogy of performing ghusl after already having made wudu—where the purpose has been fulfilled. If, however, the pilgrim had not performed sa'i prior, then he should perform raml in this tawaf (as a sunnah) and then perform sa'i afterwards (as a wajib). The commentary also clarifies that women become permissible upon completion of the tawaf, but note: the actual permissibility of marital relations is achieved by the shaving (halq) on the Day of Nahr, not by the tawaf itself; the tawaf merely activates that permissibility. The author then emphasizes that this tawaf is the obligatory (fard) circumambulation of Hajj, citing the Quranic verse 'Walyattawwafu bil-baytil-'atiq' (Surah al-Hajj 22:29) as proof. Finally, it states that it is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked) to delay this tawaf beyond the three days (10th, 11th, 12th of Dhul Hijjah). The passage ends with the beginning of a clause on what happens if one does delay, but the full ruling on delay is completed elsewhere.

Key Terms
طواف الزيارة (tawaf al-ziyarah): The circumambulation performed on the Day of Nahr or the following days, also known as Tawaf al-Ifadhah, which is the obligatory (fard) tawaf of Hajj.
رَمَل (raml): Quick walking with short steps and shoulder movement during the first three circuits of a tawaf, performed by men only.
مُحَلِّقِين (muhalliqin): Those who shave their heads (in contrast to those who trim) after completing the rituals of Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 7
B) 4
C) 3
D) 1

Key Takeaway
Tawaf al-Ziyarah is the fard circumambulation of Hajj; four circuits are rukn, and raml is omitted if sa'i has already been performed.

Raml and Sa'i in Tawaf al-Ifadah; This Tawaf is Obligatory
Ruling on raml and sa'i in Tawaf al-Ifadah and proof of its obligation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings on raml and sa'i in Tawaf al-Ifadah and identify the Quranic evidence for its obligation.

Core Idea
Tawaf al-Ifadah is the obligatory circumambulation of Hajj; raml is sunnah and sa'i is wajib if not done earlier.

In this passage from al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Quduri, we learn about Tawaf al-Ifadah—the essential circumambulation of Hajj. The text clarifies the circumstances in which raml (quick walking) and sa'i (the running between Safa and Marwa) are performed during this tawaf, and it affirms the obligation of this tawaf with a clear Quranic proof. Understanding these details is crucial for performing Hajj correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what Tawaf al-Ifadah is and its legal classification (fard/rukn).
The text states it is the obligatory tawaf (المفروض) and a pillar (ركن) of Hajj.
2
Analyze the condition for sa'i
Note when sa'i is required after this tawaf: only if it was not performed after Tawaf al-Qudum.
If sa'i was done earlier, there is no sa'i after Tawaf al-Ifadah because repetition is not legislated.
3
Determine the rulings for raml and sa'i
When sa'i is needed, raml is sunnah (استناناً) and sa'i itself is wajib (وجوباً).
Raml is only for men in the first three circuits; sa'i is wajib, not fard.
4
Understand the effect on women's permissibility
Women become permissible (حل النساء) through shaving hair, but tawaf is a condition for that permissibility to take effect.
Shaving is the ultimate halal, but tawaf delays its effect in the sense that it must be done before shaving for the sequence.
5
Trace the evidence (dalil)
The proof for the obligation of Tawaf al-Ifadah is Quran 22:29, and the imperative form indicates obligation in Hanafi usul.
The verse 'وَلْيَطَوَفُوا بِالْبَيْتِ الْعَتِيقِ' is cited; the amr (command) yields wujub.

Commentary
This passage from al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Quduri deals with the Tawaf al-Ifadah, which is the obligatory circumambulation of Hajj. The text explains that if a pilgrim did not perform sa'i (the running between Safa and Marwa) after the Tawaf al-Qudum (arrival tawaf), then during this Tawaf al-Ifadah, he should perform raml (quick walking with short steps) as a sunnah, and then do sa'i as wajib. Key Terms
رمل (raml): Quick walking with short steps, performed by men in the first three circuits of tawaf.
سعي (sa'i): The ritual walking between the hills of Safa and Marwa.
طواف الإفاضة (tawaf al-ifadah): The obligatory circumambulation of the Kaaba performed after returning from Mina, also called tawaf al-ziyarah.

Ruling on Delaying Tawaf al-Ifadah Beyond Three Days
Intra-Hanafi dispute on whether delaying Tawaf al-Ifadah requires a sacrifice (dam)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on delaying Tawaf al-Ifadah and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Delaying Tawaf al-Ifadah beyond the three days of sacrifice requires a dam according to Abu Hanifa, the relied-upon view.

Tawaf al-Ifadah is an essential rite of Hajj. Its timing is tied to the days of sacrifice. The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement: Abu Hanifa held that delaying it beyond those days triggers a penalty, while his two students disagreed. This lesson unpacks the dispute and identifies the operative ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the disputed ruling
What is the act? Tawaf al-Ifadah. What is the dispute? Whether delaying it beyond ayyam al-nahr (three days of sacrifice) requires a dam (sacrificial animal).
The act itself is wajib; the dispute is about the consequence of delay.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and basis
Abu Hanifa: a dam is required if delayed. The basis is that the obligation is time-bound to these days; delay implies a violation.
Implicit dalil: the command for tawaf is linked to the days of nahr.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and basis
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani: no dam is required. Their basis: there is no specific end time defined for the obligation, so delay does not constitute a violation.
They view the obligation as open-ended within Hajj.
4
Analyze the tarjih (preference)
Later authorities like al-Nasafi and al-Mahbubi in al-Tashih preferred Abu Hanifa's view. The mufta bihi is that a dam is required.
This is an example of tarjih based on strength of dalil and scholarly consensus of later Hanafis.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
According to the relied-upon view, a pilgrim who delays must offer a dam. According to the Sahibayn, no penalty exists.
The difference affects whether the pilgrim has an additional obligation (dam).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ویکره تحريماً ( تأخيره عن هذه الأيام) الثلاثة، (فإن أخره عنها (١) : لزمه دم عند أبي حنيفة(٢)). قال في التصحيح »: وهو المعوّل عليه عند النسفي، والمحبوبي.

(1) أي أيام النحر الثلاثة، هذا هو الصحيح عن الإمام أبي حنيفة، خلافاً لـمـا ذكره القدوري في شرح مختصر الكرخي من أن آخره آخر أيام التشريق، وتبعـه الكرماني (في المسالك (٤٢٧/١)، وصاحب المنافع، والمستصفى. ابن عابدين ١٣٥/٧ ، نقلاً عن مناسك علي القاري ص .١٥٥

(۲) وقالا : ليس عليه شيء، إذ ليس لآخره زمان معين موقـت . ينظر الاختيار ١٥٤/١ ، المسالك ٤٢٧/١ ، بدائع الصنائع ١٣٢/٢.
And it is makruh tahrimi to delay it beyond these three days, and if he delays it beyond them, a dam (sacrificial animal) is obligatory upon him according to Abu Hanifa. It is said in al-Tashih: and this is the relied-upon view according to al-Nasafi and al-Mahbubi. (1) Meaning the three days of sacrifice, this is the correct view from Imam Abu Hanifa, contrary to what al-Quduri mentioned in Sharh Mukhtasar al-Karkhi that its last time is the last day of al-Tashreeq, and al-Karmani followed him (in al-Masalik 1/427), and the author of al-Manafi' and al-Mustasfa. Ibn Abidin 7/135, quoting from Manasik Ali al-Qari p.155. (2) And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: nothing is upon him, for there is no specific time defined for its end. See al-Ikhtiyar 1/154, al-Masalik 1/427, Bada'i' al-Sana'i' 2/132.
Source pages p. 435

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on delaying the Tawaf al-Ifadah beyond the three days of sacrifice (11th, 12th, 13th of Dhul-Hijjah). The matn states that it is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked) to delay, and if one does so, a dam (sacrifice) is required according to Imam Abu Hanifa. The commentary from al-Tashih clarifies that this is the relied-upon view among later authorities like al-Nasafi and al-Mahbubi. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa held that the time for tawaf is limited to these days by obligation (wujub), while his two students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, held that there is no specific end time for the obligation, and thus no penalty for delay. The relied-upon view for fatwa, however, is Abu Hanifa's position. The footnotes provide additional references and sources, noting that al-Quduri in another work mentioned a different opinion, but the correct and operative view is that of Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal (sheep or goat) required as a penalty for certain omissions in Hajj.
أيام النحر (ayyam al-nahr): The three days of sacrifice: 10th, 11th, 12th of Dhul-Hijjah (the day of Eid and two days after).

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) The pilgrim must repeat the Hajj.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the mufta bihi is that delaying Tawaf al-Ifadah beyond the three days of sacrifice requires a dam.

Sunnah Order of Ramy on the Second Day of Tashreeq
Sunnah procedure for ramy on the second day of Tashreeq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the sunnah procedure for stoning the jamarat on the second day of Tashreeq and identify the correct starting point.

Core Idea
Begin stoning with the jamrah nearest Masjid al-Khayf, then the middle, then the large.

After spending the night in Mina, the pilgrim must stone the three jamarat on the second day of Tashreeq (11th Dhul-Hijjah). The sunnah specifies an order: start with the small jamrah near Masjid al-Khayf, then the middle, then the large. This order is based on the Prophet's practice and is considered a confirmed sunnah (sunnah muakkadah).

Guided Path
1
Identify the timing
The ramy for the second day of Tashreeq is performed after the sun passes its zenith (zawal).
2
Determine the starting point
The sunnah is to begin with the jamrah nearest Masjid al-Khayf (the small jamrah).
This is the established order from the Prophet's action.
3
Complete the sequence
After stoning the small jamrah, stone the middle jamrah, then the large jamrah.
Each jamrah requires 7 pebbles.
4
Ruling level
The specific order is sunnah muakkadah. Ramy itself is wajib; omitting the order does not invalidate the ramy but is makruh.
Omission of the ramy altogether requires dam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(۳) تقدم تخريج هذه السنة، وأنها فِعْلُ النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قبل قليل عند أول الكلام على الرمي.

Commentary
This passage outlines the sunnah procedure for the ramy (stoning) on the second day of Tashreeq (the 11th of Dhul-Hijjah, counting from the day of sacrifice). According to the Hanafi school, after returning to Mina and waiting until the sun passes its zenith (zawal), the pilgrim stones the three pillars (jamarat) in order: first the one closest to Masjid al-Khayf (the Small Jamrah), then the Middle Jamrah, and finally the Large Jamrah. The commentary emphasizes that beginning with the nearest to the mosque is a sunnah (established practice) from the Prophet's own action, as referenced in earlier sections. This ruling is part of the obligatory acts of Hajj (wajibat) but not a pillar; omission would require a dam.

Key Terms
رمي (ramy): The act of throwing pebbles at the jamarat pillars during Hajj.
جمرات (jamarat): The three stone pillars (small, middle, large) located in Mina that symbolize the devil.
مسجد الخيف (masjid al-khayf): The mosque in Mina where the Prophet (saws) is reported to have prayed; the small jamrah is located near it.
السنة (al-sunnah): In this context, a recommended practice (sunnah muakkadah) based on the Prophet's action.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Immediately after Fajr
B) After the sun passes its zenith (zawal)
C) Anytime before sunset
D) Only after stoning the large jamrah

Key Takeaway
The sunnah order for ramy on the second day of Tashreeq is to begin with the small jamrah nearest Masjid al-Khayf, then the middle, then the large.

Time Limit for Tawaf al-Ifadah and the Obligation of Dam
Intra-Hanafi dispute on dam for delayed Tawaf al-Ifadah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the relied-upon Hanafi ruling on delaying Tawaf al-Ifadah and explain the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Delaying Tawaf al-Ifadah beyond the days of Nahr requires a dam according to Abu Hanifa, but not according to the Sahibayn.

This passage from al-Lubab presents an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether a pilgrim must offer a sacrificial animal (dam) if he performs Tawaf al-Ifadah after the days of Nahr. Although all Hanafi imams agree that Tawaf al-Ifadah can be performed at any time after standing at Arafah, they differ on whether its time is fixed by obligation to the days of Nahr. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to distinguish between the Imam and his disciples within the school and to identify the operative ruling for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the disputed ruling
Recognize that the act in question is Tawaf al-Ifadah, a rukn of Hajj. The dispute is about whether delaying it beyond the days of Nahr requires a dam (sacrificial animal).
The days of Nahr are the 10th, 11th, and 12th of Dhul Hijjah.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
According to Abu Hanifa, if the pilgrim delays Tawaf al-Ifadah beyond the days of Nahr, a dam is wajib. His reasoning is that the time for Tawaf al-Ifadah is fixed to the days of Nahr by obligation (wujub) — even though it remains valid afterward, the delay necessitates compensation.
The dam is an additional obligation, not a nullification of the Tawaf.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that no dam is required. They argue that there is no specific fixed end time for Tawaf al-Ifadah; all days and nights are its time by obligation, so delaying it does not trigger any compensation.
The Sahibayn agree that it is best to perform it during the days of Nahr, but it is not obligatory to do so.
4
Recognize the common ground and the point of disagreement
All three imams agree that Tawaf al-Ifadah is valid at any time after Arafah. The disagreement is whether there is an obligatory time frame (the days of Nahr) that, if missed, requires a dam. Abu Hanifa says yes; the Sahibayn say no.
This is a dispute about the nature of the time — whether it is time-bound by obligation or not.
5
Identify the mufta bihi (relied-upon ruling)
The relied-upon view in the madhhab is Abu Hanifa's, as affirmed by al-Nasafi, al-Mahbubi, and al-Maydani in al-Lubab. Therefore, in fatwa, a pilgrim who delays Tawaf al-Ifadah beyond the days of Nahr must offer a dam.
This tarjih is based on the principle that the Imam's view is given preference when there is no clear evidence to the contrary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عنها : لزمه دم عند أبي حنيفة .
قال في التصحيح »: وهو المعوّل عليه عند النسفي، والمحبوبي.
وليس لآخر وقت طواف الإفاضة زمان معين موقت به فرضاً، بل جميع الأيام والليالي وقته فرضاً بلا خلاف بين أئمة المذهب، لكنه موقت بأيام النحر وجوباً في قول أبي حنيفة. وقالا : ليس عليه شيء، إذ ليس لآخره زمان معين موقت.
(Regarding it: a dam is incumbent upon him according to Abu Hanifa.) He said in al-Tashih: It is the relied-upon view according to al-Nasafi and al-Mahbubi. There is no specific time fixed as an obligation for the last time of Tawaf al-Ifadah; rather, all days and nights are its time by obligation without disagreement among the imams of the madhhab, but it is time-bound to the days of Nahr by obligation in the view of Abu Hanifa. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: Nothing is upon him, because there is no specific time fixed for its end.
Source pages p. 436

Commentary
This passage addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the time limit for Tawaf al-Ifadah. The matn states that according to Abu Hanifa, if one delays Tawaf al-Ifadah beyond the days of Nahr (the 10th, 11th, 12th of Dhul Hijjah), a dam (sacrificial animal) is required. The commentator al-Maydani clarifies that the relied-upon position in the madhhab, as affirmed by al-Nasafi and al-Mahbubi, is Abu Hanifa's view. However, the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that no dam is required because there is no fixed time limit for the end of Tawaf al-Ifadah; it can be performed at any time, although it is best to do it during the days of Nahr. The commentator notes that all imams agree that the time in general is all days and nights, but the obligation of a specific time (the days of Nahr) is only in Abu Hanifa's view. The practical consequence is that a pilgrim who delays Tawaf al-Ifadah beyond the 13th of Dhul Hijjah must offer a dam according to Abu Hanifa, but not according to the Sahibayn. The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's position.

Key Terms
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal (goat or sheep) required as compensation for a ritual obligation.
طواف الإفاضة (tawaf al-ifadah): The obligatory circumambulation of the Kaaba performed after standing at Arafah on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah.
أيام النحر (ayyam al-nahr): The 10th, 11th, and 12th of Dhul Hijjah, the days of sacrifice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Offer a dam (sacrificial animal).
C) Repeat the Hajj.
D) Give charity (sadaqah).

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the relied-upon view is that delaying Tawaf al-Ifadah beyond the days of Nahr requires a dam, even though the Sahibayn disagreed.

Stoning the Jamarat on the 11th and 12th of Dhul Hijjah
Detailed description of stoning procedure on the 11th and 12th

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi procedure for stoning the three jamarat on the second and third days of Tashreeq, including the required order, number of pebbles, timing, and sunnah acts.

Core Idea
Stoning the jamarat is wajib; on tashreeq days it must be after zawal, starting from the nearest jamrah to Masjid al-Khayf.

This passage details the ritual of stoning (ramy) during the days of Tashreeq. After completing the activities of the 10th of Dhul Hijjah, the pilgrim returns to Mina to stone the three stone pillars. The procedure differs slightly for the second and third days, and there are specific sunnah acts to observe. Understanding this sequence and its conditions ensures the validity of this wajib act.

Guided Path
1
Identify the days and required timing
The second day is the 11th of Dhul Hijjah, the third day is the 12th. Stoning must be performed after the sun passes its zenith (zawal). Note that the 10th day has a different procedure.
Zawal marks the beginning of Dhuhr prayer time.
2
Determine the order of stoning
On both days, the pilgrim must stone the three jamarat in a specific order: begin with the jamrah nearest to Masjid al-Khayf (al-Ula), then the middle (al-Wusta), then Jamrat al-Aqaba (the largest). This order is sunnah.
The jamarat are located in Mina near Masjid al-Khayf.
3
Count the pebbles and mention the takbir
Each jamrah is stoned with seven pebbles. With each throw, the pilgrim says 'Allahu Akbar' (takbir). This is a confirmed sunnah.
Pebbles should be small, about the size of a chickpea.
4
Observe the standing and supplication for each jamrah
After stoning the first two jamarat (al-Ula and al-Wusta), the pilgrim stands facing the Qibla, raises his hands, and makes supplication (dua). For Jamrat al-Aqaba, he does not stand or supplicate because there is no stoning after it. This is a sunnah distinction.
The third day's procedure is identical to the second day.
5
Note the option of early departure
The pilgrim may choose to leave Mina after stoning on the 12th (second day) if he wishes. If he stays until the 13th, he must stone again. The relied-upon time for stoning is after zawal, though a weak narration allows stoning after Fajr for those leaving early.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; the mufta bihi is after zawal.

Source Text

Stoning of the second day: Then he returns to Mina on that day and stays there for the sake of stoning. When the sun has passed its zenith on the second day of the days of Nahr, he stones the three jamarat. And the sunnah is that he begins with the one nearest the mosque (Masjid al-Khayf), and stones it with seven pebbles, saying takbir with each pebble, and stands there and makes supplication. Then he stones the next one similarly and stands there. Then he stones Jamrat al-Aqaba similarly but does not stand there. Commentary
This passage details the ritual of stoning the jamarat during the Hajj. It begins by stating that after finishing the activities of the 10th (sacrifice, shaving, etc.), the pilgrim returns to Mina for the days of tashreeq. On the second day (11th of Dhul Hijjah), after noon (zawal), he stones the three jamarat. The sunnah is to start with the jamrah nearest to Masjid al-Khayf (al-Jamrah al-Ula), throw seven pebbles one by one, saying 'Allahu Akbar' with each throw, then step forward and make supplication facing the Qibla. Then he does the same for the middle jamrah (al-Wusta), also standing and supplicating. Then for the largest jamrah (Jamrat al-Aqaba), he throws seven pebbles similarly but does not stand or supplicate because there is no stoning after it. On the third day (12th of Dhul Hijjah), after noon, he repeats the same procedure for all three jamarat. The commentator notes that if the pilgrim wishes to leave early (after two days), he may depart on the 12th after stoning, but if he stays until the 13th, he stones again. The times for stoning are after noon on each day, though there is a narration from Abu Hanifa allowing stoning on the third day after Fajr for those who want to leave early, but the relied-upon view is after zawal.

Key Terms
رمي (ramy): The act of throwing pebbles at the stone pillars (jamarat) during Hajj.
جمرة العقبة (jamrat al-aqaba): The largest of the three stone pillars, located near the road to Mina.
زوال الشمس (zawal al-shams): The time when the sun passes its zenith, marking the beginning of Dhuhr prayer.

Key Takeaway

Sunnah Actions in Stoning the Jamarat
Description of sunnah actions during stoning the jamarat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the sunnah actions of stoning the jamarat on the Day of Nahr and the following day, and explain the exception at Jamrat al-Aqabah.

Core Idea
Stoning includes takbir, standing, and supplication, but not at Jamrat al-Aqabah because no stoning follows.

In this passage from al-Quduri, we learn the recommended (sunnah) way to stone the jamarat. The Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) performed these actions, and we are encouraged to follow them. The text details the timing, the number of pebbles, and the gestures of takbir, standing, and supplication. Importantly, it highlights that at Jamrat al-Aqabah on the Day of Nahr, one does not stand and supplicate, unlike the other jamarat. This lesson will clarify these sunnah acts and their rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the days and jamarat
On the Day of Nahr (10th), only Jamrat al-Aqabah is stoned. On the 11th, all three jamarat are stoned after noon.
The text specifies 'after the sun's decline' for the 11th.
2
Recall the general sunnah at each jamrah
With each of the seven pebbles, say takbir. Then stand facing the jamrah and make supplication.
This is the default pattern for all jamarat.
3
Note the exception at Jamrat al-Aqabah
After stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah on the 10th, do not stand or supplicate. The same applies on the 11th for the last jamrah.
The text explicitly states 'does not stand at it'.
4
Understand the reason
The standing and supplication are done because there will be another stoning afterwards. At Jamrat al-Aqabah, it is the final stoning of that day, so no need to wait.
The commentary says: 'because there is no stoning after it'.
5
Confirm the ruling level
These actions are sunnah muakkadah, not wajib. Omitting them does not invalidate the stoning.
The Hanafi school classifies these as confirmed sunnah.

Concession for Stoning Before Noon on the 13th of Dhul Hijjah
Ruling on stoning before noon on the 13th for those hastening.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Abu Hanifa permitted stoning on the 13th before noon for those hastening, and identify the istihsan basis and its adoption by later Hanafi authorities.

Core Idea
Stoning before noon on the 13th is permissible when hastening, by way of istihsan.

The days of Tashreeq have specific timings for stoning. On the third day (12th) and fourth day (13th), stoning is normally after noon. However, a narration from Abu Hanifa provides a concession for those who wish to hasten their departure from Mina: they may stone on the 13th before noon, after Fajr. This ruling, based on istihsan, was later adopted by many Hanafi authorities as the correct view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? It is stoning the three jamarat on the fourth day (13th Dhul Hijjah) before noon for one who intends to hasten (ta'ajjul). The ruling according to Abu Hanifa is jawaz (permissible).
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a narration from Abu Hanifa himself: 'It is permissible to stone on this day after dawn for one who wants to hasten the nafar.' This is a riwaya from Abu Hanifa, not from the Qur'an or Sunnah directly, but it is considered a valid proof within the school.
The narration is zanni al-thubut and zanni al-dalala.
3
Understand the istihsan basis
The general rule (qiyas) requires stoning after noon on all days of Tashreeq. However, istihsan (juristic preference) overrides this for the sake of ease and facilitation for those hastening. This is a clear example of istihsan in action.
Istihsan is a secondary source in Hanafi usul.
4
Trace the tarjih (preponderance)
The matn (al-Quduri) presents the general rule. Al-Hidayah mentions this narration as istihsan, and later authorities like Burhan al-Shari'ah, al-Nasafi, and Sadr al-Shari'ah chose it as the correct view. Thus, the mufta bihi (operative ruling) is Abu Hanifa's concession.
This shows how later scholarship can strengthen a weak riwaya.

This passage covers the stoning on the third day (12th Dhul Hijjah) and the fourth day (13th). On the 12th, the stoning of all three jamarat occurs after noon. The pilgrim has the option to hasten (nafar) on the 12th, leaving for Mecca before the 13th, or to stay. If he stays, he stones again on the 13th after noon. Abu Hanifa, based on a narration, allows stoning on the 13th before noon (after Fajr) for those who intend to hasten, and this was adopted by later scholars as istihsan. The preferred view is to stay until the 13th.

Key Terms
النفر (al-nafar): Departing from Mina to Mecca after completing stoning
التعجل (al-ta'ajjul): Hastening the departure by stoning on the 12th and leaving before sunset
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference used to override strict analogy

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, when is it permissible to stone the jamarat on the fourth day (13th Dhul Hijjah) for one who wants to hasten?
A) Only after noon
B) Before noon after Fajr
C) Only after sunset
D) Only at night

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa's concession for stoning before noon on the 13th for those hastening is established as the relied-upon view in the later Hanafi tradition.

The Dislike of Sending Baggage Ahead Before Departure
Ruling that sending baggage ahead is disliked and interpretation of Umar's statement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on sending baggage ahead before nafar and explain why it is makruh tanzih according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Sending baggage before nafar is makruh tanzih, not invalidating hajj.

During Hajj, pilgrims often consider practical arrangements like sending luggage ahead. This lesson examines a specific ruling about sending baggage (thaqal) before the nafar (departure from Mina). We will see that while the act is discouraged, it does not nullify the Hajj according to the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is sending one's baggage and servants ahead from Mina before the nafar. According to the text, it is disliked (makruh). Determine the precise level of dislike.
The text says 'yukrahu' which in Hanafi fiqh can be either tanzih or tahrimi.
2
Locate the dalil
The evidence cited is a narration from Umar (mawquf) recorded by Ibn Abi Shaybah: 'Whoever sends his baggage before the nafar: there is no hajj for him.' Identify the type of dalil and its chain.
This is a mawquf hadith, so it is classified as a saying of a Companion, not a marfu' (prophetic) hadith.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The literal wording 'la hajj lahu' suggests nullification of Hajj. But the Hanafi scholars interpret this as a severe warning meaning the Hajj is incomplete, not invalid. Determine how the wording is understood.
The phrase is considered zanni al-dalala, open to interpretation.
4
Note the Hanafi interpretation
Ibn Abidin clarifies that the intended meaning is 'no complete hajj' and that the ruling is makruh tanzih (lightly disliked). Understand the role of later scholars in resolving apparent conflicts.
This interpretation comes from al-Bahr al-Raiq and is adopted by later authorities.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position for fatwa is that sending baggage ahead is makruh tanzih, not haram or invalidating. Summarize the practical implication.
The act is permissible but better avoided; the Hajj remains valid.

Source Text

Abu Hanifa's Exception for Throwing Jamarat Before Zawal on the 13th
Intra-Hanafi dispute on throwing jamarat before zawal on the 13th

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Abu Hanifa's ruling on throwing jamarat before zawal on the 13th of Dhul Hijjah and explain the istihsan basis that distinguishes it from the general rule.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa permits throwing before zawal on the 13th — a concession (rukhsa) based on istihsan.

This passage from Lubab al-Quduri presents the standard Hanafi ruling that throwing jamarat must occur after zawal on all days of Tashreeq, but then introduces an important exception: Abu Hanifa allows throwing before zawal on the 13th (the fourth day) if done after dawn. This exception is justified by istihsan (juristic preference) and later adopted by many authoritative Hanafi scholars. Understanding this intra-madhhab difference is crucial for a mufti when issuing fatwas during Hajj.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two options for departure
Determine what the pilgrim may do on the 12th: either perform early departure (nafr awwal) or stay for the 13th. This sets the context for the ruling.
Early departure is before dawn of the 14th.
2
State the general Hanafi ruling for the 13th
If staying, one must throw the three jamarat after zawal (sun's decline), as practiced on the previous days.
The matn states this as the default.
3
Recognize Abu Hanifa's exception
Abu Hanifa allows throwing before zawal but after dawn on the 13th. Note that this exception applies only to the 13th, not to the 11th or 12th.
The exception is a rukhsa (concession).
4
Analyze the proof for the exception
The exception is based on istihsan (juristic preference). The time for throwing is from dawn to sunset, so before zawal is included. Also, hardship of hastening departure is considered.
Istihsan overrides qiyas (analogy with other days).
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
Later scholars like Burhan al-Shari'ah, al-Nasafi, and Sadr al-Shari'ah adopted Abu Hanifa's view as the soundest. This is the operative ruling for fatwa today.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإذا أراد أن يتعجَّلَ النَّفْرَ : نَفَر إلى مكة . وإن أراد أن يقيم : رمى الجمارَ الثلاث في اليوم الرابع بعد زوال الشمس . فإن قدم الرمي في هذا اليوم قبل الزوال بعد طلوع الفجر : جاز عند أبي حنيفة . (فإذا أراد أن يتعجَّل النَّفْرَ في اليوم الثالث: (نَفَر إلى مكة) قبل طلوع فجر الرابع، لا بعده؛ لدخول وقت الرمي. (وإن أراد أن يقيم إلى الرابع، وهو الأفضل: رمي الجمار الثلاث في اليوم الرابع بعد زوال الشمس أيضاً، فإن قدَّم الرمي في هذا اليوم قبل الزوال بعد طلوع الفجر: جاز عند أبي حنيفة). قال في «الهداية»: وهذا استحسان، واختاره برهان الشريعة، والنسفي، وصدر الشريعة تصحيح».
If he wishes to hasten the departure (on the 12th), he departs to Makkah. And if he wishes to stay (for the 13th), he throws the three Jamarat on the fourth day after the sun's decline. If he throws on this day before the sun's decline after dawn, it is permissible according to Abu Hanifah. (If he wishes to hasten departure on the third day (of Tashreeq), he departs to Makkah before dawn of the fourth, not after, because the time for throwing has entered. And if he wishes to stay until the fourth, which is better, he throws the three Jamarat on the fourth day after the sun's decline as well, and if he throws on this day before the sun's decline after dawn, it is permissible according to Abu Hanifah. Al-Hidayah said: This is istihsan, and it was chosen by Burhan al-Shari'ah, al-Nasafi, and Sadr al-Shari'ah as the soundest view.)
Source pages p. 438

Commentary
This passage presents the rulings for the days of Tashreeq in Hajj. The base text states that if the pilgrim wishes to perform an early departure (النفر الأول) on the 12th of Dhul Hijjah, he may go to Makkah. If he wishes to stay until the 13th (the fourth day), he must throw the three Jamarat after the sun's decline (zawal). Abu Hanifa permits throwing before zawal but after dawn on the 13th, based on istihsan. The commentary clarifies that the early departure is from the third day (12th) before dawn of the 14th, and staying until the fourth day (13th) is better. The exception of Abu Hanifa is presented as istihsan in Al-Hidayah, and later scholars like Burhan al-Shari'ah, al-Nasafi, and Sadr al-Shari'ah have adopted it as the sound position. This is an intra-Hanafi dispute: the general ruling requires throwing after zawal, but Abu Hanifa's view is accepted as a concession.

Key Terms
النَّفْر (al-nafr): The departure from Mina to Makkah after completing the rituals of the days of Tashreeq
الزوال (al-zawal): The sun's decline from its zenith, marking the start of the time for midday prayer and for throwing the jamarat
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): Juristic preference: departing from strict analogy for ease

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on throwing the jamarat before zawal on the 13th of Dhul Hijjah according to Abu Hanifa?
A) It is invalid and the throw must be repeated after zawal.
B) It is permissible (jāʾiz) based on istihsan.
C) It is obligatory to throw only after zawal.
D) It is makruh tanzihi.

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa's istihsan-based exception for throwing jamarat before zawal on the 13th is the operative position in the Hanafi school, providing ease for pilgrims.

Ruling on Sending Luggage Ahead from Mina
Ruling on sending belongings ahead before nafr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sending luggage ahead from Mina and explain why it is makruh tanzihi.

Core Idea
Sending luggage ahead before departing Mina is mildly disliked—it does not invalidate Hajj but reduces its perfection.

During Hajj, pilgrims stay in Mina for the days of Tashreeq. Some may wish to send their heavy luggage to Makkah before they depart, to avoid the crowd. The Hanafi school addresses this action with a specific ruling based on a narration from Umar ibn al-Khattab. This lesson unpacks that ruling and clarifies its legal weight.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is sending one's luggage (thaqal) ahead from Mina before the nafr (departure to Makkah). The matn states it is disliked (yukrah).
Thaqal includes one's goods and servants.
2
Understand the key terms
Thaqal refers to heavy belongings and servants; nafr is the departure from Mina to Makkah after the days of Tashreeq.
3
Consider the evidence
The matn cites a narration from Umar (ra) who said, 'Whoever sends his luggage ahead before the departure has no Hajj.' This is the dalil.
The hadith is a single narration (ahad) and its wording is strong but interpreted figuratively.
4
Analyze Ibn Abidin's clarification
Ibn Abidin explains that 'no Hajj' means 'incomplete Hajj' and that the dislike is tanzihi (mild), not prohibitive. This is the mufta bihi position.
This clarification prevents misunderstanding that the Hajj is invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويكره أن يقدم الإنسانُ ثَقَلَه ) - بفتحتين ـ: متاعه وخدمه. (١) لما روى ابن أبي شيبة في المصنف ٦٨٩/٨ ١٥٦٢٧) عن عمر رضي الله عنه أنه قال: «مَن قَدَّمَ ثَقَله قبل النَّفْر : فلا حج له. اهـ قال ابن عابدين ١٤٧/٤: «أي : كاملاً، والظاهر أنها كراهة تنزيهية. عن البحر الرائق». اهـ

Ibn Abidin (4/147) said: 'i.e., incomplete, and it appears that it is a tanzihi dislike. From al-Bahr al-Raiq.'

This passage addresses the ruling on sending one's luggage and servants (thaqal) ahead from Mina before the departure (nufur). The matn states it is disliked (makruh). The commentary clarifies the meaning by explaining that thaqal refers to one's belongings and servants, and provides a hadith from Umar who said that whoever does so has no Hajj, meaning his Hajj is incomplete. Ibn Abidin clarifies that it is a tanzihi (preferable) dislike, not prohibitive. The ruling is based on the hadith and the idea that it preoccupies the heart.

Key Terms
ثَقَل (thaqal): One's luggage, baggage, and servants
النَّفْر (al-nafr): The departure from Mina to Makkah after the days of Tashreeq
كراهة تنزيهية (karahah tanzihiyyah): A mild dislike; not sinful but better avoided

The Hanafi school teaches that sending luggage ahead before the departure from Mina is only mildly disliked and does not affect the validity of Hajj.

Staying at Muhassab and Farewell Tawaf
Rulings on post-Mina actions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings for staying at Muhassab and the farewell tawaf, and explain why raml is omitted in the farewell tawaf.

Core Idea
Staying at Muhassab is sunnah; farewell tawaf is wajib without raml.

After completing the stoning at Mina, the pilgrim heads to Makkah. The Hanafi school recommends a brief stay at a place called al-Muhassab (near Makkah) and then performing the farewell tawaf. This lesson clarifies the rulings for these two acts and addresses a common misconception about raml (jogging) in the farewell tawaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two acts
The passage describes two recommended actions after departing Mina: staying at al-Muhassab and performing farewell tawaf.
2
Determine the ruling for each act
Staying at Muhassab is classified as sunnah (mustahabb), while farewell tawaf is wajib. The text indicates that the farewell tawaf is performed without raml.
Farewell tawaf is wajib according to the Hanafi school, not fard.
3
Understand the omission of raml
Raml (jogging) is a sunnah only in the initial tawaf of arrival. It is not prescribed for the farewell tawaf. The passage explicitly states 'without raml in it'.
Common mistake: assuming raml applies to all tawafs.
4
Analyze the condition about luggage
The footnote discusses sending luggage ahead. If the pilgrim feels secure about belongings and is not preoccupied, it is not disliked. This is based on the concept of shughl al-qalb (preoccupation of the heart).
This condition applies to the permissibility of leaving luggage, not to the acts themselves.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويقيم بها حتى يرمي . فإذا نَفَرَ إلى مكة : نزل بالمُحَصَّب . ثم طاف بالبيت سبعة أشواط، لا يَرْمُلُ فيها، (ويقيم بها ) : أي بمنى ( حتى يرمي) ؛ لأنه يوجب شغل قلبه النَّفْر إلى مكة بعد الرمي :] (فإذا نَفَرَ إلى مكة (نزل ندباً بالمُحَصَّب) - بضم، ففتحتين - : الأبطح (٢) ، ويقال له : البطحاء ، وخَيْفُ بني كنانة، قال في «الفتح»: وهو فناء مكة، وحده مابين الجبلين المتصلين بالمقابر، إلى الجبال المقابلة لذلك، مُصْعِداً في الشق الأيسر وأنت ذاهب إلى منى، مرتفعاً عن بطن الوادي. Al-Fath said: It is the courtyard of Makkah, its boundary is between the two mountains adjoining the cemeteries to the mountains opposite, ascending on the left side as you go to Mina, elevated above the valley floor. Then when he intends to travel, he performs tawaf of the House seven circuits, without raml in it. (2) It is now known in Makkah al-Mukarramah at the end of the Mu'abidah district when heading towards al-Shishah direction of Mina.

Commentary
This passage covers the recommended (sunnah) actions after the pilgrim completes the throwing of stones at Mina and before returning to Makkah. The base text says: he stays at Mina until he throws, then when he departs to Makkah, he stays at al-Muhassab (a place at the entrance of Makkah), and then performs tawaf of the Kaaba seven circuits without jogging (raml) because it is the farewell tawaf. The commentary explains that the reason for staying at Mina until the last throwing is to avoid having his heart preoccupied with his luggage if he sends it ahead. The stay at Muhassab is a sunnah and its location is described. The farewell tawaf is performed without raml because the rider is not required to jog. The footnote adds that the dislike of sending luggage ahead is conditional: if he feels secure about his belongings, it is not disliked. This is based on the reasoning of heart preoccupation. Footnote (2) identifies the modern location of Muhassab.

المُحَصَّب (al-muhassab): A place near Makkah, also called al-Abtah or al-Batha, where it is sunnah to stay after departing Mina
الرَّمَل (al-ramal): Jogging or walking briskly during tawaf, specifically in the first three circuits
طواف الوداع (tawaf al-wada'): The farewell circumambulation performed before leaving Makkah

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

The Post-Stoning Rites: Staying at Mina and Descent at al-Muhassab
Post-stoning rites: stay at Mina and travel to Makkah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on staying at Mina after stoning and explain the recommended nature of descending at al-Muhassab.

Core Idea
Staying at Mina after stoning is necessary; descending at al-Muhassab is a recommended sunnah.

After completing the stoning of the Jamarat, the pilgrim must remain in Mina until he departs for Makkah. Upon departure, it is a recommended sunnah to rest briefly at al-Muhassab, the area known as al-Abtah. This practice follows the example of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and prepares the pilgrim for the farewell circumambulation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the context
Recognize that this passage addresses actions after stoning the Jamarat during Hajj. The pilgrim has not yet left Mina permanently.
2
State the ruling on staying at Mina
The text 'ويقيم بها حتى يرمي' indicates that the pilgrim must stay at Mina until after stoning. This is a necessary (wajib) part of the rites.
The ruling is explicit in the matn.
3
Explain the recommendation of al-Muhassab
Upon departing to Makkah, it is recommended (نَدْباً) to dismount at al-Muhassab, a specific area between the mountains. This is a sunnah, not an obligation.
The commentator clarifies 'نزل ندباً'.

وهذا يقال له : (طوافُ الصَّدَر ) ، وطواف الوداع، وطواف آخر العهد بالبيت ؛ لأنه يودع البيت، ويصدر به.
كان
* (وهو واجب إلا على أهل مكة)، ومن في حكمهم ممن داخل الميقات؛ لأنهم لا يصدرون ولا يودعون، ويصلي بعده ركعتي الطواف.
ويأتي زمزم، فيشرب من مائها.
(۲)
ثم يأتي الملتزم (٢) ، فيضع صدره ووجهه عليه، ويتشبث بالأستار، ويدعو بما أحب
ويرجع فَهُقَرَى (۳) حتى يخرج من المسجد، وبصره ملاحظ
And he stays at it until he throws (the stones). Then when he departs to Makkah, he dismounts at al-Muhassab. Then he circumambulates the House seven circuits, without doing raml in them, to Makkah. And he stays at it: meaning at Mina until he throws; because it necessitates his heart being occupied with departing to Makkah after throwing. [2] Then when he departs to Makkah, he dismounts (recommended) at al-Muhassab – with damm, then fatha then shadda: al-Abtah, also called al-Batha and Khayf Bani Kinana. He said in al-Fath: It is the courtyard of Makkah, its limit is between the two mountains adjacent to the cemeteries up to the mountains opposite that, ascending on the left side as you go to Mina, elevated above the valley floor. [Tawaf al-Wada'] Then, when he intends travel, he circumambulates the House seven circuits without doing raml in them. (1) If he feels secure about his belongings in Makkah and his heart is not preoccupied with them, then it is not disliked, as in al-Durr al-Mukhtar 7/141, and Ibn Abidin narrated from al-Tahtawi that this ruling was researched by the author of al-Bahr, and followed by his brother in al-Nahr, based on the implication of the reason (ta'lil) of preoccupation of the heart. (2) It is now known in Makkah al-Mukarramah, at the end of the Ma'abada district, as you head towards al-Shisha towards Mina. And this is called Tawaf al-Sadar, and Tawaf al-Wada', and Tawaf Akhir al-Ahd bil-Bayt, because he bids farewell to the House and departs with it. * And it is obligatory except for the people of Makkah, and those in their ruling who are inside the miqat, because they do not depart nor bid farewell. And he prays after it two rak'ahs of tawaf. And he comes to Zamzam and drinks from its water. (2) Then he comes to al-Multazam (2), places his chest and face upon it, clings to the curtains, and supplicates as he wishes. And he retreats backwards (3) until he leaves the mosque, his gaze fixed (on the Ka'bah).
Source pages p. 439

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on al-Quduri covers the post-stoning rites of Hajj, specifically the recommended descent at al-Muhassab and the obligatory nature of Tawaf al-Sadr (farewell circumambulation). The commentator explains that the pilgrim should stay at Mina until after stoning the Jamarat, then upon departing to Makkah it is recommended to dismount at al-Muhassab, which is the area known as al-Abtah or Batha, located between the mountains near the cemetery. This is a sunnah act. The main ruling is that Tawaf al-Sadr, also called Tawaf al-Wada', is wajib (obligatory) for all pilgrims except the residents of Makkah and those who are within the miqat, because they are not considered 'departing' from the sacred precinct. This tawaf consists of seven circuits without raml (a brisk walk with shoulder movements), as raml is specific to the first tawaf (Tawaf al-Ifadah or al-Qudum). After completing the tawaf, the pilgrim prays the two rak'ahs of tawaf, drinks from Zamzam water, then proceeds to al-Multazam (the area between the Black Stone and the door of the Ka'bah) to make supplication, and finally exits the mosque walking backwards while keeping his gaze on the Ka'bah out of veneration. The text also notes that if the pilgrim's heart is not preoccupied with belongings left in Makkah, it is not disliked to leave without performing the farewell tawaf, but the relied-upon position is that it is wajib.

Key Terms
المحصب (al-Muhassab): The area between Makkah and Mina, also called al-Abtah or Batha, where pilgrims are recommended to rest after returning from Mina.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Obligatory
B) Recommended
C) Permissible but disliked
D) Prohibited

Key Takeaway
Descending at al-Muhassab is a recommended sunnah, not an obligation, but following it brings reward.

Tawaf al-Sadr: Obligation and Performance
Farewell circumambulation: ruling and details.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that Tawaf al-Sadr is wajib (obligatory) for non-residents of Makkah and describe its prescribed performance.

Core Idea
Tawaf al-Sadr is wajib for all except residents of Makkah—it is the final farewell to the sacred house.

After completing all rites of Hajj and before leaving Makkah, the pilgrim must perform a special circumambulation known as Tawaf al-Sadr (also Tawaf al-Wada'). The Hanafi school considers it wajib, meaning its omission requires a dam (sacrifice). Its performance is similar to other tawaf but without raml, and it concludes with prayers, drinking Zamzam, and supplication at al-Multazam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its names
Recognize that this tawaf is called Tawaf al-Sadr, Tawaf al-Wada', and Tawaf Akhir al-Ahd. It is performed after all Hajj rites before leaving Makkah.
2
State the ruling: wajib with exception
The text explicitly states 'وهو واجب إلا على أهل مكة'. Thus it is wajib for all except residents of Makkah and those within the miqat.
The exception is because they do not 'depart' from the sacred area.
3
Describe the performance
It consists of 7 circuits without raml. After tawaf, pray 2 rak'ahs, drink Zamzam, go to al-Multazam to supplicate, then exit backwards while looking at the Ka'bah.
The detailed acts are sunan.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school considers this tawaf as sunnah, not wajib. The Hanafi reliance on practice of the Prophet makes it wajib.
This affects whether a dam is required if omitted.

Tawaf al-Sadar: Ruling and Recommended Actions
Ruling statement with recommended actions after farewell tawaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of Tawaf al-Sadar in the Hanafi school and identify who is exempt from its obligation.

Core Idea
Tawaf al-Sadar is wajib upon every pilgrim except the people of Makkah.

This lesson examines the ruling of Tawaf al-Sadar (farewell circumambulation) as explained in al-Lubab. The passage establishes that it is a wajib act of Hajj, not a rukn, and clarifies the specific exemption for residents of Makkah and those within the miqat. It also guides the pilgrim on the recommended etiquette after completing this tawaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its hukm
Recognize that Tawaf al-Sadar is a wajib act, not a rukn. The text explicitly states 'وهو واجب' (it is obligatory).
Wajib means omission requires compensation (dam), while rukn invalidates the Hajj if omitted.
2
Locate the exemption
The text exempts 'أهل مكة' (people of Makkah) and 'من في حكمهم ممن داخل الميقات' (those within the miqat). Understand the reasoning: they do not 'depart' from Makkah in the same sense.
Those within the miqat are residents of the Haram area or nearby, who do not leave the sacred precincts.
3
Outline the recommended actions after tawaf
The passage lists: pray two rak'ahs, drink from Zamzam, go to al-Multazam to supplicate, then leave the mosque walking backward while gazing at the Ka'bah, and exit through Bab al-Hazwara.
These are sunan (recommended) acts that perfect the farewell.

Source Text

* (وهو واجب إلا على أهل مكة)، ومن في حكمهم ممن داخل الميقات؛ لأنهم لا يصدرون ولا يودعون، ويصلي بعده ركعتي الطواف.

And this is called: Tawaf al-Sadar, and the Tawaf of Farewell, and the Tawaf of the Last Covenant with the House, because he bids farewell to the House and departs by it. (And it is obligatory except for the people of Makkah) and those in their ruling among those within the miqat, because they do not depart nor bid farewell. And after it he prays two rak'ahs of tawaf. And he comes to Zamzam and drinks from its water. Then he comes to al-Multazam, and places his chest and face upon it, and clings to the covers, and makes supplication as he wishes. And he walks backward until he leaves the mosque, his gaze fixed on the House, weeping bitterly and sorrowful for its parting. And he exits from Bab al-Hazwara, known as the Gate of Farewell. (Then he returns to his family) because his acts of Hajj are complete.
Source pages p. 440

Commentary
This passage from al-Lubab is a commentary on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar. It states the ruling of Tawaf al-Sadar, also called Tawaf al-Wada' and Tawaf Akhir al-'Ahd. The author clarifies that this tawaf is wajib (obligatory) on all pilgrims except the people of Makkah and those within the miqat, as they do not depart from the city. After completing this tawaf, the pilgrim is recommended to perform two rak'ahs, drink from Zamzam, proceed to al-Multazam (the area between the Black Stone and the door of the Ka'bah) to supplicate, then leave the mosque walking backwards while gazing at the Ka'bah as a sign of reverence, and exit through the specific gate known as Bab al-Hazwara (the Gate of Farewell). Finally, the pilgrim returns home upon completion of the Hajj rituals.

Key Terms
طواف الصدر (Tawaf al-Sadar): The farewell circumambulation performed after completing all rites of Hajj before leaving Makkah.
الملتزم (al-Multazam): In this text, the area between the Black Stone and the door of the Ka'bah where the pilgrim places his chest and face while supplicating.
باب حزورة (Bab al-Hazwara): The gate of the Sacred Mosque known as the Gate of Farewell, through which the exiting pilgrim should leave.
