Dropping of Tawaf al-Qudum for Pilgrims Going Directly to Arafat
States that Tawaf al-Qudum is dropped for pilgrims going directly to Arafat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Tawaf al-Qudum when the pilgrim proceeds directly to Arafat and explain why it is dropped.

Core Idea
Tawaf al-Qudum is a sunnah greeting for entering the Sacred Mosque; if you don't enter, it drops without penalty.

In Hajj, upon reaching Makkah, pilgrims are encouraged to perform Tawaf al-Qudum as a greeting to the Kaaba. However, some pilgrims proceed directly to Arafat without first entering Makkah. This passage clarifies that such pilgrims are not required to perform this tawaf because it is only a sunnah act tied to entering the mosque, and leaving a sunnah incurs no compensation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
What is the act being discussed? It is Tawaf al-Qudum, the circumambulation performed upon arrival.
2
Identify the scenario
The scenario: the pilgrim does not enter Makkah but goes directly to Arafat and stands there.
3
State the ruling
The ruling: Tawaf al-Qudum is dropped (signed off) for this pilgrim.
4
Understand the reasoning
Tawaf al-Qudum is a greeting (tahiyyah) for the Sacred House. Since the pilgrim did not enter the mosque, this greeting is not applicable.
5
Note the legal consequence
No penalty (dam, sadaqah, or anything) is required for leaving it because it is a sunnah, not an obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن لم يدخل المُحْرِمُ مكةَ، وتوجه إلى عرفات، ووقف بها على ما قدمناه : فقد سَقَط عنه طواف القدوم؛ لأنه تحية البيت، ولم يدخل، ولا شيء عليه لتركه؛ لأنه سُنَّةٌ، ولا شيء بتركها.
If the pilgrim does not enter Makkah and proceeds to Arafat and stops there as we have described, then the Tawaf al-Qudum is dropped from him because it is the greeting of the House, and he did not enter, and nothing is upon him for leaving it because it is a sunnah, and nothing is required for leaving it.
Source pages p. 441

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary of al-Lubab on al-Quduri. It addresses the case of a pilgrim who heads directly to Arafat without first entering Makkah. Such a pilgrim does not perform Tawaf al-Qudum (the arrival circumambulation). The reason given is that Tawaf al-Qudum is a greeting (tahiyyah) of the Sacred Mosque, and since the pilgrim did not enter the mosque, this greeting is not required. The text further clarifies that Tawaf al-Qudum is a sunnah, not an obligation, so leaving it does not incur any penalty (dam or otherwise). This ruling applies specifically to those who proceed directly to Arafat from their miqat or from outside Makkah.

Key Terms
طواف القدوم (Tawaf al-Qudum): The circumambulation performed upon arrival at the Sacred Mosque in Makkah by a pilgrim entering ihram.
تحية البيت (Tahiyyat al-Bayt): The greeting of the House (Ka'bah); Tawaf al-Qudum is considered a greeting for the one who enters the mosque.

Key Takeaway

The Time for Standing at Arafah and Catching Hajj
States the time for standing and its effect on validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the time window for standing at Arafah and determine whether a pilgrim has caught the Hajj based on the timing of their standing.

Core Idea
A moment of standing at Arafah within its time saves the Hajj.

The standing at Arafah is the central pillar of Hajj, and its time is precisely defined. This passage from the matn and sharh clarifies the exact window: from the decline of the sun on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah until dawn on the 10th. Even a single moment within this period validates the entire Hajj. If a pilgrim misses this window, the Hajj is invalid, and they must repeat it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its legal category
Locate the act being ruled: standing at Arafah. Classify it as a rukn (pillar) of Hajj – its omission invalidates the Hajj. Note that the text describes catching it even for a moment as sufficient.
In Hanafi fiqh, the standing is one of the four pillars of Hajj.
2
Extract the time window
From the text: time is from 'zawal al-shams min yawm Arafah' (noon of the 9th) to 'tulu al-fajr min yawm al-Nahr' (dawn of the 10th). This is the period during which the standing must occur.
Dawn here is true dawn (fajr sadiq).
3
Determine the condition for catching Hajj
The condition is simple: performing the standing within that window, even for the briefest moment. The sharh interprets 'adrak al-hajj' as being safe from invalidity – the Hajj is valid.
The moment must be intentional and while at Arafah.
4
Analyze the consequence of missing it
If the pilgrim does not stand within that time, the text says 'the second pillar remains upon him' – implying the Hajj is not valid; the pilgrim must later complete it (i.e., repeat the Hajj). The Tawaf al-Ziyarah is the second pillar, but it cannot make up for the missed standing.
In practice, a missed standing means the Hajj is invalid; the pilgrim should perform an umrah and repeat Hajj the following year.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
*(ومن أدرك الوقوف بعرفة)، ولو لحظة في وقته، وهو (ما بين زوال الشمس من يوم عرفة، إلى طلوع الفجر من يوم النحر، فقد أدرك الحج) : أي أمن من فساده وإلا فقد بقي عليه الركن الثاني، وهو طواف الزيارة.
*(Whoever catches the standing at Arafah), even for a moment within its time, which is (between the decline of the sun on the day of Arafah and the dawn of the day of Nahr, has caught the Hajj): meaning he is safe from its invalidity; otherwise, the second pillar remains upon him, which is the Tawaf al-Ziyarah.
Source pages p. 442

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement about the time of the standing at Arafah and what constitutes catching the Hajj. The matn defines the time: from the decline of the sun on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah until dawn on the 10th (the day of Nahr). The sharh explains that if a person performs the standing within this time, even for a moment, they have caught the Hajj and it is valid; otherwise, the obligation of Hajj remains, and they must still perform the second pillar, Tawaf al-Ziyarah. The ruling indicates that the standing is a pillar (rukn) of Hajj, but catching it saves the Hajj from invalidity.

Key Terms
الوقوف بعرفة (al-wuquf bi Arafah): The standing at Arafah, which is a pillar of Hajj.
يوم النحر (yawm al-nahr): The 10th of Dhul Hijjah, the day of sacrifice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ending time for the standing at Arafah according to this passage?
A) Sunset of the 9th
B) Midnight of the 10th
C) Dawn of the day of Nahr (10th)
D) Noon of the 10th

Key Takeaway
Catching even a brief moment of standing at Arafah within its defined time window makes the Hajj valid; missing it invalidates the Hajj.

Women's Specific Rulings in Hajj: Head, Face, and Voice
States women's obligations regarding head covering, face uncovering, and voice lowering during Hajj.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on a woman's head covering, face covering, and voice during Hajj, and explain the evidence and the exception for covering the face when non-mahram men are present.

Core Idea
A woman in ihram must cover her head but uncovers her face, except when non-mahram men are present—then covering becomes wajib to avoid fitnah.

In this lesson, we examine the specific rulings for women during Hajj and Umrah. While most rituals are the same for men and women, there are key differences concerning covering the head and face, and the voice in talbiyah. The Hanafi school balances the requirements of ihram with the need to prevent fitnah, as demonstrated by the practice of the Prophet's companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Principle
The matn states that women are like men in all rites except where specified. This establishes that the default is equality except for specific exemptions.
The phrase 'wa al-mar'atu fi dhalika kullihi ka al-rajul' sets the baseline.
2
Note the Exception for Head and Face
A woman must cover her head because it is 'awrah, but she may uncover her face during ihram. However, if non-mahram men are present, she must cover her face to prevent fitnah.
The commentary clarifies that uncovering the face is for the ritual, but covering becomes necessary when there is a risk of fitnah.
3
Examine the Evidence
The hadith from Aisha (RA) reports that women would cover their faces with their jilbabs when non-mahram riders passed by, then uncover after they passed. This is the primary proof.
The hadith is from Sunan Abi Dawud (1829) and is debated in strength, but accepted by Hanafi scholars.
4
Apply the Ruling on Voice
A woman should not raise her voice in talbiyah; she only recites loud enough for herself to hear, to avoid attracting attention and causing fitnah.
This is based on the principle of avoiding fitnah, not on a specific proof in this passage.
5
Understand the Reasoning
All these rulings are rooted in the concept of fitnah. The Hanafi school prioritizes blocking avenues of temptation, even if it means modifying the normal ihram practice.
The commentary uses 'daf'an li al-fitnah' as the operative cause.

Commentary
This passage is a set of rulings specific to women in Hajj. The matn states that women are like men in the rites except that they must cover their heads (as it is 'awrah) and may uncover their faces. The commentary adds that she can uncover her face during ihram due to the ritual, but if non-mahram men are looking, she must cover it to avoid fitnah. The text then mentions she should not raise her voice in talbiyah, only loud enough for herself to hear, again to avoid fitnah. The commentary further discusses that if she covers her face from non-mahram, she should do so without the cloth touching her face (by propping it away). It cites hadith from A'ishah and others to show that women in the Prophet's time covered their faces when non-mahram passed by. The ruling is that covering the face from non-mahram during ihram is obligatory to prevent fitnah, though some say it is recommended. If she covers it in a way that touches the face, it is disliked. Covering the face less than a full day requires only charity (sadaqah).

Key Terms
الفتنة (al-fitnah): The temptation or disturbance caused by women's voices or faces to non-mahram men.
الجلباب (al-jilbāb): A loose outer garment used to cover the body; in the hadith, it is used to cover the face.
التلبية (al-talbīyah): The recitation of 'Labbayk Allahumma Labbayk...' during Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Consensus of the four schools

Key Takeaway
A woman in ihram may uncover her face, but must cover it wajib when non-mahram men are present, and she must lower her voice in talbiyah, all to prevent fitnah.

Women Not Raising Voice in Talbiyah During Hajj
Ruling on woman's talbiyah delivery

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a woman's talbiyah delivery and explain the rationale of preventing fitna.

Core Idea
A woman in ihram must recite talbiyah softly to avoid fitna, while men must raise their voices.

This brief passage from al-Quduri's matn, expanded by al-Maydani, draws a clear gender distinction in the Hajj ritual of talbiyah. While men are required to raise their voices, women are instructed to recite only loud enough for themselves to hear. The underlying rationale is preventive: avoiding fitna (temptation or disorder). Understanding this ruling requires appreciating how the Hanafi school balances ritual obligation with social considerations in the sacred state of ihram.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and subject
The act is the recitation of talbiyah (the pilgrim's chant 'Labbayk Allahumma labbayk...'). The subject is a female pilgrim in ihram.
Men are governed by a separate ruling: they must raise their voices.
2
State the prohibition
The text explicitly says 'wa la tarfa' sawtaha' – she should not raise her voice. This is a directive indicating dislike (karahah) rather than absolute prohibition.
The Hanafi level is makruh tanzihi, not haram.
3
Determine the prescribed method
She should recite audibly enough for herself to hear ('bal tusmi' nafsaha'). This means a soft, moderate voice, not a whisper or silence.
She must articulate the words, not merely think them.
4
Locate the rationale (illah)
The reason given is 'daf'an lil-fitnah' – to prevent temptation or disorder. The voice of a woman is considered a potential source of fitna for men, so she must moderate it.
This is a preventive measure, not a judgment on the worth of her voice.
5
Note the gender contrast
Compare with men: they are required to raise their voices in talbiyah. The difference arises from the risk of fitna, which is not present when men raise their voices.
The same fitna consideration applies to other aspects of ihram, such as covering the face.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا ترفع صوتها بالتلبية . بل تُسمع نفسها؛ دفعاً للفتنة.
And she should not raise her voice in talbiyah. Rather, she makes only herself hear it, to prevent fitna.
Source pages p. 443

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from the matn of al-Quduri, expanded by al-Maydani. It specifies that a woman in ihram should not raise her voice when reciting the talbiyah (labbayk). Instead, she should recite it audibly enough for herself to hear, avoiding any risk of fitna (temptation) that might arise from men hearing her voice. The rationale is preventive: the voice of a woman is considered 'awrah in the sense of causing temptation, so she must moderate it. This ruling is specific to women; men are required to raise their voices in talbiyah.

Key Terms
التلبية (al-talbiyah): The utterance 'Labbayk Allahumma labbayk...' recited by a pilgrim upon entering ihram.
الفتنة (al-fitnah): Temptation or trial, specifically the risk of arousing sexual desire or disorder.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) She should not recite it at all; it is not required for women.

Key Takeaway
A woman must recite talbiyah softly to avoid fitna, unlike men who raise their voices.

Women Covering Face in Ihram: The Permissible Method and Its Analogy
Ruling on permissible method of face covering in ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for valid face covering in ihram and explain the qiyas that underlies it.

Core Idea
A woman in ihram may cover her face if the covering does not touch it, analogous to seeking shade.

Women in ihram face a special rule: they may cover their faces from non-mahram men, but the method matters. This lesson focuses on the condition that the covering must be loose, not touching the skin, drawing an analogy to seeking shade under a litter (mahmil). Understanding this condition prevents common errors and clarifies the school's reasoning.

Guided Path
1
State the basic ruling
From the text, identify that the act of letting down a covering over the face is permissible (ja'iz) under a specific condition.
The text opens with 'if she lets down something over it and keeps it away from it, it is permissible'.
2
Identify the condition
The condition is 'tujafihi 'anhu' – the covering must be kept away from the face, not touching or sticking. Note the reasoning: it is like seeking shade under a mahmil, which is permitted.
The analogy (qiyas) to mahmil is crucial: a mahmil does not touch the head, just as the covering should not touch the face.
3
Understand the dislike of tight covering
Contrast the permissible method with the disliked one: if the covering is tight and touching the face, it is makruh tanzihan. The text also mentions a penalty for less than a full day of covering.
The ruling balances preventing fitna and avoiding a prohibited action (covering in a way similar to a man's ihram head-covering).
4
Apply to a scenario
Consider a woman wearing a niqab that is tied snugly around her face. According to this lesson, that method is disliked unless necessary to avoid fitna; the preferred method is a loose drape that does not contact the skin.
The modern practice of wearing a loose face veil or using a cap under the covering is derived from this ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سدلت شيئاً عليه، وجافتـه عنـه جـاز؛ لأنه بمنزلة الاستظلال بالمحمل. وجهها للأجانب، فتسدل عليه ما يستره وجوباً، كما في النهاية، والمحيط، واستحباباً كما في الفتح؛ دفعاً للفتنة. ولا تجعله لاصقاً مماساً لوجهها، بل تجافيه بإرخاء الستر من فوق شيء تجعله على رأسها، ينظر ابن عابدين ١٦٤/٧، ومصادره العديدة مناسك علي القاري ص ۷۸. ولو سترت وجهها عن الأجانب بما يلاصق وجهها يكره، لكن الفتنة أشد، وستره دون يوم كامل: يوجب الصدقة فقط. بل نقل الحافظ ابن حجر في فتح الباري ٤٠٦/٣ عن ابن المنذر عن فاطمة بنت المنذر قالت: كنا نخمر وجوهنا ونحن محرمات مع أسماء بنت أبي بكر الصديق - تعني : جدتها ـ (الموطأ ٣٢٨/١). وعن مجاهد عن عائشة رضي الله عنها قالت: كان الركبان يمرون بنا ونحن مع رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم مُحرمات، فإذا حاذوا بنا سدلت إحدانا جلبابهـا مـن رأسها على وجهها، فإذا جاوزونا كشفناه. سنن أبي داود ٤٥٧/٢ (١٨٢٩)، سنن ابن ماجه (۲۹۲٥)، مسند أحمد ٣٠/٦ ، وفي سنده مقال، ينظر تهذيب سنن أبي داود للمنذري ٣٥٤/٢ ، أما ابن حجر في الفتح ٤٠٦/٣ : فقال: فيه ضعف، لكنه قال التلخيص الحبير ۲۷۲/۲: أخرجه ابن خزيمة وقال في القلب من يزيد بن أبي زياد، ولكن وَرَدَ من وجه آخر وساقه، وصححه الحاكم. وروى ابن أبي خيثمة أن امرأة كانت تأبى أن تغطي وجهها وهي مُحرِمة، فرفعت الله عنها خمارها من صدرها فغطّت به وجهها». اهـ باختصار. رضي
If she lets down something over it (her face) and keeps it away from it, it is permissible, because it is like seeking shade with a litter. Her face is for non-mahram, so she lets down over it what covers it, obligatorily, as in al-Nihaya and al-Muhit, and recommended as in al-Fath; to prevent fitna. And she should not make it adhesive and touching her face, rather she should keep it away by loosening the covering from above something she places on her head, see Ibn Abidin 7/164 and his many sources, Manasik Ali al-Qari p. 78. And if she covers her face from non-mahram with something that touches her face, it is disliked, but the fitna is worse, and covering it for less than a full day: only requires charity. Rather, al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar in Fath al-Bari 3/406 narrated from Ibn al-Mundhir from Fatima bint al-Mundhir who said: We used to cover our faces while we were in ihram with Asma bint Abi Bakr al-Siddiq - meaning her grandmother - (al-Muwatta 1/328). And from Mujahid from Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) who said: The riders used to pass by us while we were with the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) in ihram, so when they came near us, one of us would let down her jilbab from her head over her face, and when they passed by we would uncover it. Sunan Abi Dawud 2/457 (1829), Sunan Ibn Majah (2925), Musnad Ahmad 6/30, and in its chain there is discussion, see Tahdhib Sunan Abi Dawud by al-Mundhiri 2/354. As for Ibn Hajar in al-Fath 3/406: he said it is weak, but he said in al-Talkhis al-Habir 2/272: Ibn Khuzayma narrated it and said there is doubt about Yazid ibn Abi Ziyad, but it came from another path and he cited it, and al-Hakim authenticated it. And Ibn Abi Khaythama narrated that a woman refused to cover her face while in ihram, so Allah lifted her khimar from her chest and she covered her face with it. End quote briefly. Radya.
Source pages p. 443

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the issue of a woman covering her face during ihram. The commentator, al-Maydani, begins by stating the condition: if a woman lets down a covering over her face but keeps it from touching (by using a structure like a cap or canopy), it is permissible. This is compared to seeking shade under a litter (mahmil), which does not break ihram. Then he states that the woman's face is 'awrah with respect to non-mahram men, so she must cover it. He notes a difference within the Hanafi school: some (like the authors of al-Nihaya and al-Muhit) say it is wajib (obligatory) to cover, while others (like the author of al-Fath) say it is mustahabb (recommended). The reason for covering is to prevent fitna. Then he gives the method: she should not let the covering stick to her face; rather, she should drape it loosely from above something placed on her head. If she covers tightly with something touching the face, it is makruh (disliked), but the fitna is worse, so she may do it out of necessity. Covering for less than a full day only requires sadaqah (charity). The commentator then provides hadith proofs: the practice of the Sahabiyyat (Fatima bint al-Mundhir and Aisha) who covered their faces when non-mahram riders passed by, and the story of a woman who was forced to cover by divine intervention. These proofs support the permissibility and desirability of covering the face in ihram.

Key Terms
السدل (al-sadl): Letting down a covering (like a jilbab or khimar) over the face from the head.
المحمل (al-mahmil): A litter or covered howdah on a camel; used in analogy for a canopy-like covering.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The covering must be made of white fabric.
B) The covering must not touch the face directly.
C) The covering must be removed when entering Makka.
D) The covering must be secured with an aqal.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits a woman to cover her face in ihram provided the covering is loose and does not touch her skin, analogous to seeking shade under a litter.

The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Face Covering in Ihram: Wajib or Mustahabb?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on obligation vs recommendation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi views on whether face covering in ihram is wajib or mustahabb, citing the proof for each.

Core Idea
Covering the face for women in ihram is wajib according to some Hanafis and mustahabb according to others; the aim is to prevent fitna.

While the previous lesson covered the method (looseness), this lesson tackles a deeper disagreement within the Hanafi school: is covering the face from non-mahram in ihram obligatory (wajib) or merely recommended (mustahabb)? The source notes that authors like al-Nihaya and al-Muhit declare it wajib, while al-Fath considers it mustahabb. This ikhtilaf has real practical consequences for sin and reward. Let us unpick the proofs and reasoning behind each view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Locate in the text the two phrases: 'wajiban' (obligatorily) from al-Nihaya/al-Muhit, and 'istihbaban' (recommended) from al-Fath. Note that both aim to prevent fitna.
The text states: 'فتسدل عليه ما يستره وجوباً، كما في النهاية، والمحيط، واستحباباً كما في الفتح'.
2
Examine the proof for wajib
The wajib view likely relies on the hadith of Aisha and the practice of the Sahabiyyat, showing consistent covering. Also the qiyas on mahmil and the general principle that a woman's face is 'awrah.
The text quotes the hadith of Aisha and Fatima bint al-Mundhir as evidence for covering, supporting the wajib position.
3
Examine the proof for mustahabb
The mustahabb view argues that the face is not 'awrah in ihram specifically (as men uncover their heads), and covering is only a precaution. The hadith shows covering when riders pass but uncovering afterwards, indicating it is not a constant obligation.
The text itself cites the hadith that they uncovered after the riders passed, suggesting it is situational.
4
Understand the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
If wajib, leaving the face uncovered without a valid excuse incurs sin and may require dam (sacrificial penalty). If mustahabb, there is no sin, but reward for covering.
The text also mentions that covering for less than a full day only requires sadaqah, which aligns with a lenient view.
5
Note the mufta bihi
Later Hanafi fatwa tends towards mustahabb (as in al-Fath), but many contemporary scholars lean towards wajib due to modern fitna. The text does not resolve definitively; see Ibn Abidin for further discussion.
The reference to Ibn Abidin 7/164 points to later tarjih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سدلت شيئاً عليه، وجافتـه عنـه جـاز؛ لأنه بمنزلة الاستظلال بالمحمل. وجهها للأجانب، فتسدل عليه ما يستره وجوباً، كما في النهاية، والمحيط، واستحباباً كما في الفتح؛ دفعاً للفتنة. ولا تجعله لاصقاً مماساً لوجهها، بل تجافيه بإرخاء الستر من فوق شيء تجعله على رأسها، ينظر ابن عابدين ١٦٤/٧، ومصادره العديدة مناسك علي القاري ص ۷۸. ولو سترت وجهها عن الأجانب بما يلاصق وجهها يكره، لكن الفتنة أشد، وستره دون يوم كامل: يوجب الصدقة فقط. بل نقل الحافظ ابن حجر في فتح الباري ٤٠٦/٣ عن ابن المنذر عن فاطمة بنت المنذر قالت: كنا نخمر وجوهنا ونحن محرمات مع أسماء بنت أبي بكر الصديق - تعني : جدتها ـ (الموطأ ٣٢٨/١). وعن مجاهد عن عائشة رضي الله عنها قالت: كان الركبان يمرون بنا ونحن مع رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم مُحرمات، فإذا حاذوا بنا سدلت إحدانا جلبابهـا مـن رأسها على وجهها، فإذا جاوزونا كشفناه. سنن أبي داود ٤٥٧/٢ (١٨٢٩)، سنن ابن ماجه (۲۹۲٥)، مسند أحمد ٣٠/٦ ، وفي سنده مقال، ينظر تهذيب سنن أبي داود للمنذري ٣٥٤/٢ ، أما ابن حجر في الفتح ٤٠٦/٣ : فقال: فيه ضعف، لكنه قال التلخيص الحبير ۲۷۲/۲: أخرجه ابن خزيمة وقال في القلب من يزيد بن أبي زياد، ولكن وَرَدَ من وجه آخر وساقه، وصححه الحاكم. وروى ابن أبي خيثمة أن امرأة كانت تأبى أن تغطي وجهها وهي مُحرِمة، فرفعت الله عنها خمارها من صدرها فغطّت به وجهها». اهـ باختصار. رضي
If she lets down something over it (her face) and keeps it away from it, it is permissible, because it is like seeking shade with a litter. Her face is for non-mahram, so she lets down over it what covers it, obligatorily, as in al-Nihaya and al-Muhit, and recommended as in al-Fath; to prevent fitna. And she should not make it adhesive and touching her face, rather she should keep it away by loosening the covering from above something she places on her head, see Ibn Abidin 7/164 and his many sources, Manasik Ali al-Qari p. 78. And if she covers her face from non-mahram with something that touches her face, it is disliked, but the fitna is worse, and covering it for less than a full day: only requires charity. Rather, al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar in Fath al-Bari 3/406 narrated from Ibn al-Mundhir from Fatima bint al-Mundhir who said: We used to cover our faces while we were in ihram with Asma bint Abi Bakr al-Siddiq - meaning her grandmother - (al-Muwatta 1/328). And from Mujahid from Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) who said: The riders used to pass by us while we were with the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) in ihram, so when they came near us, one of us would let down her jilbab from her head over her face, and when they passed by we would uncover it. Sunan Abi Dawud 2/457 (1829), Sunan Ibn Majah (2925), Musnad Ahmad 6/30, and in its chain there is discussion, see Tahdhib Sunan Abi Dawud by al-Mundhiri 2/354. As for Ibn Hajar in al-Fath 3/406: he said it is weak, but he said in al-Talkhis al-Habir 2/272: Ibn Khuzayma narrated it and said there is doubt about Yazid ibn Abi Ziyad, but it came from another path and he cited it, and al-Hakim authenticated it. And Ibn Abi Khaythama narrated that a woman refused to cover her face while in ihram, so Allah lifted her khimar from her chest and she covered her face with it. End quote briefly. Radya.
Source pages p. 443

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the issue of a woman covering her face during ihram. The commentator, al-Maydani, begins by stating the condition: if a woman lets down a covering over her face but keeps it from touching (by using a structure like a cap or canopy), it is permissible. This is compared to seeking shade under a litter (mahmil), which does not break ihram. Then he states that the woman's face is 'awrah with respect to non-mahram men, so she must cover it. He notes a difference within the Hanafi school: some (like the authors of al-Nihaya and al-Muhit) say it is wajib (obligatory) to cover, while others (like the author of al-Fath) say it is mustahabb (recommended). The reason for covering is to prevent fitna. Then he gives the method: she should not let the covering stick to her face; rather, she should drape it loosely from above something placed on her head. If she covers tightly with something touching the face, it is makruh (disliked), but the fitna is worse, so she may do it out of necessity. Covering for less than a full day only requires sadaqah (charity). The commentator then provides hadith proofs: the practice of the Sahabiyyat (Fatima bint al-Mundhir and Aisha) who covered their faces when non-mahram riders passed by, and the story of a woman who was forced to cover by divine intervention. These proofs support the permissibility and desirability of covering the face in ihram.

Key Terms
وجوباً (wujūban): Obligatorily; indicating the action is wajib (obligatory but not a fundamental pillar).
استحباباً (istiḥbāban): Recommended; indicating the action is mustahabb (recommended but not obligatory).
دفعاً للفتنة (daf'an lil-fitnah): To repel fitna (temptation or social disorder); the underlying reason for the ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi (operative ruling) in later Hanafi fatwa, what is the ruling on a woman covering her face in ihram?
A) It is wajib (obligatory) without exception.
B) It is mustahabb (recommended) and not obligatory.
C) It is prohibited (haram).
D) It is fard (a pillar of ihram).

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds two views on face covering in ihram: wajib (obligatory) and mustahabb (recommended); the mufta bihi is mustahabb, but covering is strongly encouraged to prevent fitna.

Women's Specific Rulings in Ihram: Tawaf, Sa'y, Hair, Dress, and Khuntha
Rulings on women's actions in tawaf, sa'y, hair cutting, dress, and khuntha

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five specific rulings for women in ihram regarding tawaf, sa'y, hair cutting, dress, and the treatment of khuntha mushkil.

Core Idea
Women in ihram do not perform men-specific rituals and are permitted sewn clothes.

This passage from the Lubab al-Mukhtar summarizes key differences between male and female ihram practices. Understanding these rulings prevents common errors and ensures valid performance of Hajj and Umrah. The rulings are clear and emphasize precaution in ambiguous gender cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts mentioned
The passage lists five items: raml in tawaf, idtiba', running in sa'y, shaving head, wearing sewn clothes/khuff, and khuntha mushkil.
2
Determine the ruling for women for each act
For raml/idtiba': prohibited. For running in sa'y: prohibited. For shaving: prohibited, instead trim. For dress: permitted. For khuntha: treated as woman.
3
Understand the gender distinction
Many rulings are opposites: what is sunnah for men (raml, idtiba', running) is not for women; what is prohibited for men (sewn clothes) is allowed for women.
4
Apply the precaution for khuntha
Khuntha mushkil adopts women's rules to ensure they haven't missed obligations.
This is a cautious approach, as the actual gender may be male.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا تَرْمُلُ في الطواف، ولا تضطبع. ولا تسعى بين الميلين الأخضرين . ولا تحلق رأسها، ولكن تُقصر من ربع شعرها، كما مر. وتلبس المخيط، والخفين. والخنثى المُشكِل كالمرأة فيما ذُكِر ؛ احتياطاً.
And she does not do raml in tawaf, nor does she do idtiba'. And she does not run between the two green milestones. And she does not shave her head, but she trims from a quarter of her hair, as passed. And she wears sewn clothes and khuff. And a problematic hermaphrodite (khuntha mushkil) is like a woman in what was mentioned; as a precaution.
Source pages p. 444

Commentary
This passage states several rulings specific to women in ihram. First, women are not to perform raml (walking briskly with shoulders moving) in tawaf, nor idtiba' (uncovering the right shoulder) – these are sunnah for men only. Second, they are not to run (sa'y) quickly between the two green milestones in the sa'y between Safa and Marwa; they should proceed at a normal pace. Third, women are prohibited from shaving their heads (which is a rite for men); instead, they must trim their hair. The commentary adds that the trim should be from a quarter of the head's hair length (i.e., cutting the length of a fingertip from each lock). Fourth, women are permitted to wear sewn garments (like ordinary clothes) and khuff (leather socks) during ihram – unlike men who must wear unsewn garments. Finally, a khuntha mushkil (a hermaphrodite whose gender is unclear) is treated like a woman in all these rulings, as a precaution to ensure fulfilling the obligations without violation.

Key Terms
الرمول (al-raml): Walking briskly with short steps and moving the shoulders during tawaf; a sunnah for men.
الاضطباع (al-idtiba'): Uncovering the right shoulder by placing the ihram cloth under the right armpit; a sunnah for men in tawaf.
المخيط (al-makhit): Sewn garments; clothes that are stitched, normally prohibited for men in ihram but allowed for women.
الخفين (al-khuffayn): Leather socks that cover the feet and ankles; normally prohibited for men in ihram but allowed for women.
الخنثى المشكل (al-khuntha al-mushkil): A person with ambiguous genitalia where the gender cannot be determined; treated as female in these rulings as a precaution.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What must a woman do instead of shaving her head during Hajj?
A) She must shave like a man.
B) She must cut a quarter of the length of her hair.
C) She must not cut her hair at all.
D) She must cut all her hair short.

Key Takeaway
Women in ihram have distinct rules: they avoid men-specific actions and are permitted sewn clothes; khuntha mushkil follows women's rulings as a precaution.

Women's Special Rulings in Hajj: Ramal, Sa'y, and Hair Shortening
Ruling statement on women's exemptions and requirements in Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings for women in tawaf, sa'y, and hair removal during Hajj, and apply the precautionary rule for the hermaphrodite.

Core Idea
Women do not perform ramal, idtiba', or running in sa'y; they shorten hair instead of shaving, and may wear stitched garments.

The rituals of Hajj have specific rulings that differentiate between men and women. This passage from Al-Lubab clearly outlines the exceptions granted to women in three key areas: tawaf, sa'y, and the exit from ihram. Understanding these distinctions is essential for correct practice and for addressing common confusions.

Guided Path
1
Identify each act and its ruling for women
Go through the passage line by line: ramal, idtiba', running in sa'y are not performed; shaving is prohibited; taqsir is required; stitched clothes are permitted. Determine the hukm (obligation, prohibition, permission) for each.
Not all acts have the same hukm level; distinguish between what is not required, what is forbidden, and what is permissible.
2
Understand the wisdom behind exemptions
Reflect on why women are exempt from ramal and running: these actions display physical strength and are not expected of women. The same applies to idtiba'. Shaving is not required because it would remove all hair, which is excessive for women.
The rationale helps in remembering the rulings and applying them to similar situations.
3
Detail the hair removal ruling
Women must shorten their hair (taqsir) by cutting about a quarter of its length. This is wajib. Shaving is haram for women. Clarify the required quantity.
Taqsir is also performed by men in certain types of Hajj, but for women it is the only option.
4
Apply the precautionary rule for hermaphrodites
The khuntha mushkil (ambiguous genitalia) is treated as a woman in these rulings because caution (ihtiyat) demands following the stricter set of rules.
This is a general principle for khuntha: in acts of worship, they follow the more restrictive ruling when gender is uncertain.
5
Practice with a scenario
Take a female pilgrim: advise her not to run in sa'y, to wear sewn clothes if needed, and to shorten her hair after tawaf al-ifadah. Check understanding.
Emphasize that she may feel confused if she sees men doing ramal; reassure her that her worship is complete without it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا تَرْمُلُ في الطواف، ولا تسعى بين الميلين الأخضرين. ولا تحلق رأسها، ولكن تُقصر. (ولا تَرْمُلُ في الطواف)، ولا تضطبع. (ولا تسعى بين الميلين الأخضرين. ولا تحلق رأسها، ولكن تُقصر) من ربع شعرها، كما مر. وتلبس المخيط، والخفين. والخنثى المُشكِل كالمرأة فيما ذُكِر ؛ احتياطاً.
She does not do ramal in tawaf, nor does she run between the two green pillars. She does not shave her head, but she shortens. (She does not do ramal in tawaf) nor idtiba'. The hermaphrodite is like a woman in what has been mentioned, out of caution.
Source pages p. 444

Commentary
This passage from Al-Lubab details several rulings specific to women during Hajj. Women are exempt from the sunnah acts of ramal (quick walking with chest out) and idtiba' (uncovering the right shoulder) in tawaf. They also do not run between the green pillars in sa'y because these are acts of showing strength, which are not required of women. Women must not shave their heads; instead, they shorten their hair by cutting about a quarter of its length, similar to the tamattu' or qiran procedure. Women are permitted to wear sewn garments (makhit) and khuffs (leather socks), unlike men who must wear ihram. Finally, a hermaphrodite (khuntha mushkil) is treated as a woman in all these rulings as a precautionary measure because their true gender is uncertain.

Key Terms
الرمل (ar-ramal): Quick walking with short steps and slight jiggling, performed by men in the first three rounds of tawaf.
السعي بين الميلين الأخضرين (as-sa'y bayn al-milayn al-akhdarayn): Running between the two green pillars (markers) in the sa'y ritual between Safa and Marwah.
التقصير (at-taqsir): Shortening the hair by cutting about a quarter of its length, the required act for women exiting ihram.
الخنثى المشكل (al-khuntha al-mushkil): A person with ambiguous genitalia whose gender cannot be determined.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Shorten it by cutting about a quarter
C) Leave it as is
D) Cut it all off

Key Takeaway
Women in Hajj are exempt from ramal and running in sa'y, must shorten their hair, and may wear stitched garments; the hermaphrodite follows the woman's ruling out of caution.

The Superiority of Qiran and Its Method
Declares qiran superior and defines its method

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the superiority of qiran, describe its valid methods, and identify the ruling for the reverse order.

Core Idea
Qiran combines umrah and hajj in one continuous ihram, making it the most virtuous form of Hajj in the Hanafi school.

When a Muslim sets out for Hajj, they have three options: tamattu‘, ifrad, or qiran. The Hanafi school teaches that qiran carries the highest reward because it maintains a single state of consecration from the miqat to the completion of both rites. This lesson unpacks the precise method of qiran and the ruling for its reverse order.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling on Virtue
The passage states that qiran is 'afdal' (superior) to tamattu‘ and ifrad. This is a preference of reward, not an obligation.
The Hanafi position is sunnah mu’akkadah (emphasized sunnah) in terms of virtue.
2
Define Qiran
Qiran is combining umrah and hajj in a single ihram from the miqat, either by intending both together or by adding one to the other before completing most of the tawaf of the first.
'Most of the tawaf' means more than three rounds (i.e., four or more).
3
Recognize the Two Valid Methods
Method 1: Declare intention for both umrah and hajj at the miqat. Method 2: Assume ihram for umrah first, then add hajj before performing most of the umrah tawaf.
Both methods achieve qiran. The first is more straightforward.
4
Understand the Reverse Order
If one assumes ihram for hajj first and then adds umrah, this is also considered qiran but it is makruh (disliked) and requires a dam (sacrifice).
The dam is a form of shukr (thanksgiving) for the irregularity.
5
Acknowledge the Ikhtilaf with the Shafi‘i School
The Shafi‘i school holds that ifrad (only hajj) is superior. The Hanafi reasoning is based on the continuity of ihram.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; each school follows its own proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب القرآن. القران عندنا أفضل من التمتع والإفراد. وصفةُ القرآن : أن يُهِلَّ بالعمرة والحج معاً من الميقات، حقيقة، أو حكماً بأن أحرم بالعمرة أولاً، ثم بالحج قبل أن يطوف لها أكثر الطواف؛ لأن الجمع قد تحقق ؛ لأن الأكثر منها قائم، وكذا عكسه (۱) ، لكنه مكروه. (۱) بأن يُدخل إحرام العمرة على الحج قبل أن يطوف للقدوم وإن أساء، وعليه دم شكر، أو بعد طواف القدوم وإن لزمه .دم ينظر ابن عابدين ١٧٤/٧ - ١٧٥ .
Chapter of Qiran. Qiran with us is superior to tamattu' and ifrad. The description of qiran is that one raises the talbiyah for umrah and hajj together from the miqat, either literally or legally, such that one assumes ihram for umrah first, then for hajj before having performed most of the tawaf for it, because the combination has been realized since most of it is standing. Likewise the reverse (1), but it is makruh. (1) That one brings the ihram of umrah into hajj before performing tawaf al-qudum, even if it is bad, and upon him is the dam of thanksgiving, or after tawaf al-qudum even if it is required. See Ibn Abidin 7/174-175.
Source pages p. 445

Commentary
This passage from Al-Lubab begins the chapter on qiran. According to the Hanafi school, qiran (combining umrah and hajj in one state of ihram) is more virtuous than tamattu' (performing umrah first, then hajj with separate ihrams) and ifrad (performing only hajj). The reasoning is that qiran involves continuous ihram from the miqat until completion, whereas tamattu' breaks it. The proper method of qiran is to declare intention for both umrah and hajj simultaneously from the miqat, or to first assume ihram for umrah and then add hajj before completing most of the tawaf for umrah. If one reverses the order (first hajj then umrah), it is still considered qiran but is makruh and requires a dam (sacrifice).

Key Terms
القرآن (al-qiran): Combining umrah and hajj in a single ihram from the miqat, either by intending both together or by adding one to the other before significant tawaf.
التمتع (at-tamattu'): Performing umrah first, then exiting ihram, then later assuming ihram for hajj in the same season.
الإفراد (al-ifrad): Performing only hajj without umrah in the same journey.
الإهلال (al-ihlal): Pronouncing the talbiyah to enter the state of ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How is qiran performed according to the Hanafi school?
A) Ihram for umrah first, then hajj after completing all rituals
B) Ihram for hajj first, then add umrah, which is recommended
C) Ihram for both umrah and hajj together from the miqat
D) Ihram for hajj only, then add umrah after tawaf al-qudum

Key Takeaway
Qiran is the most virtuous form of hajj in the Hanafi school, performed by combining umrah and hajj in one continuous ihram.

Definition and Superiority of Qiran
Defines qiran and argues for its superiority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of qiran and explain why the Hanafi school considers it superior to tamattu' and ifrad.

Core Idea
Qiran is the best because it maintains continuous ihram from miqat to completion.

The Hajj chapter introduces three forms: ifrad, tamattu', and qiran. This lesson focuses on qiran, its linguistic and legal meaning, and the Hanafi preference for it over the other two forms. The key argument hinges on the continuity of the state of ihram.

Guided Path
1
Define qiran linguistically
The Arabic root indicates 'joining'. The legal definition is combining umrah and hajj in one state of ihram from the miqat.
2
Identify the Hanafi claim
The passage states that qiran is superior (afdal) to tamattu' and ifrad.
3
Understand the proof
The superiority is due to continuous ihram from miqat until completion, which is lacking in tamattu' (where one exits ihram after umrah).
This is a rational legal argument (dalil aqli).
4
Note the effective combining methods
Qiran can be done by entering ihram for both simultaneously, or by entering for umrah first then hajj before performing most of the tawaf. The reverse order (adding umrah to hajj) is disliked.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب القرآن
مصدر قرن من باب ضَرَب ونَصَرَ. (القِرَانُ) لغة: الجمع بين الشيئين مطلقاً.
وشرعاً: الجمع بين إحرام العمرة والحج في سفر واحد. * وهو (عندنا أفضل من التمتع ، والإفراد)؛ لأن فيه استدامة الإحرام بهما من الميقات إلى أن يفرغ منهما، ولا كذلك التمتع،
فكان القران أولى منه. «هداية».
(وصفةُ القِرآن : أن يُهِلَّ بالعمرة والحــج معـاً مـن الميقات)، حقيقة، أو حكماً بأن أحرم بالعمرة أولاً، ثم بالحج قبل أن يطوف لها أكثر الطواف؛ لأن الجمع قد تحقق ؛ لأن الأكثر منها قائم، وكذا عكسه (۱) ، لكنه مكروه.
(۱) بأن يُدخل إحرام العمرة على الحج قبل أن يطوف للقدوم وإن أساء، وعليه دم شكر، أو بعد طواف القدوم وإن لزمه .دم ينظر ابن عابدين ١٧٤/٧ - ١٧٥ .

ثم: ويقول عقيب الصلاة : اللهم إني أريد العمرة والحج، فيسرهما لي، وتقبلهما مني . فإذا دخل مكة : ابتدأ فطاف بالبيت سبعة أشواط، يَرْمُلُ في الثلاثة الأول منها، ويمشي فيما بقي على هيئته . وسعى بعدها بين الصفا والمروة، وهذه أفعال العمرة.
وإذا عَزَم على أدائهما يُسنُّ له سؤال التيسير فيهما، ويُقدم ذكر العمرة على الحج فيه ؛ ولذا قال : (ويقول عقيب الصلاة: اللـهـم إني أريد العمرة والحج، فيسرهما لي، وتقبلهما مني). وفي بعض النسخ): تقديم ذكـر الـحـج على العمرة، والأُولى: أولى، وكذلك يقدمها في التلبية ؛ لأنه يبدأ بأفعال العمرة، فكذلك يبدأ بذكرها. «هداية».
فإذا دخل مكة: ابتدأ بأفعال العمرة ، فطاف بالبيت سبعة أشواط) وجوباً، والفرضُ منها أكثرها ، ويُسن أن (يَرْمل في الثلاثة(۲) الأول منها، ويمشي فيما بقي على هيئته. * وسعى بعدها بين الصفا والمروة) وجوباً. (وهذه أفعال العمرة، ولا يحلق ؛ لأنه بقي عليه أفعال الحج، ولو حَلَق : لم يَحِلّ من عمرته، ولزمه دمان. (۱) أي نسخ القدوري. (۲) في بعض نسخ القدوري: «الثلاث».
Chapter of Qiran. [Qiran] is a verbal noun from the root qarana, form daraba and nasara. Linguistically: absolute joining of two things. Legally: combining the ihram of umrah and hajj in one journey. And it is, according to us, superior to tamattu' and ifrad, because it involves continuous ihram for both from the miqat until finishing them, and tamattu' is not like that, so qiran is preferable. Hidayah. Its description: that one enters ihram for umrah and hajj together from the miqat, literally or effectively by first entering ihram for umrah, then for hajj before performing most of the tawaf for it, because the combination has occurred, since most of the tawaf remains; similarly its opposite (1), but it is disliked. (1) i.e., by entering ihram for umrah onto hajj before performing tawaf al-qudum even if he has sinned, and upon him is a blood of thanksgiving, or after tawaf al-qudum even if a blood is required. See Ibn 'Abidin 7/174-175. Then: He says after the prayer: O Allah, I intend umrah and hajj, make them easy for me and accept them from me. When he enters Makkah, he begins by performing tawaf of the House, seven circuits; he walks briskly in the first three (of them), and walks normally in the rest. And after that he performs sa'i between Safa and Marwah. These are the acts of umrah. When he resolves to perform them, it is recommended for him to ask for ease, and he should mention umrah before hajj in that; therefore he says: (He says after the prayer: O Allah, I intend umrah and hajj...). In some copies it mentions hajj before umrah, but the first is better, and likewise he should give precedence to it in the talbiyah because he begins with the acts of umrah, so he should begin with its mention. Hidayah. When he enters Makkah, he begins with the acts of umrah, so he performs tawaf of the House seven circuits as an obligation, and the obligatory part of it is most of it, and it is recommended that he walks briskly in the first three of them, and walks normally in the rest. And after that he performs sa'i between Safa and Marwah as an obligation. These are the acts of umrah, and he does not shave his head because the acts of hajj remain upon him; if he shaves, he does not become free from his umrah and two bloods become due upon him. (1) i.e., the copies of Quduri. (2) In some copies of Quduri: 'the three'.
Source pages p. 445

Commentary
This passage from Al-Lubab is an expansion on the chapter of Qiran in Hajj. It begins by defining qiran linguistically and legally: the combination of umrah and hajj in one state of ihram. The author then states the Hanafi position that qiran is superior to tamattu' and ifrad, providing the rationale that continuous ihram from miqat until completion is maintained, unlike tamattu' which involves exiting ihram after umrah. He quotes from Al-Hidayah to support this. Next, the description of qiran is given: one must enter ihram for both together from the miqat, either literally or effectively by first doing umrah and then hajj before performing most of the tawaf of umrah. The opposite procedure—adding umrah onto hajj before tawaf al-qudum—is considered makruh (disliked). The footnote references Ibn Abidin for details. The text then moves to recommended actions: after the prayer, one should ask Allah to facilitate the umrah and hajj, saying a specific dua, and it is better to mention umrah before hajj. Upon entering Makkah, one begins with the acts of umrah: tawaf of seven circuits (walking briskly in the first three) and sa'i. These are obligatory. The passage concludes by noting that shaving (halaq) is not done after umrah in qiran, as the ihram continues for hajj; if one shaves, it does not release him from umrah and he must offer two dam (sacrificial penalties).

Key Terms
القران (al-qiran): Combining the ihram of umrah and hajj in one journey, entering ihram for both from the miqat.
الإهلال (al-ihlal): To raise the voice with talbiyah, meaning to enter the state of ihram.
الرمَل (al-ramal): Walking briskly with short steps while moving the shoulders, performed in the first three circuits of tawaf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which form of Hajj and Umrah combination is considered the most virtuous?
A) Tamattu'
B) Qiran
C) Ifrad
D) All are equal

Key Takeaway
Qiran is the most virtuous form of combining Hajj and Umrah because it maintains continuous ihram.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
10 min
Performing Qiran: Rituals and Rulings
Describes the practical steps of performing qiran.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the sequence of acts in qiran and identify the rulings (wajib, sunnah, makruh) for each step.

Core Idea
In qiran, begin with umrah acts; do not shave until hajj is complete.

After entering ihram for both umrah and hajj, the pilgrim proceeds to perform the acts of umrah first. This lesson details the recommended dua, the tawaf and sa'i, and the prohibition of shaving. Understanding the ruling of each act is crucial for the validity of the qiran.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the intention and dua
The pilgrim says after prayer a specific dua asking for ease and accepts, mentioning umrah before hajj.
2
Perform tawaf and sa'i for umrah
Upon entering Makkah, perform tawaf of seven circuits (obligatory) with ramal in the first three (sunnah), then sa'i (obligatory).
Most of the seven circuits of tawaf is fard; the full seven is wajib.
3
Note that shaving is not allowed
After umrah, the pilgrim does not shave because hajj acts remain. If he shaves, he does not exit ihram and two damm are due.

Source Text

فكان القران أولى منه. «هداية».

Hajj — Pilgrimage

Rulings of Qiran (Combined Hajj and Umrah)
Describes the actions of Qiran from intention to sacrifice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sequence of wajib and sunnah acts for a Qarin and identify the ruling on Dam al-Qiran.

Core Idea
A Qarin performs Umrah fully, stays in Ihram, and must sacrifice an animal.

This passage from al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Quduri details the rituals for someone performing Qiran—combining Hajj and Umrah with one Ihram. It explains the recommended du'a, the obligatory and recommended acts of Umrah upon entering Makkah, and the crucial rule that one does not exit Ihram after Umrah. The passage concludes with the obligation of Dam al-Qiran and its alternative fasting.

Guided Path
1
Identify the intention and its wording
The text prescribes a specific du'a after the obligatory prayer, mentioning Umrah before Hajj, and explains the wisdom of this order.
The recommendation is from the Hidayah.
2
Describe the Umrah acts for a Qarin
Upon entering Makkah, the Qarin performs tawaf of seven circuits (wajib) with raml in the first three (sunnah), then sa'i between Safa and Marwah (wajib). These are the acts of Umrah.
Raml is jogging with shoulder movement, specific to men.
3
Explain the prohibition of shaving and penalty
The Qarin does not shave after Umrah because he remains in Ihram for Hajj. If he shaves, he does not exit Ihram and owes two dam.
This highlights that Umrah alone does not complete Qiran.
4
Outline the Hajj acts after Umrah
After the Umrah sa'i, the Qarin performs Tawaf al-Qudum (sunnah) with raml in the first three, then sa'i for Hajj (wajib).
These are similar to the mufrid's actions.
5
State the ruling on Dam al-Qiran and its alternative
On the Day of Nahr, the Qarin must sacrifice a sheep, cow, or camel (or share). This is wajib. If unable, he must fast three days during Hajj, with the last day being Arafah. If he misses the fast, he must still sacrifice.
The sacrifice is a blood of thanks; he may eat from it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب القرآن
ويقول عقيب الصلاة : اللهم إني أريد العمرة والحج، فيسرهما لي، وتقبلهما مني . فإذا دخل مكة : ابتدأ فطاف بالبيت سبعة أشواط، يَرْمُلُ في الثلاثة الأول منها، ويمشي فيما بقي على هيئته . وسعى بعدها بين الصفا والمروة، وهذه أفعال العمرة. وإذا عَزَم على أدائهما يُسنُّ له سؤال التيسير فيهما، ويُقدم ذكر العمرة على الحج فيه ؛ ولذا قال : (ويقول عقيب الصلاة: اللـهـم إني أريد العمرة والحج، فيسرهما لي، وتقبلهما مني). وفي بعض النسخ): تقديم ذكـر الـحـج على العمرة، والأُولى: أولى، وكذلك يقدمها في التلبية ؛ لأنه يبدأ بأفعال العمرة، فكذلك يبدأ بذكرها. «هداية». فإذا دخل مكة: ابتدأ بأفعال العمرة ، فطاف بالبيت سبعة أشواط) وجوباً، والفرضُ منها أكثرها ، ويُسن أن (يَرْمل في الثلاثة الأول منها، ويمشي فيما بقي على هيئته. وسعى بعدها بين الصفا والمروة) وجوباً. (وهذه أفعال العمرة، ولا يحلق ؛ لأنه بقي عليه أفعال الحج، ولو حَلَق : لم يَحِلّ من عمرته، ولزمه دمان. ثم يطوف بعد السعي طواف القدوم، ويسعى بين الصفا والمروة للحج، كما بينا في حق المفرد. وإذا رمى الجمرة يوم النحر : ذَبَحَ شاةً، أو بقرة، أو بدنة، أو سبع بدنة، أو سبع بقرة، فهذا دم القرآن . فإن لم يكن له ما يذبحُ : صام ثلاثة أيام في الحج، آخرها يوم عرفة . فإن فاته الصوم حتى أتى يوم النحر : لم يُجْزِه إلا الدم . (ثم) يَشرَعُ بأفعال الحج كالمفرد : (يطوف بعد) فراغـه مـن (السعي) للعمرة (طواف القدوم)، ويَرمُل في الثلاثة الأول، (ويسعى بين الصفا والمروة للحج، كما بيّنا) ذلك (في حق المفرد) آنفاً. (وإذا رمى الجمرة الأولى (يوم النحر : ذبح) وجوباً (شاةً، أو بقرة، أو بدنةً ، أو سُبعَ بدنة ، أو سبع بقرة، فهذا دم القرآن)، وهو دم شكر، فيأكل منه. (فإن لم يكن له ما يذبح صام ثلاثة أيام في الحج)، ولـو متفرقة، (آخرها يوم عرفة. فإن فاته الصوم) : أي صوم الثلاثة الأيام في أيام الحج، (حتى أتى يوم النحر : لم يُجزه إلا الدم).
Chapter of Qiran. And he says after the prayer: 'O Allah, I intend Umrah and Hajj, so make them easy for me and accept them from me.' So when he enters Makkah, he begins and performs tawaf around the House seven circuits, jogging in the first three of them, and walking normally in the rest. And he performs sa'i after it between Safa and Marwah. These are the acts of Umrah. And when he resolves to perform both, it is recommended for him to ask for ease in them, and he should mention Umrah before Hajj in that; hence he said: 'And he says after the prayer: O Allah, I intend Umrah and Hajj, so make them easy for me and accept them from me.' In some copies, the mention of Hajj is before Umrah, but the first is better; and likewise he should give precedence to it in the talbiyah, because he begins with the acts of Umrah, so he begins with its mention. [From Hidayah]. So when he enters Makkah, he begins with the acts of Umrah. He performs tawaf around the House seven circuits obligatorily, and the majority of them are obligatory; and it is recommended that he jogs in the first three of them and walks normally in the rest. And he performs sa'i after it between Safa and Marwah obligatorily. These are the acts of Umrah. He does not shave his head because the acts of Hajj remain upon him. If he shaves, he does not become free from his Ihram, and two dam become obligatory upon him. Then after the sa'i he performs Tawaf al-Qudum, and he performs sa'i between Safa and Marwah for Hajj, as we explained regarding the ifrad. And when he throws the pebble on the Day of Nahr, he sacrifices a sheep, or a cow, or a camel, or a seventh of a camel, or a seventh of a cow. This is the blood of Qiran. If he does not have anything to sacrifice, he fasts three days during Hajj, the last of them being the Day of Arafah. If fasting is delayed until the Day of Nahr arrives, nothing suffices him except the blood. Then he proceeds with the acts of Hajj like the mufrid: he performs Tawaf al-Qudum after finishing the sa'i for Umrah, and he jogs in the first three, and performs sa'i between Safa and Marwah for Hajj, as we explained regarding the mufrid earlier. And when he throws the first pebble on the Day of Nahr, he sacrifices obligatorily a sheep, or a cow, or a camel, or a seventh of a camel, or a seventh of a cow. This is the blood of Qiran, and it is a blood of thanks, so he eats from it. If he does not have anything to sacrifice, he fasts three days during Hajj, even if scattered, the last of them being the Day of Arafah. If fasting is delayed until the Day of Nahr arrives, nothing suffices him except the blood.
Source pages p. 446

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement detailing the rituals of Qiran (combining Hajj and Umrah in one Ihram) according to the Hanafi school. The author begins with the recommended du'a after the obligatory prayer while still in the state of Ihram: asking Allah for ease and acceptance, mentioning Umrah before Hajj because the acts of Umrah come first. Upon entering Makkah, one must immediately begin the acts of Umrah: first the tawaful qudum (which for a Qarin is actually tawaful umrah), seven circuits obligatorily, with raml (jogging with short steps and shoulder movement) in the first three circuits as a sunnah, then walking normally for the remaining four. After tawaf, he performs sa'i between Safa and Marwah obligatorily. These constitute the Umrah. He does not shave or trim after Umrah because his Ihram continues for Hajj; if he does shave, he does not exit Ihram and must pay two dam (sacrificial animals) for violating the sanctity of Ihram. Then he performs another tawaf, Tawaf al-Qudum, which is a sunnah for the Hajj, followed by a second sa'i for Hajj. On the Day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah), after throwing the Jamrah al-Aqabah, he must sacrifice a sheep, cow, or camel (or share in one) as Dam al-Qiran, which is a wajib sacrifice of thanks; he may eat from it. If he cannot afford the animal, he must fast three days during the days of Hajj, the last being the Day of Arafah (9th Dhul Hijjah). If he fails to fast these three days before the Day of Nahr, then only a sacrifice suffices; no fasting after that day. This ruling reflects the Hanafi position that Dam al-Qiran is wajib, and its alternative is fasting within a specific time frame.

Key Terms
القرآن (al-Qiran): Combining Hajj and Umrah in one Ihram with a single intention and talbiyah.
الرمل (al-raml): Jogging with moderate speed, moving the shoulders, in the first three circuits of tawaf.
دم القرآن (dam al-Qiran): The obligatory sacrifice due upon a Qarin for combining Hajj and Umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling of raml (jogging) in tawaf for a Qarin?
A) Wajib in all seven circuits
B) Sunnah in the first three circuits
C) Sunnah in the last three circuits
D) Not recommended

Key Takeaway
A Qarin must complete Umrah acts without exiting Ihram and owes a wajib sacrifice or alternative fasting within specific times.

Sacrifice and Fasting Obligations for the Qarin
States the wajib sacrifice and alternative fasting for the Qarin

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the wajib acts upon the Qarin on the Day of Nahr and explain the substitute fasting rule, including its timing conditions.

Core Idea
If a Qarin cannot slaughter on the 10th, he must fast three days before Arafah; after that, only slaughter suffices.

In this passage from Al-Lubab, the commentator expands on Al-Quduri's matn clarifying two key obligations for the one performing Hajj Qiran: the wajib sacrifice after throwing the jamrah on Yawm al-Nahr, and the alternative of fasting three days during Hajj if one cannot afford an animal. The commentary emphasizes that the fasts need not be consecutive, but the last must be on the Day of Arafah, and missing the fast entirely means only the sacrifice will discharge the obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The Qarin must slaughter on the Day of Nahr after throwing the first jamrah. This is a wajib act (dam al-qiran). Note the range of acceptable animals: sheep, cow, camel, or a seventh share of a cow or camel.
The text uses 'ذبح' (slaughter) and specifies the animals.
2
Recognize the alternative for incapacity
If the Qarin cannot afford an animal, the obligation shifts to fasting three days during the Hajj period. The commentary explicitly permits these fasts to be non-consecutive.
The condition is financial inability (لم يكن له ما يذبح).
3
Note the timing condition
The last of the three fast days must be the Day of Arafah (9th Dhul-Hijjah). If the pilgrim delays and misses fasting until the Day of Nahr (10th), then fasting is no longer accepted; only slaughter remains valid.
The phrase 'آخرها يوم عرفة' and 'فإن فاته الصوم حتى أتى يوم النحر' are key.
4
Understand the nature of the sacrifice
Dam al-qiran is a sacrifice of thanks (شكر), from which the pilgrim may eat. It is distinct from other sacrificial blood (e.g., dam al-jabaran).
The commentary says 'وهو دم شكر، فيأكل منه.'

And when he throws the jamrah on the Day of Nahr, he slaughters a sheep, or a cow, or a camel, or a seventh of a camel, or a seventh of a cow; this is the blood of Qiran. Commentary
This passage from Bab al-Qiran of Al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Quduri explains the obligations specific to the Qarin (one performing Hajj Qiran). After completing the Umrah sa'i, the Qarin performs tawaf al-qudum (the arrival tawaf) with raml in the first three circuits, and then performs the Hajj sa'i between Safa and Marwah. On the Day of Nahr (10th Dhul-Hijjah), after throwing the first jamrah, he must slaughter an animal: a sheep, cow, or camel, or a seventh share of a camel or cow. This is called 'dam al-qiran' (blood of Qiran) and is a sacrifice of thanks (shukr), from which he may eat. If he cannot afford an animal, he fasts three days during the Hajj period, the last being the Day of Arafah. The fasts may be separated (not necessarily consecutive). If he delays and the Day of Nahr passes without fasting, then fasting is no longer sufficient; he must slaughter. The footnote clarifies the lexical range of badanah: some include both camels and cows, but the preferred Hanafi view allows either.

Key Terms
قارن (qārin): One who performs Hajj Qiran, intending Umrah and Hajj together in one state of ihram.
دم القرآن (dam al-qirān): The blood sacrifice incumbent upon the Qarin as a wajib act.
بدنة (badanah): A camel or cow, according to the preferred view; some include both, some restrict to camel.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Slaughter the animal.
C) Fast three days after Hajj.
D) Do nothing; obligation drops.

Key Takeaway
The Qarin's wajib sacrifice (dam al-qiran) can be replaced by fasting three days if unable, but only if the fast is completed before the Day of Nahr.

Timing of the Seven-Day Fast for the Qarin
Clarifies when the seven-day fast may be completed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two permissible timings for the seven-day fast for the Qarin and apply the Hanafi dispensation for fasting in Makkah.

Core Idea
The seven-day fast may be completed after returning home or in Makkah after finishing Hajj.

This lesson continues the obligations of the Qarin who chooses fasting over slaughter. After the three days fasted during Hajj, seven additional days are required. The default instruction is to fast upon returning to one's family, but the text clarifies that 'returning' means completion of Hajj, allowing the fast to be performed in Makkah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the obligation
The Qarin who substitutes fasting for slaughter must fast seven days after the three days of Hajj.
This complements the previous lesson on the three-day fast.
2
State the default timing
The text says 'then he fasts seven days when he returns to his family.'
This is the primary ruling.
3
Note the dispensation
If he fasts them in Makkah after finishing the actions of Hajj, it is permissible.
This shows flexibility.
4
Understand the legal reasoning
The commentary explains that 'returning' is interpreted as finishing Hajj rituals, not physical return. Thus, fasting in Makkah after completion is valid.
This is an example of ta'wil (interpretation).
5
Apply the ruling
The mufta bihi position is that fasting in Makkah after Hajj is allowed.
The student should be able to advise pilgrims accordingly.

Therefore, fasting these seven days in Makkah after concluding the Hajj rituals is valid and fulfills the obligation.

Qarin Bypassing Makkah: Consequences and Rulings
States the consequence when a Qarin bypasses Makkah and goes to Arafat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a Qarin proceeds directly to Arafat without entering Makkah, identify the moment he becomes rafid, and calculate the required blood sacrifices.

Core Idea
A Qarin who skips Makkah and stands at Arafat becomes a rafid, voiding dam al-qiran and triggering dam al-rafd.

This lesson examines an exceptional scenario in Hajj: a pilgrim who enters ihram with the intention of Qiran (combining Umrah and Hajj) but proceeds directly to Arafat without first entering Makkah and performing Umrah. The Hanafi school rules that such an action invalidates the Umrah, substituting one obligation (dam al-qiran) for another (dam al-rafd). We will trace the legal reasoning and explore what happens if the pilgrim is unable to sacrifice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the subject
The act is a Qarin (one who intends Qiran) not entering Makkah and heading to Arafat. Determine what he does and its sequence.
The Qarin must originally perform Umrah first, then Hajj. Skipping Makkah breaks this order.
2
Determine the legal consequence (rafd)
When does he become a rafid (abandoner) of his Umrah? The text specifies it occurs by standing at Arafat (wuquf), not by mere intention or heading out.
The correct view is that wuquf is the operative event; mere niyyah is insufficient.
3
Analyse the change in obligations
Because the Umrah is abandoned, the original dam al-qiran (owed for combining) is voided. Instead, he must offer dam al-rafd (blood sacrifice for abandoning the Umrah).
This is a substitution: one wajib replaces another.
4
Consider the case of incapacity
If he cannot offer the sacrifice, he may perform tahallul (remove ihram) before slaughtering. Then two dams become wajib: one for the original Qiran and one for tahallul before the sacrifice.
The second dam is called dam al-tahallul, for the premature exit from ihram.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن لم يدخل القارنُ مكة، وتوجه إلى عرفات : فقد صار رافضاً لعمرته بالوقوف، وبطل عنه دم القرآن، وعليه دم لرفض عمرته ، ... 
فلو لم يقدر تحلَّل، وعليه دمان دم القرآن، ودم التحلل قبل الذبح .
(وإن لم يدخل القارنُ مكةَ، وتوجه إلى عرفات، ووقف بها في وقته، وإلا : فلا عبرة به: (فقد صار رافضاً لعمرته بالوقوف)؛ لأنه تعذر عليه أداؤها ؛ لأنه يصير بانياً أفعال العمرة على أفعال الحج وذلك خلاف المشروع، ولا يصير رافضاً بمجرد التوجه(۱)، وهو الصحيح. «هداية».

Commentary
This passage addresses an exceptional case for the Qarin. If the Qarin enters ihram with the intention of Qiran but proceeds directly to Arafat without entering Makkah, his Umrah becomes invalid because he cannot properly perform its actions later. The moment he stands at Arafat, he becomes 'rafid' (abandoner) of his Umrah. Consequently, the original obligation of dam al-qiran falls away (since he is no longer doing both rites together), and instead he must offer a blood sacrifice for abandoning the Umrah (dam al-rafd). If he cannot afford it, he may perform tahallul (remove ihram) before sacrificing, but he then owes two dams: one for the original Qiran (since the obligation originally existed) and one for tahallul before the sacrifice. The sharh clarifies that merely setting out (tawajjuh) without actual standing at Arafat does not constitute rafd; the key action is the wuquf itself. The correct view is as stated in al-Hidayah.

Key Terms
رافض (rāfiḍ): One who abandons his Umrah by proceeding to Arafat without completing Umrah first.
دم التحلل (dam al-taḥallul): Blood sacrifice for removing ihram before completing the rites (usually due to inability).
دم الرفض (dam al-rafḍ): Blood sacrifice for abandoning the Umrah, owed by the Qarin who invalidates his Umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Fast three days instead.
C) Remove ihram and then offer two blood sacrifices.
D) Perform tawaf al-qudum later.

Key Takeaway
A Qarin who bypasses Makkah and stands at Arafat becomes rafid, voiding dam al-qiran and obligating dam al-rafd; if unable to sacrifice, tahallul followed by two dams is required.

Rulings for the Qarin Who Neglects the 'Umrah
Ruling statement on consequences for qarin who neglects 'umrah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the obligations on a qarin who fails to perform 'umrah before standing at 'Arafat and identify the difference between mere intention and actual neglect.

Core Idea
The qarin who stands at 'Arafat before 'umrah loses the Qiran dam but must sacrifice a dam and make up the 'umrah.

In Hanafi fiqh, the qarin (one performing Hajj Qiran) must perform 'umrah before proceeding to Hajj rituals. If he fails to do so and stands at 'Arafat, he becomes neglectful of his 'umrah. This lesson explains the consequences: the original Qiran dam is waived, but he must offer a new dam and later perform a make-up 'umrah. We also clarify that neglect is triggered only by actual standing, not mere intention.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The qarin does not enter Makkah and proceeds to 'Arafat, then stands there at its time.
2
Determine the ruling on the Qiran dam
The dam of Qiran is nullified (falls from him) because he did not complete both rites.
3
Identify the new obligations
He must offer a dam for neglecting his 'umrah and must later make up that 'umrah.
4
Note the exception for inability
If he cannot afford the dam, he may perform tahlul (exit ihram) and then owes two dams: one for Qiran and one for tahlul.
5
Recognize the intra-madhhab distinction
Neglect occurs only by actual standing at 'Arafat, not by mere intention or direction of travel. This is the correct view per al-Hidayah.

Source pages p. 448

Commentary
This passage from the sharh of al-Quduri discusses the rulings for a qarin (one performing Hajj Qiran) who fails to perform the 'umrah part of the Qiran. The author first states the ruling for fasting: the qarin who cannot afford a sacrificial animal must fast three days during Hajj and seven days after returning home. However, these seven days may be fasted in Makkah after completing Hajj, as 'returning to his family' is interpreted as finishing the Hajj rituals.

Then the passage addresses the situation where a qarin enters ihram for Qiran but does not enter Makkah before proceeding to 'Arafat. By standing at 'Arafat, he is considered to have neglected his 'umrah intentionally? Actually, it says he becomes 'raafidan' (neglectful) of his 'umrah because he cannot perform it after starting Hajj rituals. The ruling: the dam originally required for Qiran (دم القرآن) drops from him, but he must offer a dam for neglecting the 'umrah (دم لرفض عمرته). If he cannot afford the sacrifice, he may perform tahlul (exit ihram) and then owes two dams: one for the Qiran and one for the early tahlul.

The commentary clarifies that merely intending to proceed to 'Arafat does not constitute neglect; actual standing at 'Arafat is required. This is the correct position according to al-Hidayah. Furthermore, since he started the 'umrah by entering ihram, it becomes obligatory upon him, and since he did not complete it, he must make it up (qada') with a separate 'umrah.

Thus, the qarin in this situation has three obligations: (1) a dam for neglecting the 'umrah, (2) make-up of the 'umrah, and (3) if he performed tahlul before sacrificing, an additional dam for that. The original Qiran dam is waived.

Key Terms
قارن (qārin): One who performs Hajj Qiran, entering ihram for both 'umrah and Hajj together.
رفض العمرة (rafḍ al-ʿumrah): Neglecting or leaving the 'umrah after having entered ihram for it, here due to proceeding to 'Arafat without performing it.
دم القرآن (dam al-qirān): The sacrificial animal required of the qarin for performing Qiran, normally a sheep or seventh of a camel/cow.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a qarin proceeds to 'Arafat without entering Makkah first and stands at 'Arafat, what happens to his obligation of the dam for Qiran (دم القرآن)?
A) It remains obligatory.
B) It is waived, but he must offer a dam for neglecting his 'umrah.
C) He must offer two dams: one for Qiran and one for neglect.
D) He must fast instead of sacrificing.

Key Takeaway
The qarin who stands at 'Arafat before 'umrah must offer a dam for neglect and make up the 'umrah, while the Qiran dam is nullified.

Rulings on the Compensatory Blood and Make-Up of Qiran
Ruling on compensatory blood and make-up obligation for Qiran

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two rulings regarding the compensatory blood and make-up in Qiran, and explain the reasoning provided.

Core Idea
The compensatory blood (dam jabr) in Qiran may not be eaten, and if the Hajj is missed, make-up becomes wajib.

This passage from al-Lubab presents two crucial rulings for the one who performs Qiran (combining Hajj and Umrah). First, the animal slaughtered as compensatory blood (dam jabr) for a deficiency may not be consumed by the pilgrim. Second, if the Qiran Hajj is not completed, the pilgrim must make it up. The reasoning is that entering Ihram for Qiran makes the Hajj obligatory upon oneself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings stated
Read the passage and pinpoint the two distinct legal rulings: one about the slaughter (dam jabr) and one about make-up (qada).
The passage uses 'la yajuz' for the first and 'wajaba' for the second.
2
Understand the prohibition on eating dam jabr
The text explicitly states that it is not permissible to eat from this sacrificial blood. This is a specific prohibition for compensatory blood.
Contrast with voluntary sacrifices (dam tatabbu') which may be eaten.
3
Recognize the obligation of qada
If the Qiran Hajj is not performed (e.g., due to invalidation of Ihram), the pilgrim must make it up (qada). This is an obligation.
Qada applies to the entire Qiran, not just parts.
4
Trace the reasoning
The passage gives the cause: 'by starting it he made it obligatory upon himself'. Entering Ihram for Qiran creates a binding obligation to complete the Hajj and Umrah. Since he did not fulfill it, make-up becomes necessary.
This is a concise logical deduction (ta'lil) typical of Hanafi matn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهو دم جبرٍ، لا يجوز أكله منه، (و) وَجَبَ (عليه قضاؤها)؛ لأنه بشروعه فيها: أوجبها على نفسه، ولم يوجد منه الأداء؛ فلزمه القضاء.
And it is a compensatory blood, it is not permissible to eat from it, and it is obligatory upon him to make it up because by starting it he made it obligatory upon himself, and no performance came from him, so the make-up is necessary.
Source pages p. 449

Commentary
This passage states a ruling from the chapter on Qiran (combining Hajj and Umrah). The 'it' refers to the Hajj that was started as Qiran. The blood mentioned is the compensatory slaughter (dam jabr) required due to a deficiency in the ritual. It is not permissible to eat from this blood. Additionally, if the person began the Qiran but did not complete its actions (e.g., due to invalidating the Ihram), he must make up that Hajj. The reasoning: by entering Ihram for Qiran, he obliged himself to perform the Hajj; since he did not fulfill that obligation, make-up (qada) becomes binding. This is a concise ruling without explicit proof, typical of a matn text.

Key Terms
دم جبر (dam jabr): Compensatory blood; a sacrificial animal required to compensate for a deficiency or violation in Hajj.

Key Takeaway
The compensatory blood (dam jabr) may not be consumed, and if the Qiran Hajj is missed, make-up (qada) is obligatory.
