Tamattu': Definition and Superiority over Ifrad
Definition of Tamattu' and its superiority over Ifrad with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of tamattu', explain the proof for its superiority over ifrad, and identify the distinction between mutamatti' with and without hadi.

Core Idea
Tamattu' combines Umrah and Hajj with an extra sacrifice, making it better than Ifrad in the Hanafi school.

This passage from the chapter on Tamattu' begins by explaining its connection to the prior chapter on Qiran. It then provides a precise legal definition of tamattu' and establishes that it is superior to Ifrad in the Hanafi school, based on analogy to Qiran and the added virtue of sacrifice. The passage also hints at two categories of mutamatti' that affect the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Define tamattu' legally
Identify the key elements: combining Umrah and Hajj in the months of Hajj, performing most acts of each, and avoiding sexual intercourse between the two ihrams.
The definition is from al-Jawharah.
2
Identify the ruling and its proof
The passage states that tamattu' is better (afdal) than ifrad. The proof is qiyas to Qiran (which combines both rites) and the additional act of sacrifice.
The proof is from al-Hidayah.
3
Examine the analogy (qiyas)
Break down the qiyas: asl = Qiran (known virtue), far' = Tamattu', illa = combination of two acts of worship, hukm = superiority.
This is a qiyas jaliy because the illa is clear.
4
Recognize the two types of mutamatti'
The passage prefigures that mutamatti' who drives a hadi and one who does not have different rulings, to be explained later.
This shows the passage is part of a larger discussion.

Chapter of Tamattu'. Its relevance to Qiran: that in each of them there is a combination of the two rites, and Qiran is given precedence due to its greater virtue. (from Nahr). Tamattu' linguistically: benefiting; legally: combining the ihram of Umrah and its actions, or most of them, and the ihram of Hajj and its actions, in the months of Hajj, without a valid sexual encounter with one's spouse. (from Jawharah). * And it is better than Ifrad in our school, because in it there is a combination of two acts of worship, so it resembles Qiran, and then there is an additional act of worship, which is shedding blood (slaughtering). Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on Tamattu'. First, it explains the connection to the previous chapter on Qiran: both involve combining two rites, but Qiran is placed first due to its greater virtue. Then it gives definitions: linguistically, tamattu' means benefiting; legally, it means the pilgrim enters ihram for Umrah during the months of Hajj, performs most of its actions, then enters ihram for Hajj in the same year, without having had a valid sexual encounter with his spouse in between. Finally, it prefigures that there are two types of Mutamatti': one who brings a sacrificial animal (Hadi) and one who does not, and their rulings differ, to be explained later.

Key Terms
تمتع (tamattu'): Legally: combining the ihram of Umrah and its actions, or most of them, with the ihram of Hajj and its actions, in the months of Hajj, without a valid sexual encounter with one's spouse.
إفراد (ifrad): Performing Hajj alone, without Umrah, in the state of ihram.
هدي (hadi): A sacrificial animal (usually a sheep, goat, or cow) brought by a Mutamatti' or Qarin to be slaughtered.

The Hanafi Preference for Tamattu' and Its Description
States Hanafi preference and describes tamattu' without hady

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position that tamattu' is superior to ifrad, identify the proof given, and describe the actions of a mutamatti' who does not bring a sacrificial animal.

Core Idea
Tamattu' combines two worships and includes an extra sacrifice, making it superior to ifrad.

This passage opens the chapter on tamattu' by asserting its superiority over ifrad. The author provides a logical proof: tamattu' resembles qiran and adds the ritual of sacrifice. The text also distinguishes two types of mutamatti' and details the steps for the one who does not drive a sacrificial animal, offering a clear sequence for practice.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi Ruling
Identify the exact ruling: tamattu' is afdal (better) than ifrad according to the Hanafi school.
The ruling is a preference, not an obligation.
2
Extract the Proof
Find the justification: it combines two acts of worship (resembling qiran) and includes an additional sacrifice (dam).
This is a rational proof (qiyas/talil).
3
Distinguish the Two Types
Note that mutamatti' is divided into one who drives hady and one who does not, with different rulings.
The description focuses on the second type.
4
List the Sequence for the Mutamatti' without Hady
Outline the steps: enter ihram from miqat for Umrah, perform tawaf and sa'y, shave or trim, become halal, and wait until the day of Tarwiyah.
He does not perform tawaf al-qudum because he can do the obligatory tawaf immediately.

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on Tamattu' begins by stating the Hanafi ruling that tamattu' (performing Umrah first and then Hajj within the same journey with a break) is superior to ifrad (performing Hajj alone or Umrah alone). The proof given is that tamattu' combines two acts of worship, resembling Qiran, and additionally involves an extra sacrifice (dam). The text then clarifies that tamattu' is of two types: one where the pilgrim drives a sacrificial animal (hady) with him, and one where he does not, with different rulings. The definition of tamattu' is given: linguistically 'benefiting', and legally: combining the ihram of Umrah and most of its actions with the ihram of Hajj during the Hajj months without returning home. The author then describes the actions of a mutamatti' who does not bring hady: he enters ihram from the miqat for Umrah, performs tawaf and sa'y, shaves or trims, and becomes halal. He stops talbiyah when beginning tawaf. He stays in Makkah in a non-muhrim state until the day of Tarwiyah (8th Dhul Hijjah). Notably, he does not perform a tawaf of arrival (tawaf al-qudum) because he is able to perform the obligatory tawaf (of Umrah) immediately. The text contrasts this with Hajj where upon arrival one cannot yet perform the Hajj tawaf, so one performs the sunnah greeting tawaf.

Key Terms
التمتع (al-tamattu'): Combining Umrah and Hajj in one journey with a break, entering ihram for Umrah first, completing it, then entering ihram for Hajj later.
الإفراد (al-ifrad): Performing Hajj without Umrah in the same journey, or performing Umrah alone.
الهدي (al-hady): A sacrificial animal (camel, cow, sheep, or goat) brought by the mutamatti' and qarin as an obligatory sacrifice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Procedure and Obligations of Tamattu' Hajj
Defines tamattu' and outlines its rituals and obligatory blood

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the step-by-step procedure of tamattu' and identify the conditions and wajibat (including dam) that distinguish it from ifrad.

Core Idea
Tamattu': combine 'Umrah and Hajj in one journey, with a thank offering (dam) as wajib.

Tamattu' is one of the three ways to perform Hajj. This passage from Al-Lubab details its exact procedure: you begin with 'Umrah from the miqat, exit ihram, and then re-enter for Hajj from the Haram on the Day of Tarwiyah. The text also explains when ramal and sa'y are required and when they are not, and it establishes the obligation of a sacrificial animal or fasting as compensation. Understanding these details helps you distinguish tamattu' from ifrad and qiran.

Guided Path
1
1. Trace the ihram sequence
Identify the two separate ihrams: first for 'Umrah from the miqat, then for Hajj from the Haram on Yawm al-Tarwiyah. Note that the pilgrim becomes halal after 'Umrah.
The condition for the second ihram is that it must be inside the Haram.
2
2. Spot the special tawaf/sa'y rule
The mutamatti' must perform ramal and sa'y with tawaf al-ziyarah because it is his first tawaf in Hajj. However, if he already did tawaf and sa'y before going to Mina, he omits them later.
This differs from the mufrid who already performed sa'y once.
3
3. Identify the wajib: dam al-tamattu'
The text states that dam (sacrificial blood) is obligatory as a thank offering. If unable, fasting is substituted: three days during Hajj and seven after returning home.
The dam is wajib, not fard – omission requires compensation but does not invalidate Hajj.
4
4. Apply the conditions and pillars
List the necessary conditions (e.g., ihram from miqat for 'Umrah, then from Haram for Hajj) and the standard pillars of Hajj. Note which elements are sunnah (e.g., assuming ihram for Hajj from the mosque).
Refer to the conditions/pillars block below for a complete breakdown.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب التمتع
وصفة التَّمتُّع: أن يبتدئ من الميقات، فيُحرم بعمرة، ويدخل مكة، فيطوف لها، ويسعى ويحلق أو يقصر، وقد حَلَّ من عمرته.
ويقطع التلبية إذا ابتدأ بالطواف، ويقيم بمكة حلالاً.
فإذا كان يوم التروية - وقد روى أن الأفضل أن يحرم بالحج من المسجد -: أحرم بالحج من المسجد ندباً، والشرط: أن يُحرم من الحرم؛ لأنه في معنى المكي وميقاتُ المكي في الحج: الحرم، كما تقدم، وفَعَلَ ما يفعله الحاج المفرد؛ لأنه مؤد للحج، إلا أنه يرمل في طواف الزيارة، ويسعى بعده؛ لأن هذا أول طواف له في الحج، بخلاف المفرد؛ لأنه قد سعى مرة.
ولو كان هذا المتمتع بعد ما أحرم بالحج، طاف وسعى قبل أن يروح إلى منى: لم يرمل في طواف الزيارة، ولا يسعى بعده؛ لأنه قد أتى بذلك مرةً.
ووجب عليه دم التمتع، وهو دم شكر، فيأكل منه. فإن لم يجد الدم: صام ثلاثة أيام في الحج، وسبعة إذا رجع إلى أهله.
Chapter of Tamattu'. Description of Tamattu': He begins from the miqat, assumes ihram with 'Umrah, enters Makkah, performs tawaf for it, and sa'y, and shaves or shortens, and has exited from his 'Umrah. He cuts off the talbiyah when he begins tawaf, and stays in Makkah in a non-ihram state. Then on the Day of Tarwiyah - and it has been reported that the best is to assume ihram for Hajj from the mosque -: he assumes ihram for Hajj from the mosque as a recommendation, and the condition is that he assume ihram from the Haram; because he is like a Makkan, and the miqat of a Makkan for Hajj is the Haram, as has preceded, and he does what the individual pilgrim (mufrid) does; because he is performing Hajj, except that he does ramal in the tawaf of ziyarah, and performs sa'y after it; because this is his first tawaf in Hajj, unlike the mufrid because he has already performed sa'y once. And if this mutamatti' after he has assumed ihram for Hajj, performed tawaf and sa'y before going to Mina, he does not do ramal in tawaf of ziyarah, nor does he perform sa'y after it; because he has already done that once. And he is obligated (to offer) the blood (dam) of tamattu', which is a blood of thanksgiving, so he eats from it. And if he does not find the blood: he fasts three days in Hajj and seven when he returns to his family.
Source pages p. 451

Commentary
This passage from Al-Lubab explains the procedure for tamattu' in Hajj. It begins with the pilgrim assuming ihram for 'Umrah from the miqat, performing tawaf, sa'y, and shaving or shortening, thereby completing the 'Umrah. He then stays in Makkah in a non-ihram state until the Day of Tarwiyah, when he assumes ihram for Hajj from the Haram (preferably from the mosque). The text notes that the mutamatti' performs ramal and sa'y during the tawaf of ziyarah, as this is his first tawaf in Hajj, unlike a mufrid who already did sa'y. However, if he performed tawaf and sa'y before proceeding to Mina on the Day of Tarwiyah, he omits them later. Finally, a sacrificial animal (dam) is obligatory as a thank offering, and if he cannot afford it, he must fast three days during Hajj and seven after returning home.

Key Terms
التمتع (al-tamattu'): A type of Hajj where one first performs 'Umrah, then exits ihram, then re-enters ihram for Hajj from the Haram on the Day of Tarwiyah.
دم التمتع (dam al-tamattu'): A sacrificial animal (usually a sheep or goat) required from a mutamatti' as a thank offering for combining 'Umrah and Hajj in one journey.
يوم التروية (yawm al-tarwiyah): The 8th day of Dhul-Hijjah, when pilgrims proceed to Mina and assume ihram for Hajj if not already.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the obligation upon a mutamatti' who cannot find or afford a sacrificial animal (dam)?
A) He must perform an additional 'Umrah.
B) He fasts three days during Hajj and seven after returning home.
C) He must give charity equivalent to the value of the animal.
D) He may skip the dam and the Hajj remains valid.

Key Takeaway
In tamattu', the pilgrim performs 'Umrah first, then Hajj from the Haram, and must offer a dam (or fast) as wajib; the rules for ramal and sa'y depend on timing.

The Mutamatti's Hajj: Ramal and Sa'y in Tawaf al-Ziyarah
Explains Mutamatti's Hajj actions with proof and exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on when the Mutamatti' performs ramal and sa'y and identify the exception when he does not.

Core Idea
The Mutamatti' performs ramal and sa'y in Tawaf al-Ziyarah because it is his first Hajj tawaf; if already done, he does not repeat.

This lesson examines the specific actions of the Mutamatti' pilgrim during Hajj. While the Mutamatti' generally follows the Mufrid, a key difference arises in Tawaf al-Ziyarah: he must perform ramal and sa'y. This ruling is based on qiyas (analogy) and has a clear exception. Understanding this helps avoid common mistakes in Hajj practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The Mutamatti' enters ihram from the mosque (recommended) within the Haram. He does what the Mufrid does, except he performs ramal and sa'y in Tawaf al-Ziyarah. The ruling is sunnah (recommended).
The condition is that ihram must be from within the Haram, as the miqat for a Meccan is the Haram.
2
Understand the dalil (proof)
The proof is qiyas: the Mutamatti' is like the Mufrid in performing Hajj, but his first tawaf in Hajj is Tawaf al-Ziyarah, so he performs ramal and sa'y then. The Mufrid does not repeat because he already performed them in Tawaf al-Qudum.
This is a talil (reasoning) from the text.
3
Apply the exception
If the Mutamatti' performed tawaf and sa'y before going to Mina (e.g., on the 8th of Dhul-Hijjah), then he does not repeat ramal and sa'y in Tawaf al-Ziyarah. The action has already been done for Hajj.
The text from al-Hidayah clarifies this exception.
4
Compare with other schools
The Shafi'i school holds that the Mutamatti' does not perform a separate sa'y for Hajj because the 'Umrah sa'y suffices. The Hanafi response is that the two sa'y are separate acts.
This ikhtilaf is reflected in the Hanafi insistence on the second sa'y.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أحرم بالحج من المسجد ندباً، والشرط: أن يُحرم من الحرم؛ لأنه في معنى المكي وميقاتُ المكي في الحج: الحرم، كما تقدم، وفَعَلَ ما يفعله الحاج المفرد)؛ لأنه مؤد للحج، إلا أنه يرمل في طواف الزيارة، ويسعى بعده؛ لأن هذا أول طواف له في الحج، بخلاف المفرد ؛ لأنه قد سعى مرة. ولو كان هذا المتمتع بعد ما أحرم بالحج، طاف وسعى قبل أن يروح إلى منى: لم يرمل في طواف الزيارة، ولا يسعى بعده؛ لأنه قد أتى بذلك مرةً. «هداية». (1) راح، يروح، بعض الناس أن «الرَّواح» لا يكون إلا في آخر النهار وليس كذلك، بل «الرواح»، و«الغدو» عند العرب يُستعملان في المسير أي وقت كان، من ليل أو نهار، قاله الأزهري، وغيره. اهـ من المصباح المنير (روح). رواحاً يكون بمعنى الغُدُوِّ، وبمعنى الرجوع، وقد يتوهم [؟]
He enters ihram for Hajj from the mosque as a recommendation, and the condition is that he should enter ihram from the Haram because he is like the Meccan and the miqat of the Meccan for Hajj is the Haram, as previously stated, and he does what the Hajj Mufrid does because he is performing Hajj, except that he performs ramal in Tawaf al-Ziyarah and performs sa'y after it because this is his first tawaf in Hajj, unlike the Mufrid because he has already done sa'y once. And if this Mutamatti', after he had entered ihram for Hajj, performed tawaf and sa'y before going to Mina, then he does not perform ramal in Tawaf al-Ziyarah and does not perform sa'y after it because he has already done that once. (From al-Hidayah). (1) Rāḥa, yarūḥu; some people think that 'al-rawāḥ' is only at the end of the day, but it is not so; rather, 'al-rawāḥ' and 'al-ghudū' among the Arabs are used for traveling at any time, night or day, said by al-Azhari and others. End from al-Miṣbāḥ al-Munīr (r-w-ḥ). Rawāḥ is used in the sense of ghudūw (going in the morning) and in the sense of returning, and it may be misunderstood [؟]
Source pages p. 452

Commentary
This is a ruling-with-proof passage from the commentary (sharḥ) of al-Qudūrī's Mukhtaṣar. It explains the actions of the Mutamatti' (one performing Tamattu' Hajj) upon entering ihram for Hajj. The author states that it is recommended (nadban) to enter ihram from the mosque within the Haram, as the Miqat for a Meccan is the Haram itself. The Mutamatti' then does everything the Mufrid (one performing Ifrad) does, except that he performs ramal (quick walking with shoulders swaying) in Tawaf al-Ziyarah and sa'y (the running between Safa and Marwa) after it. The reason is that this is his first tawaf for Hajj—the 'Umrah tawaf does not count for Hajj—unlike the Mufrid who has already done sa'y once. The passage then gives an exception: if the Mutamatti', after entering ihram for Hajj, had already performed tawaf and sa'y before going to Mina (i.e., during the days of staying at Mina), then he does not repeat ramal and sa'y because he has already done them. This is cited from al-Hidayah. A linguistic note follows explaining the word 'rawāḥ' (going) used in the exception; it means departure at any time, not just evening, and can also mean return.

Key Terms
متمتع (mutamatti'): One who performs Tamattu' Hajj, i.e., performs 'Umrah first, then after a break performs Hajj in the same year.
رمل (ramal): Quick walking with shoulders swaying in tawaf; a sunnah act for men.
طواف الزيارة (tawaf al-ziyarah): The obligatory tawaf of Hajj, performed on the 10th of Dhul-Hijjah or the days of Tashriq.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does the Mutamatti' perform ramal and sa'y in Hajj according to the Hanafi school?
A) In Tawaf al-Qudum (arrival tawaf)
B) In Tawaf al-Ziyarah and sa'y after it
C) In all circuit tawafs
D) Only in the 'Umrah tawaf

Key Takeaway
The Mutamatti' must perform ramal and sa'y in Tawaf al-Ziyarah; this is his first Hajj tawaf, unless he already performed tawaf and sa'y before Mina.

Ish'ar for the Mutamatti's Hady: Abu Hanifa vs. the Sahibayn
Presents the ruling on marking the hady and the dispute on ish'ar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on marking the hady, explain the intra-madhhab dispute on ish'ar between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Ish'ar is allowed by the Sahibayn but not by Abu Hanifa; later mufta bihi permits it.

When a Mutamatti' drives a sacrificial animal (hady) with him, it is considered more virtuous. The animal is marked to identify it as a sacrificial offering. The classical Hanafi text discusses two methods: taqlid (garlanding) and ish'ar (marking by wound). This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa opposed ish'ar for the camel, while his two main disciples permitted it. Understanding how the school resolved this disagreement gives insight into the Hanafi methodology of tarjih (weighing evidence).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act described? Driving a hady for tamattu'. What is its ruling? It is mustahabb (sunnah). Marking the animal is part of this sunnah.
The ruling level is sunnah, not wajib.
2
Distinguish the two marking methods
What are taqlid and ish'ar? Taqlid: hanging a piece of leather or a sandal around the neck. Ish'ar: making a slight cut on the hump or side to leave a scar.
Taqlid is agreed upon; ish'ar is the point of dispute.
3
State the positions of the Hanafi imams
Abu Hanifa does not allow ish'ar, considering it mutilation. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani allow it, based on the Prophet's practice.
The text explicitly says 'عند أبي يوسف ومحمد'.
4
Identify the evidence for each position
The Sahibayn rely on authentic ahadith that the Prophet performed ish'ar on his sacrificial camel. Abu Hanifa relies on the general prohibition of mutilation and striking the face.
The commentary does not quote the hadith but references it.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and the tarjih
Later Hanafi authorities (al-Jawharah, al-Mughrib) preferred the Sahibayn's view, making ish'ar permissible. This is the operative position for fatwa.
The tarjih is based on the strength of the hadith evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن أراد المتمتع أن يسوق الهدي) معه، وهو أفضل: (أحرم، وساق هديه، فإن كانت بَدَنَةً)، وهي من الإبل خاصة، وتقع على الذكر والأنثى، والجمع : البدن. (مغرب): (قلدها (1) بمَزادة) - بالفتح : الراوية (2) - ، والمراد : أن يُعلّق في عنقها قطعة من أدم من مزادة، أو غيرها، أو نعل)، وهو أولى من التجليل (3). وأشعر البدنة عند أبي يوسف ومحمد، وهو) أي الإشعار: (1) وفي الجوهرة 203/1 التقليد إنما يكون فيما يغيب عن صاحبه، كالإبل والبقر خاصة، أما الغنم فلا يقلد ، لأنه يضيع إذا لم يكن معه صاحبه». (2) وهي ما يوضع فيها الماء عند السقيا، وتكون من ثلاثة جلود. المغرب 354/1) (روي) ، المعجم الوسيط (روي). كما تطلق الراوية على البعير الذي يستقى عليه. (3) جل الدابة : ما تغطى به من الجلد ونحوه ، لتُصان به، والتجليل: إلباسها جلَّها. القاموس المحيط (جلل)، المعجم الوسيط (جلل). والتقليد أولى من التجليل، لأنه ذُكر في القرآن الكريم : ﴿وَالْهُدَى وَالْقَلَمدَ﴾ المائدة/97 ، وهو مقصود للإعلام بأنها نسك للحرم. ينظر الجوهرة 203/1.
And if the Mutamatti' intends to drive the hady with him, it is more virtuous: he enters ihram and drives his hady. If it is a badanah (a camel), specifically from camels, applying to both male and female, plural: budun. (al-Mughrib): He garlands it with a mizādah (a waterskin) — with fath (on the mīm) meaning the water-carrying vessel — and the intent is to hang on its neck a piece of leather from a mizādah or other, or a sandal (na'l), and that is better than covering (tajlīl). And ish'ar (marking by wound) of the badanah is according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, and it (i.e., ish'ar) is: (1) In al-Jawharah 1/203: 'Taglīd (garlanding) is only for what is hidden from its owner, like camels and cows specifically. As for sheep, they are not garlanded because they would be lost if not with its owner.' (2) It is what water is placed in when giving drink, and it is made of three skins. al-Mughrib 1/354 (r-w-y), al-Mu'jam al-Wasīt (r-w-y). Also the term rāwiyah is applied to the camel on which water is carried. (3) Jull (covering) of an animal is what covers it from leather and the like to protect it, and tajlīl is putting its covering on it. al-Qāmūs al-Muhīt (j-l-l), al-Mu'jam al-Wasīt (j-l-l). And taglīd is better than tajlīl because it is mentioned in the Noble Qur'an: 'and the hady and the garlands' (al-Ma'idah 5:97), and it is intended for notification that it is a ritual of the Haram. See al-Jawharah 1/203.
Source pages p. 452

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute passage from the commentary on al-Qudūrī. It deals with the case where a Mutamatti' drives a sacrificial animal (hady) with him, which is considered more virtuous. The text explains that if the animal is a camel (badanah), it is to be marked by garlanding (taqlīd) with a piece from a waterskin or a sandal around its neck. This garlanding is better than covering (tajlīl) because it is mentioned in the Qur'an. Then the dispute: ish'ar (marking by making a slight wound on the hump or side of the camel to mark it as a sacrificial animal) is allowed according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, but Abu Hanifa did not permit ish'ar for the hady, considering it akin to mutilation. The text states 'عند أبي يوسف ومحمد' implying their approval, so Abu Hanifa's opposition is understood. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school later shifted to allow ish'ar as a valid method of marking, following the Sahibayn. The footnotes clarify that garlanding applies only to camels and cows, not sheep, and that the waterskin is used for carrying water.

Key Terms
هدي (hady): A sacrificial animal driven to the Haram for the purpose of Hajj or 'Umrah.
بدنة (badanah): A camel used as a sacrificial animal, applicable to both male and female.
تقليد (taqlid): Garlanding the sacrificial animal around its neck with a piece of leather or a sandal to indicate it is a hady.
إشعار (ish'ar): Marking a camel by making a slight cut on its hump or side so that it leaves a scar, indicating it is a sacrificial animal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which Hanafi imams allowed ish'ar (marking by wound) for a sacrificial camel?
A) Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf
B) Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani
C) Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani
D) Only Abu Hanifa

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, ish'ar for the sacrificial camel is permissible according to the Sahibayn, and this is the mufta bihi position, though Abu Hanifa did not allow it.

The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Ish'ar (Marking the Sacrificial Camel)
Intra-Hanafi dispute on ish'ar with dalil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute over ish'ar, identify its dalil, and state the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Ish'ar is makruh for Abu Hanifa but permitted by the Sahibayn; the mufta bihi is permissibility.

This passage from al-Lubab details the sunnah actions for a mutamatti' who drives a sacrificial camel. While taqlid (garlanding) is uncontroversial, ish'ar (slitting the hump) is a point of ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school. Understanding this dispute and its resolution is essential for correct practice.

Guided Path
1
State the two positions
Identify the position of Abu Hanifa (makruh) and the Sahibayn (permissible) on ish'ar.
The text explicitly says: 'لا يشعر عند أبي حنيفة' and 'أشعر البدنة عند أبي يوسف ومحمد'.
2
Locate the textual basis
The passage cites the Prophet's action of stabbing the left side of the camel's hump. This hadith is the dalil for the practice.
The hadith is from Muslim, as referenced in al-Hidayah.
3
Analyze the reason for the ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa's dislike is based on the excessive harm caused by the people of his time. The Sahibayn consider the moderate practice sunnah.
The commentary notes: 'أبا حنيفة كره إشعار أهل زمانه؛ لمبالغتهم فيه'.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
Later Hanafi authorities (al-Qari, Ibn Abidin) rule that the mufta bihi is the view of the Sahibayn, making ish'ar permissible.
This is an example of tarjih within the school.
5
Apply the ruling
A mutamatti' today may perform ish'ar as a recommended act, but should avoid excessive harm following Abu Hanifa's concern.
The khilaf is in the action itself, not in its permissibility after tarjih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب التمتع
وإن أراد المتمتع أن يسوق الهدي معه، وهو أفضل: أحرم، وساق هديه. فإن كانت بدنة، وهي من الإبل خاصة، وتقع على الذكر والأنثى، والجمع: البدن. قلدها بمزادة – بالفتح – الراوية – والمراد: أن يعلق في عنقها قطعة من أدم من مزادة أو غيرها، أو نعل، وهو أولى من التجليل. وأشعر البدنة عند أبي يوسف ومحمد، وهو: أن يشق سنامها من الجانب الأيمن. ولا يشعر عند أبي حنيفة. وفي الهداية قالوا: والأشبه: الأيسر؛ لأن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم طعن في جانب اليسار مقصوداً، وفي جانب اليمين اتفاقاً. ولا يشعر عند أبي حنيفة، ويكره، قال في الهداية: وقيل: إن أبا حنيفة كره إشعار أهل زمانه؛ لمبالغتهم فيه على وجه يخاف منه.
Chapter of Tamattu'. If the mutamatti' wants to drive the sacrificial animal with him, and it is better: he enters ihram and drives his sacrificial animal. If it is a badanah—and it is specifically from camels, and applies to male and female, plural: budn—he garlands it with a mazadah (a leather water-skin), or a sandal, and that is better than covering it. And he marks (ash'ara) the badanah according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, which is: to slit its hump from the right side. And according to Abu Hanifa, he does not mark it. In al-Hidayah they said: the more likely is the left side, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) stabbed the left side intentionally, and the right side incidentally. And according to Abu Hanifa, he does not mark it, and it is disliked; he said in al-Hidayah: it is said that Abu Hanifa disliked the marking of the people of his time because of their excess in it in a way that is feared.
Source pages p. 453

Commentary
This passage from al-Lubab, a commentary on al-Quduri, addresses the rulings for a person performing tamattu' Hajj who wishes to bring a sacrificial animal (hady). The author establishes that doing so is superior (afdal). The ruling is that such a person enters ihram and drives the animal. The passage then focuses on the treatment of a specific type of hady: the badanah (a camel). For a badanah, two actions are mentioned: taqlid (garlanding) and ish'ar (marking). Taqlid involves hanging a piece of leather (from a water-skin or sandal) around the camel's neck; this is recommended (mustahabb) and preferable to covering the animal with a cloth. The core of the passage is the intra-Hanafi dispute over ish'ar, which is the practice of slitting the camel's hump on the right side to mark it as a sacrificial offering. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) permit ish'ar, while Abu Hanifa considers it makruh (disliked) and forbids it. The text from al-Hidayah clarifies that the more appropriate side for marking is the left, based on the Prophet's action, but this does not change the fact of the disagreement. The reason for Abu Hanifa's dislike, as quoted from al-Hidayah, is that the people of his time were excessive in ish'ar, causing unnecessary harm to the animal. The mufta bihi (relied-upon position) in the later school is the view of the Sahibayn, permitting ish'ar.

Key Terms
متمتع (mutamatti'): One who performs tamattu' Hajj, combining 'umrah and Hajj with a break in between, and is obligated to offer a sacrificial animal.
هدي (hady): A sacrificial animal (camel, cow, sheep, or goat) offered in the Haram during Hajj.
بدنة (badanah): A camel specifically, used as a sacrificial animal; can be male or female; plural: budn.
تقليد (taqlid): Garlanding the sacrificial animal by hanging something (e.g., leather strip or sandal) around its neck to mark it as a sacrifice.
إشعار (ish'ar): Marking a sacrificial camel by slitting its hump on one side to draw blood, indicating it is for sacrifice.
مزادة (mazadah): A leather water-skin, typically made from three hides, used for carrying water; here, a piece of it is hung around the camel's neck.
نعل (na'l): A sandal; used in taqlid as an alternative to leather.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the ruling on performing ish'ar on a sacrificial camel?
A) It is wajib (obligatory).
B) It is mustahabb (recommended).
C) It is makruh (disliked).
D) It is haram (forbidden).

Key Takeaway
Ish'ar is permissible (mufta bihi) but must be done moderately, avoiding excessive harm as cautioned by Abu Hanifa.

Cutting the Hump and Ish'ar of Hady: Two Sunan of Hajj
Ruling with proof on two hady practices

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the preferred method of cutting the hady's hump and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on ish'ar, identifying the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Cut the hump on the left side; ish'ar is sunnah according to Sahibayn, though Abu Hanifa disliked it for his time.

This lesson examines two specific practices related to the sacrificial animal (hady) during Hajj tamattu': cutting the hump (shaqq al-sanam) and marking the animal by drawing blood (ish'ar). The base text from al-Quduri provides a concise ruling, while al-Hidayah expands with evidence and clarifies the preferred side. Additionally, an intra-Hanafi difference emerges on the ruling of ish'ar, which we will analyse to understand its application in fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two practices
Read the passage and note the two distinct actions: cutting the hump (shaqq al-sanam) and marking (ish'ar). Understand that both are performed on the hady (sacrificial animal) in Hajj tamattu'.
2
Analyse the ruling on shaqq al-sanam
The base text states the hump is cut from the right side. Al-Hidayah corrects this, referencing the Prophet's action: he intentionally stabbed on the left side. Therefore, the left side is the sunnah. Recognize that this is a preferred method, not an obligation.
The hadith is cited as evidence; note the term 'maqsūdan' (intentionally) indicating deliberate worship.
3
Examine the ikhtilaf on ish'ar
Abu Hanifa holds ish'ar as makruh (disliked) due to excessive harm in his time, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider it sunnah. This is an intra-Hanafi dispute based on contextual factors.
Note that Abu Hanifa's disapproval was specific to his era's exaggerated practices.
4
Evaluate the evidence for each view
Review the dalil_block: the Prophet's action supports sunnah. Abu Hanifa's reason is based on preventing harm (mafsada). Understand that both are valid within the Hanafi framework, but the mufta bihi (fiqh position) follows the Sahibayn.
The tarjih authority (al-Hidayah, al-Qari) chooses the Sahibayn's view for fatwa.
5
Apply the mufta bihi ruling
Conclude that today, a Hanafi pilgrim should perform ish'ar as a sunnah and cut the hump on the left side. Recognize that following Abu Hanifa's view is also permissible but not the operative opinion.
The practical effect (thamarah al-khilaf) is that ish'ar is not mandatory but recommended, and the left side is the sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب التمتع
أن يَشقَّ سَنَامَها من الجانب الأيمن .
ولا يُشعِرُ عند أبي حنيفة .
( أن يَشقَّ سَنَامَها (۱) من الجانب الأيمن).
وفي «الهداية» قالوا: والأشبه (۲) : الأيسر؛ لأن النبي صلى الله عليه سلم طَعَنَ في جانب اليسار (۳) مقصوداً، وفي جانب اليمين اتفاقاً (٤).
( ولا يُشعر عند أبي حنيفة) ، ويكره (٥) ، قال في «الهداية»: وقيل: إن أبا حنيفة كره إشعار أهل زمانه ؛ لمبالغتهم فيه على وجه يُخاف منه
Chapter of Tamattu'. That he cuts its hump from the right side. And he does not perform ish'ar according to Abu Hanifa. (That he cuts its hump from the right side). And in al-Hidayah they said: The more appropriate is the left side, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) stabbed on the left side intentionally, and on the right side coincidentally. (And he does not perform ish'ar according to Abu Hanifa), and it is disliked. He said in al-Hidayah: It is said that Abu Hanifa disliked ish'ar of the people of his time due to their exaggeration in it in a manner feared from it.
Source pages p. 454

Commentary
This passage addresses two rulings related to the sacrificial animal (hady) in Hajj tamattu': the cutting of the hump (shaqq al-sanam) and the practice of ish'ar (marking by drawing blood). The base text (matn) states that the hump should be cut from the right side. The commentary from al-Hidayah notes that the more appropriate view is to cut from the left side, citing the Prophet's action: he intentionally stabbed on the left side, while the right side was coincidental. Thus, the recommended method is the left side. Regarding ish'ar, Abu Hanifa holds that it should not be done; rather, it is disliked (makruh). The reason mentioned in al-Hidayah is that Abu Hanifa observed people's exaggeration in ish'ar to the point of causing harm, so he disliked it. This ruling is specific to his era, but the general principle remains that ish'ar is a sunnah according to the majority, though Abu Hanifa's disapproval is noted.

Key Terms
الإشعار (al-ish'ar): Marking the sacrificial animal by drawing blood from its hump to indicate it is a hady.
شق السنام (shaqq al-sanam): Cutting or slitting the hump of the hady, usually done on the left side according to the preferable view.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Hidayah, from which side did the Prophet intentionally mark the hady?
A) The right side
B) The left side
C) The front
D) The back

Key Takeaway
The left side is preferred for cutting the hump, and ish'ar is sunnah according to the mufta bihi view, though Abu Hanifa's concern for harm contextualizes his disapproval.

Actions of the Mutamatti' Upon Entering Makkah
Rulings for mutamatti' after entering Makkah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sequence of actions for a mutamatti' upon entering Makkah and explain the obligation of dam al-tamattu'.

Core Idea
The mutamatti' must remain in ihram after umrah until shaving on the day of Nahr and owes a dam sacrifice.

In this lesson, we examine the rulings for a pilgrim performing Hajj tamattu' from the moment they enter Makkah. The passage from al-Quduri, expanded by al-Maydani's commentary, outlines the required tawaf and sa'i, the prohibition on becoming halal after umrah, the timing of ihram for Hajj, and the obligation of the dam sacrifice. Understanding this sequence is crucial for correctly performing tamattu'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Pilgrim's State
The pilgrim has entered Makkah in ihram for umrah. Note that tamattu' involves performing umrah first, then Hajj in the same year with a break.
The pilgrim remains in ihram throughout the interim period.
2
Determine the Required Acts Upon Entry
The passage states: 'he performs tawaf and sa'i' for his umrah. These are the essential rites of umrah.
Tawaf is circumambulation of the Ka'bah; sa'i is walking between Safa and Marwah.
3
Analyze the Prohibition on Tahlil
The mutamatti' does not become halal after umrah. He must remain in ihram until he slaughters his hady on the day of Nahr (10th of Dhul-Hijjah).
This differs from ifrad (Hajj only) or qiran (combined with one ihram).
4
Examine the Timing of Ihram for Hajj
He must assume ihram for Hajj on the day of Tarwiyah (8th of Dhul-Hijjah). Bringing it forward is permissible and considered better; delaying is also permissible.
The commentary emphasizes haste and increased hardship as reasons for preference.
5
Recognize the Obligation of Dam
The passage states 'upon him is dam al-tamattu''. This sacrifice is wajib (obligatory) as compensation for the ease of combining the two rites.
If unable, one may fast three days during Hajj and seven after returning (Quran 2:196).
6
Understand the Final Tahlil
On the day of Nahr, shaving the head renders the pilgrim halal from both ihrams (umrah and Hajj) simultaneously. The commentary compares shaving to the salam in prayer as a concluding act.
This is the complete release from the state of ihram.

Source Text

Source pages p. 455

Commentary
This passage outlines the sequence of actions for a person performing Hajj tamattu' after entering Makkah. Upon arrival, the mutamatti' first performs tawaf (circumambulation) and sa'i (walking between Safa and Marwah) for his umrah. Crucially, he does not perform tahlil (exit from ihram) after umrah; instead, he remains in a state of ihram. He must continue in ihram until he assumes ihram for Hajj on the day of Tarwiyah (8th of Dhul-Hijjah). If he brings forward the ihram for Hajj before the 8th, it is permissible and in fact considered better because it shows haste and additional exertion. Similarly, it is also permissible if he delays it after that day. The passage then states that the mutamatti' is obliged to offer a dam (blood sacrifice) for tamattu'. Finally, on the day of Nahr (10th of Dhul-Hijjah), when he shaves his head, he becomes halal from both the ihram of umrah and Hajj simultaneously. The commentary from al-Hidayah explains that shaving is to Hajj what the salam (greeting of peace) is to prayer: a concluding act that brings the ritual to completion. The reference to al-Tahawi and the 'correction' indicate that Tahawi's interpretation is considered more appropriate. There is also a textual note that some copies of al-Quduri simply say 'upon him is blood' without specifying 'tamattu'.

Key Terms
التمتع (al-tamattu'): A type of Hajj where the pilgrim performs umrah first, then after a break, performs Hajj in the same year, offering a sacrifice as compensation.
دم التمتع (dam al-tamattu'): The blood sacrifice (hady) required from a mutamatti' as compensation for the ease of combining umrah and Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Day of Arafah
B) Day of Tarwiyah (8th of Dhul-Hijjah)
C) Day of Nahr (10th of Dhul-Hijjah)
D) Any day before the 8th

Key Takeaway
Upon entering Makkah, the mutamatti' must perform tawaf and sa'i, remain in ihram, assume ihram for Hajj on Tarwiyah (or earlier), owe a dam, and become halal only after shaving on the day of Nahr.

Tamattu' and Qiran Invalid for the People of Makkah
Definition ruling with expansion on condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tamattu' and qiran for the people of Makkah, explain why tamattu' is invalid due to the condition of 'adam al-ilmaam, and distinguish this ruling from the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
A Makkan cannot perform tamattu' because the necessary condition of not returning home after 'umrah is impossible for him to fulfill.

In this lesson, we examine a specific fiqh ruling that restricts the people of Makkah from performing tamattu' or qiran, allowing only ifrad. The commentator in al-Lubab expands on why tamattu' is not merely prohibited but legally inconceivable for them. This rests on the Hanafi condition known as 'adam al-ilmaam (not returning to one's home) which a Makkan cannot meet. Understanding this will clarify the school's consistency in applying conditions to acts of worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the overall ruling for the people of Makkah regarding the three types of Hajj: tamattu', qiran, and ifrad. According to the Hanafi school, only ifrad is valid for them.
This is a definitive ruling in Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Understand the condition for tamattu'
The validity of tamattu' requires the absence of 'ilmaam – meaning the pilgrim does not return to his home after performing 'umrah and before starting Hajj. 'Ilmaam is the act of returning to one's family and residence.
This condition is specific to tamattu', not qiran.
3
Apply the condition to Makkans
A Makkan lives in Makkah itself. After performing 'umrah, he inevitably remains in or returns to his home, thus fulfilling 'ilmaam. Therefore, the condition is impossible for him to avoid, making tamattu' invalid.
The commentator emphasizes that tamattu' is not just prohibited but inconceivable (ghayr mutasawwar).
4
Distinguish qiran
Qiran does not require absence of 'ilmaam, so it could theoretically be performed by a Makkan. However, the school still rules it not legislated (laysa mashru'an) for them; only ifrad is.
The reason for qiran's invalidity is different and relates to the lack of travel for the people of the miqat.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school allows tamattu' for Makkans because they do not require 'adam al-ilmaam as a condition. This is a legitimate ikhtilaf rooted in different usul principles.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) affects how a Makkan performs Hajj.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Chapter of Tamattu'
And there is no tamattu' for the people of Makkah, nor qiran, but only ifrad specifically for them.
Tamattu' of the Makkan:]
* (And there is no tamattu' for the people of Makkah and those in their ruling who are within the miqat, nor is qiran legislated, but the legislated (for them is only ifrad), but their tamattu' is not conceivable; because they have stated that the absence of ilmaam is a condition for the validity of tamattu', not for qiran, and that valid ilmaam invalidates tamattu', not qiran.
Our teacher said in his gloss on al-Durr: The implication of this is that the tamattu' of a Makkan is invalid due to the presence of valid ilmaam between his two ihrams, whether he brings the hady or not; because an afaqi's ilmaam is only valid if he does not bring the hady and shaves, because then the return to Makkah is not required of him, but the Makkan cannot be imagined not returning to Makkah because he is in it, as stated in al-Inayah and others.
And in al-Nihayah and al-Mi'raj from al-Muhit: Valid ilmaam is that he returns to his family after 'umrah, and the return to 'umrah is not required. So we say: no tamattu' for the people of Makkah and the people of the miqat. End. That is, unlike qiran, because it is conceivable from them because the absence of ilmaam is not a condition for it.
(1) Like this from this in Hashiyat Ibn Abidin 7/203 (Damascus edition), but in some copies of al-Lubab: 'and about this'.
Source pages p. 456

Commentary
This passage from al-Lubab clarifies the ruling for the people of Makkah and those living within the miqat regarding the types of Hajj. It is a definitional ruling. The Hanafi position is that only ifrad (Hajj alone) is legislated for them; tamattu' and qiran are not valid. The commentator explains that tamattu' is actually inconceivable for them because tamattu' requires the absence of 'ilmaam'—meaning that the pilgrim should not return to his home between 'umrah and Hajj in a way that he remains in Makkah. For a Makkan, he is already in Makkah, so he cannot avoid returning to his home after 'umrah. Valid ilmaam (i.e., returning home after 'umrah and then coming back for Hajj) invalidates tamattu', but does not invalidate qiran. Therefore, a Makkan's tamattu' is invalid. As for qiran, it is also not legislated for them—only ifrad is. The commentary quotes various sources like al-Durr, al-Inayah, al-Nihayah, and al-Mi'raj to support this. A footnote indicates that Ibn Abidin's Hashiyah confirms the same, though some manuscripts of al-Lubab have a variant reading.

Key Terms
أهل مكة (ahl Makkah): The residents of Makkah and those living within the miqat boundaries (e.g., the people of the miqat).
الإفراد (al-ifrad): Performing Hajj alone without 'umrah in the same journey.
القران (al-qiran): Combining 'umrah and Hajj with one ihram, intending both simultaneously.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that tamattu' and qiran are invalid for the people of Makkah because the condition of not returning home (ilmaam) cannot be fulfilled, leaving ifrad as their only valid option.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
8 min
Why Tamattu' is Invalid for the People of Makkah
Ruling with rational proof on the invalidity of tamattu' and qiran for Makkans.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tamattu' and qiran for Makkans and explain why the condition of ilmaam (returning home) makes tamattu' impossible for them.

Core Idea
Tamattu' requires the pilgrim not to return home between Umrah and Hajj; a Makkan cannot fulfill this, so only ifrad is valid.

This passage from al-Lubab addresses a key distinction in Hajj rites: are tamattu' and qiran available to the residents of Makkah? The matn gives a firm negative, and the commentary reveals the underlying logic. The key lies in the condition of 'adam al-ilmaam' — not returning home after Umrah. A Makkan, by virtue of living in Makkah, inevitably returns, making tamattu' inconceivable. Let's trace how this ruling is derived.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling from the matn
The matn of al-Quduri states: 'There is no tamattu' nor qiran for the people of Makkah; only ifrad is for them.' This is a clear ruling invalidating both tamattu' and qiran for residents of Makkah and those within the miqat boundaries.
The text also covers those 'in their ruling' — anyone who resides within the miqat.
2
Understand the condition for valid tamattu'
The commentary explains that valid tamattu' requires 'adam al-ilmaam' — the pilgrim must not return to his homeland after performing Umrah and before starting Hajj. If he does return (valid ilmaam), the tamattu' is nullified. This is a condition, not a pillar.
Ilmaam is defined as returning to one's family after Umrah such that return to Umrah is no longer obligatory. For a non-Makkan (afaaqi), this can be avoided by not returning home.
3
Apply the condition to the Makkan
A Makkan resides in Makkah; he cannot avoid returning home after Umrah because his home is Makkah itself. Thus the condition of 'adam al-ilmaam' is impossible for him to fulfill. Consequently, his tamattu' is invalid (batil).
The commentator emphasizes that bringing a hadi does not affect this; the impossibility is inherent.
4
Distinguish qiran
Qiran does not require 'adam al-ilmaam' as a condition, so it is theoretically possible for a Makkan to combine Umrah and Hajj in one ihram. However, the matn still prohibits qiran for them; this is a separate ruling, not based on impossibility but on prescription.
Thus, qiran is not prescribed (mashru') for Makkans, even though it is conceivable.
5
Recognize the proof type
The proof here is rational (dalil aqli): it derives the invalidity from the impossibility of meeting a required condition. This is a form of qiyas or istidlal bi'l-istiqra' (inductive reasoning) based on the established condition from the Sunnah.
No specific Quranic verse or hadith is quoted; the reasoning is based on the logical consequence of the condition.

Source Text

Source pages p. 456

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and commentary on the permissibility of types of Hajj for the people of Makkah and those within the miqat. The ruling clearly states that for the people of Makkah, neither tamattu' (performing Umrah and Hajj with a break) nor qiran (performing both with a single ihram) is valid; only ifrad (performing Hajj alone) is permissible. The commentator explains that tamattu' is inconceivable for a Makkan because a condition for its validity is 'adam al-ilmaam' — that the pilgrim does not return to his homeland between the Umrah and Hajj. For an afaaqi (one coming from outside the miqat), if he returns home after Umrah without having brought a hadi (sacrificial animal) and shaved, his returning home is considered valid and invalidates his tamattu'. But for a Makkan, it is impossible for him not to return to Makkah since he resides there; thus his returning home always occurs, making tamattu' invalid. The commentator cites the gloss of his teacher on al-Durr and references al-Inayah, al-Nihayah, and al-Mi'raj to support this. The passage also distinguishes qiran, where the condition of not returning home is not required, so qiran is hypothetically possible for a Makkan, but the primary ruling is that it is not prescribed for them. The text concludes by affirming the matn's statement that there is no tamattu' or qiran for a Makkan, meaning negation of legality, not inconceivability.

Key Terms
تمتع (tamattu'): Performing Umrah first, then Hajj during the Hajj season with a break between them.
قران (qiran): Performing Umrah and Hajj together in a single ihram.
إفراد (ifrad): Performing Hajj alone without Umrah, then performing Umrah separately if desired.
إلمام (ilmaam): Returning to one's homeland after completing Umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because the Prophet prohibited Makkans from performing tamattu'.
D) Because he must bring a hadi, which is difficult for him.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, tamattu' is invalid for residents of Makkah and those within the miqat because the condition of not returning home (adam al-ilmaam) cannot be fulfilled.

Effect of Returning Home after 'Umrah on Tamattu' (Intra-Hanafi Dispute)
Intra-Hanafi dispute on tamattu' validity when returning home with hadi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the intra-Hanafi disagreement on whether returning home with a hadi invalidates tamattu' and apply the relied-upon ruling.

Core Idea
Returning home with a hadi does not invalidate tamattu' because the return is obligatory.

This passage addresses a nuanced point in tamattu' Hajj: what happens when a pilgrim returns to his hometown after completing Umrah? The ruling depends on whether he brought a hadi (sacrificial animal). Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani differs from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf on the effect of returning with a hadi. Understanding this dispute clarifies the school's reliance on obligation versus voluntary action.

Guided Path
1
State the agreed premise
Both sides agree that if a mutamatti' returns home after Umrah without a hadi, his tamattu' becomes invalid because he has validly returned to his family between the two rites.
2
Identify the point of divergence
When the pilgrim brings a hadi, does returning home still invalidate tamattu'? Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say no; Muhammad says yes.
The presence of hadi is the key variable.
3
Follow the opposing view (Muhammad)
Muhammad argues that even with a hadi, returning home constitutes two separate journeys and returning to one's family, which invalidates tamattu'.
His dalil: 'because he performed both rites in two travels' and 'because he returned to his family.'
4
Analyse the majority view (Abu Hanifa & Abu Yusuf)
They argue that the return is not voluntary but obligatory because shaving (tahalluq) must be done within the Haram. Since shaving is time-constrained to the Haram, the pilgrim is compelled to return to Makkah, so the return home is not a valid ilmaam that would break tamattu'.
The return is legally coerced (mustahiq), not optional.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
The practical difference: under the majority view, a mutamatti' with a hadi may return home after Umrah without invalidating his tamattu'. Under Muhammad's view, he would need to restart tamattu' or change to ifrad. The mufta bihi is the position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.
Ibn Abidin's Hashiyah confirms this reliance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And if he had brought the hadi, then his returning home is not valid, and his tamattu' does not become invalid according to them (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), and Muhammad said: his tamattu' becomes invalid because he performed both (rites) in two travels, and because he returned to his family. Commentary
This passage presents a ruling and an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of a mutamatti' (one performing tamattu' Hajj) returning to his hometown after completing the Umrah. The ruling states that if the mutamatti' returns home after completing Umrah, shaves (i.e., exits ihram), and had not brought a hadi (sacrificial animal), his tamattu' becomes invalid because his returning home is considered a valid ilmaam, which nullifies tamattu'. However, if he had brought a hadi, then according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (referred to as 'them'), his returning home is not considered valid, so his tamattu' remains valid. Imam Muhammad disagrees, arguing that even with a hadi, the tamattu' is invalid because it necessitates two separate journeys and involves returning to one's family. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf respond that the return is actually obligatory upon him because he must shave within the Haram (sacred precincts), which requires him to go to Makkah; thus, the return is not voluntary but required, and therefore does not invalidate the tamattu'. The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, as indicated by 'indahuma' and the context.

Key Terms
هدي (hadi): The sacrificial animal brought by a mutamatti' or qarin as a requirement for tamattu' or qiran.
إلمام صحيح (ilmaam sahih): Valid returning home: returning to one's homeland after Umrah without the obligation to return to Umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because the return is obligatory due to shaving being time-constrained to the Haram.
C) Because tamattu' is always valid regardless of return.
D) Because the hadi forgives the return.

Key Takeaway
When a mutamatti' brings a hadi, returning home after Umrah is obligatory due to shaving constraints, thus tamattu' remains valid per the majority Hanafi view.

Returning Home After 'Umrah: Does It Invalidate Tamattu'?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on tamattu' invalidation upon return with/without hadi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tamattu' invalidation upon returning home after 'umrah, distinguish the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf regarding the hadi, and apply the mufta bihi position to a given scenario.

Core Idea
Returning home after 'umrah invalidates tamattu' unless a hadi was brought; with hadi, the relied-upon view is tamattu' remains valid.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on a specific hajj scenario: a mutamatti' who returns to his hometown after completing 'umrah. The baseline ruling is clear: returning without a sacrificial animal (hadi) invalidates tamattu'. But if he brought a hadi, the companions differ: Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) say the return is not legally valid, so tamattu' stands; Muhammad ibn al-Hasan argues the opposite. Understanding the evidence behind each position will sharpen your ability to navigate Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
State the baseline ruling
Identify the act and the default ruling: a mutamatti' who returns home after 'umrah without a hadi has his tamattu' invalidated. Note why: his return to family is considered valid (ilmaam sahih), which breaks the continuity of tamattu'.
This is agreed upon by all Hanafi imams.
2
Identify the point of disagreement
The ikhtilaf arises when the mutamatti' has brought a hadi. Determine the two positions: Sahibayn say tamattu' is not invalidated; Muhammad says it is invalidated.
The hadi changes the legal nature of the return.
3
Examine the proof for each side
Sahibayn argue that returning is obligatory for shaving (hair removal), which is time-restricted to the sanctuary; therefore the return is not a valid return to family (ilmaam). Muhammad argues the pilgrim performed two separate journeys and validly returned to his family, which breaks tamattu'.
The key concept is whether the return is legally 'valid' (sahih).
4
Analyse the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: a mutamatti' with a hadi who returns home—according to Sahibayn his tamattu' is intact and he proceeds to hajj; according to Muhammad his tamattu' is void and he must do ifrad or another form.
This affects whether a hadi is still required and how he completes hajj.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The author of Lubab supports Sahibayn's view, citing the Jawharah. The relied-upon position for fatwa is that tamattu' is not invalidated when a hadi is brought.
Always check the tarjih authority in later Hanafi works.

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the invalidation of tamattu' when the mutamatti' returns to his hometown after completing 'umrah. The base ruling: without a hadi (sacrificial animal), returning invalidates tamattu' because it constitutes a valid return to one's family between the two rituals (umrah and hajj). When he has brought a hadi, the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that the return is not considered valid, so tamattu' remains intact; but Muhammad ibn al-Hasan holds that tamattu' is invalidated because the pilgrim performs the two rituals in two separate journeys and returns to his family. The text also clarifies a misconception from al-Sharnablaliyyah regarding the ruling for a Makkan and presents the author's correction that the return is valid regardless of having a hadi. Additionally, the passage distinguishes the qarin (one performing qiran): returning home does not invalidate qiran by consensus.

إلمام (ilmaam): Returning to one's family or home between the two rituals of hajj.
قارن (qarin): One who performs qiran, i.e., enters ihram for both 'umrah and hajj together.

Key Takeaway
Returning home after 'umrah invalidates tamattu' without a hadi; with a hadi, the relied-upon Hanafi view (Sahibayn) holds tamattu' remains valid.

Partial Tawaf Before Hajj Months Determines Tamattu' Status
Determines when partial tawaf before Hajj months makes one a mutamatti'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi condition for tamattu' based on the number of tawaf circuits performed before the Hajj months and explain the underlying legal maxim.

Core Idea
Majority of tawaf after Hajj months triggers tamattu'; otherwise, it's ifrad or qiran.

The timing of 'umrah acts relative to the Hajj months determines whether a pilgrim becomes a mutamatti'. The Hanafi school specifies a clear criterion: the number of tawaf circuits completed before the Hajj months. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its proof from al-Hidayah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its time frame
Determine when the 'umrah is begun and when the tawaf circuits are performed relative to the onset of the Hajj months (Shawwal, Dhul-Qi'dah, Dhul-Hijjah).
The key moment is the start of the Hajj months, not the completion of 'umrah.
2
Distinguish the two scenarios
If fewer than four circuits occur before the Hajj months, one scenario applies; if four or more, the opposite scenario.
Four circuits is more than half of seven, thus the majority.
3
Apply the legal maxim
The maxim 'al-akthar lahu hukm al-kull' (the majority takes the ruling of the whole) means that if most of the tawaf is performed after the Hajj months begin, the entire 'umrah is considered to occur within the Hajj months.
This is a Hanafi usul principle used here.
4
Derive the ruling
If the majority of tawaf is after the months, the pilgrim is a mutamatti'; otherwise, he is not.
The ruling is based on talil (legal reasoning) rather than explicit text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإحرام بالعمرة قبل أشهر الحج :]
ومن أحرم بالعمرة قبل أشهر الحج ، فطاف لهـا أي لعمرتـه أقل من أربعة أشواط ، ثم لم يُتِمَّها حـتـى دخـلـت أشهر الحج ، فتممها في أشهره ، وأحرم بالحج كان متمتعاً ؛ لأن الإحرام عندنا شرط، فيصح تقديمه على أشهر الحج، وإنما يُعتبر أداء الأفعال فيها، وقد وجد الأكثر ، وللأكثر حكم الكل. هداية.
وإن كان طاف لعمرته قبل أشهر الحج أربعة أشواط فصاعداً، ثم حج من عامه ذلك : لم يكن متمتعاً ؛ لأنه أدى الأكثر
Ihram for 'umrah before the months of Hajj: And whoever enters ihram for 'umrah before the months of Hajj, and performs tawaf for it, i.e., for his 'umrah, less than four circuits, then does not complete it until the months of Hajj enter, then completes it in its months, and enters ihram for Hajj: he is a mutamatti'; because according to us ihram is a condition, so it is valid to advance it before the months of Hajj, and only the performance of the actions within them is considered, and the majority has been found, and the majority has the ruling of the whole. Hidayah. And if he had performed tawaf for his 'umrah before the months of Hajj four circuits or more, then performs hajj in that same year: he is not a mutamatti'; because he performed the majority.
Source pages p. 458

Commentary
This passage from al-Hidayah explains the ruling on performing 'umrah before the Hajj months. The key distinction is the number of tawaf circuits performed before the onset of the Hajj months. If a person enters ihram for 'umrah before Shawwal, Dhul-Qi'dah, and Dhul-Hijjah (the hajj months), and performs fewer than four tawaf circuits before the months begin, then completes the 'umrah and enters ihram for hajj within the hajj months, he is considered a mutamatti' (one performing tamattu'). The reasoning: ihram can be validly commenced before its time as a condition, but the actual performance of the rituals must be within the proper time. Since the majority of the 'umrah (most of the actions) occurs after the hajj months begin, it is as if the entire 'umrah was performed then. Conversely, if he performed four or more circuits before the hajj months, the majority of the 'umrah was already performed outside the hajj months, so he is not a mutamatti'; rather, his hajj is considered ifrad or qiran depending on intention. Note: four circuits constitute the majority of the seven circuits (more than half), hence the ruling.

Key Terms
أكثر (akthar): Majority; here it refers to performing more than half of the tawaf circuits (four or more out of seven) before the Hajj months.
أشهر الحج (ashhur al-hajj): The months of Hajj: Shawwal, Dhul-Qi'dah, and the first ten days of Dhul-Hijjah according to the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He is a mutamatti'.
B) He is a mufrid.
C) He is a qarin.
D) His 'umrah is invalid.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school uses the maxim 'al-akthar lahu hukm al-kull' to rule that performing fewer than four tawaf circuits before the Hajj months results in tamattu' status; performing four or more prevents it.

Conditions for Becoming a Mutamatti' and the Ruling on Returning Home
Ruling on tamattu' based on tawaf timing and returning home

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that the majority has the ruling of the whole to determine when a person is a mutamatti', and distinguish the effect of returning home for a mutamatti' versus a qarin.

Core Idea
A mutamatti' requires that the majority of Umrah acts fall within the Hajj months; a qarin's ihram is unaffected by returning home.

This passage from al-Lubab clarifies a key condition for tamattu': when exactly must the Umrah acts occur to be considered part of the same Hajj journey? The answer hinges on a powerful usul principle—the majority has the ruling of the whole. Additionally, an intra-Hanafi dispute about returning home after starting tamattu' distinguishes the mutamatti' from the qarin.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules on whether a person who begins Umrah before the months of Hajj becomes a mutamatti' if he performs Hajj in the same year. The ruling depends on how many tawaf circuits were completed before the months began.
2
Understand the threshold: four circuits
If the person performed fewer than four circuits before the months of Hajj, he is a mutamatti'. If he performed four or more circuits, he is not a mutamatti'. The number four is not arbitrary; it represents the majority of the seven circuits.
The principle: al-akthar lahu hukm al-kull (the majority has the ruling of the whole).
3
Apply the principle to the scenario
When less than four circuits are done before the months, the majority of the Umrah occurs within the months, so the entire Umrah is considered to have taken place during the months, fulfilling the condition for tamattu'. When four or more occur before, the majority is outside the months, so the Umrah is treated as complete before the months, and tamattu' does not occur.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on returning home
Abu Hanifa holds that returning to one's home country after starting tamattu' invalidates the state of ihram (wujub), while Abu Yusuf considers it only recommended (istihbab) and not invalidating. The qarin is not affected by returning home according to all three imams.
This dispute applies specifically to the mutamatti', not the qarin.
5
Derive the practical difference
For a mutamatti', returning home may require repeating the Umrah according to Abu Hanifa, but according to Abu Yusuf, it is makruh but the tamattu' remains valid. For a qarin, returning home does not affect the validity of either Umrah or Hajj.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(ومن أحرم بالعمرة قبل أشهر الحج فطاف لها أقل من أربعة أشواط، ثم لم يُتِمَّها حتى دخلت أشهر الحج، فتممها في أشهره، وأحرم بالحج كان متمتعاً) ؛ لأن الإحرام عندنا شرط، فيصح تقديمه على أشهر الحج، وإنما يُعتبر أداء الأفعال فيها، وقد وجد الأكثر ، وللأكثر حكم الكل. «هداية». (وإن كان طاف لعمرته قبل أشهر الحج أربعة أشواط فصاعداً، ثم حج من عامه ذلك : لم يكن متمتعاً) ؛ لأنه أدى الأكثر قبل أشهر الحج ، فصار كما إذا تحلل منها قبل أشهر الحج. والأصل في المناسك : أن الأكثر له حكم الكل، فإذا حَصَل الأكثر قبل أشهر الحج، فكأنها حصلت كلها، وقد ذكرنا أن المتمتع الذي يتم العمرة والحج في أشهر الحج. «جوهرة». ثم وجوباً عند أبي حنيفة، واستحباباً عند أبي يوسف، والعود يمنع صحة الإلمام. «جوهرة». ثم قال: وقيَّد بالمتمتع، إذ القارن لا يبطل قرانه بالعود إلى بلده في قولهم جميعاً.
And whoever performs ihram for Umrah before the months of Hajj, and performs less than four circuits of tawaf for it, then the months of Hajj enter, so he completes it (the Umrah) and performs ihram for Hajj: he is a mutamatti'. And if he performed four or more circuits of tawaf for his Umrah before the months of Hajj, then performs Hajj in that same year: he is not a mutamatti'. Then, it is obligatory according to Abu Hanifa, and recommended according to Abu Yusuf, and returning (to one's country) prevents the validity of the ihlam. Then he said: And it is restricted to the mutamatti', for the qarin does not invalidate his qiran by returning to his country, according to all of them.
Source pages p. 458

Commentary
This passage from al-Lubab sets out the conditions for being a mutamatti' (one who performs Umrah and then Hajj within the same journey, with a break of ihram between them). The ruling is that if one begins Umrah before the months of Hajj (Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, and the first ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah) and performs fewer than four tawaf circuits, then when the months enter he completes the Umrah and does Hajj, he is a mutamatti'. The reason is that ihram is only a condition (shart) that can be performed before the months; what matters is that the actual acts fall within the months. Since the majority of the Umrah (the remaining circuits) are done in the months, the majority has the ruling of the whole, so the entire Umrah is considered to have occurred within the months. But if he performed four or more circuits before the months, then the majority of the Umrah acts have been done before the months, so it is as if he completed the Umrah entirely before the months, and thus he is not a mutamatti'. The text also notes an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Abu Hanifa holds that returning to one's home country after starting tamattu' prevents the validity of the tahalul (i.e., it invalidates the state of ihram) as an obligation (wujub), while Abu Yusuf considers it recommended (istihbab). The last part clarifies that this ruling about returning applies only to the mutamatti', not to the qarin (one who combines Umrah and Hajj in one ihram); the qarin's qiran is not invalidated by returning home, according to the unanimous view of the three (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad).

Key Terms
متمتع (mutamatti'): One who performs Umrah first, then after tahalul performs Hajj in the same year within the months of Hajj.
قارن (qarin): One who combines Umrah and Hajj in a single ihram, entering both simultaneously.
إحرام (ihram): The state of ritual consecration for Hajj or Umrah, beginning with the intention and talbiyah.
أشهر الحج (ashhur al-hajj): The months of Hajj: Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, and the first ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person performs ihram for Umrah on 1st Shawwal, performs 3 circuits of tawaf, then on 2nd Shawwal completes the remaining circuits and does Hajj. Is he a mutamatti'?
A) Yes, because he performed less than 4 circuits before Shawwal.
B) No, because he performed some circuits before the months.
C) Yes, because he completed all acts within the months.
D) No, because he became a qarin.

Key Takeaway
The key to tamattu' is that the majority of Umrah acts must occur within the Hajj months; returning home invalidates tamattu' only according to Abu Hanifa, not for the qarin.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
beginner
6 min
Months of Hajj and Early Ihram
Definition of Hajj months and ruling on early ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the months of Hajj according to the Hanafi school and explain the ruling on ihram performed before them, including the reasons for validity and dislike.

Core Idea
Ihram before the Hajj months is valid but disliked — a condition (shart) can precede the act but resembles a pillar out of time.

This lesson defines the specific months in which Hajj acts must occur, then examines an important edge case: what if someone enters ihram before those months? Understanding the distinction between a condition (shart) and a pillar (rukn) is key to grasping the Hanafi ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the defined subject
Determine what is being defined: the 'months of Hajj' (ashhur al-hajj) according to the Hanafi school.
Focus on the three months: Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, and the first ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah.
2
Understand the definition
Why are only the first ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah included? Because the main Hajj rites (e.g., standing at Arafah) occur within these days, and the rest of Dhu al-Hijjah is for catching up on missed rites or for 'Umrah.
The Hanafi school limits the months to ten days; other schools include the entire month.
3
Analyze the ruling on early ihram
The passage states that if one performs ihram before the months, it is valid (jāza) but disliked (kurihat). Identify the hukm level: sahih and makruh tanzihan.
Makruh tanzihan means it is disliked but not sinful.
4
Explore the legal reasoning
Why valid? Because ihram is a shart (condition) for Hajj, and conditions can precede the conditioned act. Why disliked? Because it resembles performing a rukn (pillar) before its time, which would be invalid; thus, to avoid resemblance, it is disliked.
The distinction between shart and rukn is crucial: a condition can be done early, a pillar must be in its proper time.
5
Note the practical consequence
Even though the ihram is valid, no acts of Hajj (e.g., talbiyah, tawaf, sa'i) are to be performed until the months begin. The pilgrim must wait.
This prevents any misunderstanding that one can start Hajj rituals early.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأشهر الحج : شوال، وذو القعدة) - بفتح القاف، وتكسر - (وعَشر من ذي الحجة) - بكسر الحاء ، وتُفتَح - (فإن قدم الإحرام بالحج عليها أي الأشهر المذكورة: (جاز إحرامه)؛ لأنه شَرْطٌ ، وكُره ؛ لشبهه بالركن، وانعقد حجاً)، إلا أنه لا يجوز له شيء من أفعاله إلا في الأشهر.
And the months of Hajj are: Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, and ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah. And if he performs ihram for Hajj before them, that is, before the mentioned months: his ihram is valid because it is a condition, and it is disliked due to its resemblance to a pillar (rukn), and it takes effect as Hajj. However, he may not perform any of its acts except in the months.
Source pages p. 459

Commentary
This passage defines the months of Hajj as Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, and the first ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah. This definition is crucial because certain acts of Hajj, like standing at Arafat and tawaf al-ifadah, must occur within these months. The text then discusses performing ihram for Hajj before these months. The ruling is that the ihram is valid and counts as Hajj because ihram is only a condition (shart) that can precede the actual acts. However, it is makruh (disliked) to do so because it resembles making ihram for Hajj outside its time, similar to performing a pillar before its time. Despite the validity, no acts of Hajj (like wearing ihram garments, talbiyah, or entering the state of ihram) are to be performed until the months begin; the pilgrim must wait. This ruling reflects the Hanafi view that ihram is a condition, not a pillar.

Key Terms
أشهر الحج (ashhur al-hajj): The three months: Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, and the first ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah.
إحرام (ihram): The state of consecration for Hajj, entered by intention and talbiyah.
شرط (shart): A condition that must be present for an act to be valid but can be fulfilled before the act.
ركن (rukn): A pillar or integral part of an act that must be performed within its proper time; omission invalidates the act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a person performs ihram for Hajj on the 1st of Ramadhan?
A) Valid and recommended; acts may begin immediately.
B) Valid but disliked; no Hajj acts until Shawwal.
C) Invalid; must repeat ihram in Dhu al-Hijjah.
D) Invalid; the intention is for 'Umrah automatically.

Key Takeaway
Ihram before the months of Hajj is valid but makruh; the pilgrim must wait until the months to perform the rites.
